تشریح قوله ومن غصب ..... الخ - حکم غصب اجمالاً ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس کی تفصیل ہے۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگرشی مغصوب ہلاک ہوگئی ہو اور وہ مثلی ہو یعنی کیلی یا وزنی (جیسے گیہوں ، جو ، درہم و دینار وغیرہ) تو مثل مغصوب واپس کرنا ضروری ہے لقولہ تعالى فمَنِ اعْتَدی ۔ اور اگر اس کا مثل منقطع ہو گیا ہو یعنی وہ بازار میں نہ پایا جاتا ہو تو اس کی قیمت واجب ہے جس میں امام صاحب کے نزدیک خصومت کے دن کا اعتبار ہے۔ یعنی جس دن حاکم کا حکم ہوا ہو اس دن کل قیمت دینا واجب ہے۔ امام مالک فقیہ ابواللیث اور امام شافعی کے اکثر اصحاب اسی کے قائل ہیں امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک غصب کے دن کی قیمت واجہ ، ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس دن کی قیمت واجب ہے جس دن اس کا مثل منقطع ہوا ہے۔ امام زفر ، امام احمد اور بعض اصحاب امام شافعی اسی کے قائل ہیں ۔

قوله لابي يوسف ...... الخ - امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب اس کا مثل منقطع ہو گیا تو وہ بھی غیر متلی اشیاء کے ساتھ لاحق ہو گئی ۔ لہذا انعقاد سب کے دن کی قیمت کا اعتبار ہوگا۔

امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ غاصب کے ذمہ اس کا مثل واجب ہے اور انقطاع کی وجہ سے وہ مثل قیمت کی طرف منتقل ہو جاتا ہے۔ تو انقطاع کے دن کی قیمت معتبر ہوگی ۔ امام صاحب یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مثل واجب کا قیمت کی طرف منتقل ہو جانا صرف انقطاع مثل کی وجہ سے نہیں ہوتا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر مالک مثل مغصوب ملنے تک صبر کرے یہاں تک کہ اس کا مثل لے تو اس کو اسکا اختیار ہوتا ہے بلک قیمت کی جانب منتقل ہونا قاضی قضاء سے ہوتا ہے۔ پس خصومت کے دن کی قیمت کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ بخلاف ایسی چیز کے جس کا مشکل نہیں ہوتا کہ اس میں اصل سبب یعنی غصب پائے جاتے ہی قیمت کا مطالبہ ثابت ہو جاتا ہے تو اس میں وہی قیمت معتبر ہوگی جو غصب کرنے کے روز تھی خزانہ میں امام صاحب کے قول کو اصح کہا ہے اور شرح وقایہ میں امام ابو یوسف کے قول کو اعدل اور نہایہ میں اس کو مختار کہا ہے اور ذخیرة الفتاوی میں امام محمد کے قول کو مفتی یہ کہا ہے۔

فائدہ یہاں صاحب ہدایہ نے اپنی عادت کے خلاف تعلیل میں امام ابو یوسف کے قول کو مقدم کیا ہے جب کہ ان کے قول کی تعلیل کا حق یہ تھا کہ قول طرفین کے درمیان میں ذکر کرتے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے اس کی دو وجہیں ذکر کی ہیں ۔ اول یہ کہ ممکن ہے کہ موصوف کے نزدیک قوت دلیل کے لحاظ سے قول ابو یوسف مختار ہو بایں معنی کہ اس میں ثبوت موجب کے اعتبار سے حکم کا اثبات ہے اس لئے کہ شی مغصوب غصب ہی کے وقت سے غاصب کے نعمان میں داخل ہو چکی تو قیمت کا اعتبار بھی وقت غصب ہی سے ہونا چاہیے۔

دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ اقوال ثلثہ کا اثبات ترتیب زمانی کے موافق منظور ہے کہ اوقات ثلثہ میں سے اول وقت یوم غصب ہے پھر یوم انقطاع پھر یوم خصومت ، اور اقوال مذکورہ کو ان از منہ کی ترتیب کے لانا اسی طور پر ہوسکتا ہے کہ پہلے قول ابو یوسف ہو پھر قول محمد پھر قول ابو حنیفہ ۔

مگر ان دونوں وجہوں پر صاحب نتائج نے یہ مناقشہ کیا ہے کہ دلیل مذکور کا مضمون اس کی قوت پر دلالت نہیں کرتا۔ اس لئے کہ مثلی مغصوب جو بوقت غصب غاصب کے ضمان میں داخل ہوا ہے۔ وہ ضمان مثل کے ساتھ ہوا ہے پھر انقطاع کی وجہ سے ضمان قیمت کی طرف منتقل ہو گیا۔ جیسا کہ خود صاحب ہدایہ نے دلیل امام محمد کے ذکر میں اس کی تصریح کی ہے۔ پس قیمت کا وقت غصب سے معتبر ہونا کہاں سے لازم آیا۔ یہاں تک کہ یہ قوت دلیل کو ستلزم ہو۔ اور اگر دلیل کی قوت ہی تسلیم کر لی جائے تو صاحب ہدایہ کی عادت کے مطابق دلیل ابو یوسف مؤخر ہونی چاہیے۔ اذمن عادة المستمرة ان يؤخر القوى عند ذكر الادلة رہی وجہ ثانی سو اقوال کو تر تیب زمانی کے مطابق لانے سے کوئی فقہی غرض وابستہ نہیں ہے۔ پس اس امر وحی کی وجہ سے اپنے مقررہ اسلوب کو بدلنا صاحب ہدایہ کے شایان شان نہیں ہے۔
He said: Whoever usurps something that has a mithl (like measured and weighed goods) and it perishes in his possession, then upon him is its mithl. In some copies: upon him is the guarantee of its mithl, and there is no difference between them. This is because the obligatory is the mithl due to His statement: 'So whoever transgresses against you, then transgress against him with the like of what he transgressed against you' (2:194) and because the mithl is more just because it considers both genus and monetary value, thus it repels harm. He said: If he cannot pay its mithl, then upon him is its value on the day they litigate. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: the day of usurpation. Muhammad said: the day of interruption (when the mithl becomes unavailable). The proof for Abu Yusuf: when it was interrupted, it becomes like something without a mithl, so its value is considered on the day the cause arose, because that is the obligating factor. For Muhammad: the obligatory is the mithl in the liability, and it transfers to value only due to interruption, so the value is considered on the day of interruption. For Abu Hanifa: the transfer is not established merely by interruption; that is why if he waits until its genus is found, he may take it. Rather, transfer occurs by the judge's ruling, so the value is considered on the day of litigation and judgment, unlike something without a mithl because its value is claimed from the beginning due to the original cause, so the value at that time is considered. 

Translation: Whoever usurps a mithli item, i.e., measured or weighed goods, and it perishes in his possession, then upon him is its mithl. In some copies: upon him is the guarantee of its mithl, and there is no difference between them. This is because the obligatory is the mithl, due to the divine statement: 'So whoever transgresses against you, then transgress against him with the like of what he transgressed against you' and because the mithl is more just, as it observes genus and monetary value, thus harm is properly repelled. Then if he cannot pay its mithl, then upon him is its value on the day of litigation. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Imam Abu Yusuf says: the day of usurpation. Imam Muhammad says: the day of interruption. The proof for Abu Yusuf: when it became interrupted, it is attached to non-mithli items, so the value on the day the cause (usurpation) arose is considered, as that is the obligator. For Muhammad: the mithl is obligatory in the liability, and transfer to value occurs due to interruption, so the value on the day of interruption is considered. For Abu Hanifa: the transfer is not established by mere interruption; that is why if the owner waits until the mithl is found, he has the option to take it; rather, the transfer to value occurs by the judge's ruling, so the value on the day of litigation and judgment is considered, unlike non-mithli items because in them the claim for value is established from the original cause, so the value at that time is considered.

Explanation: The statement 'Whoever usurps...' is a detail after the general ruling. He says: If the usurped item is destroyed and it is mithli, i.e., measured or weighed (like wheat, barley, dirham, dinar, etc.), then returning the mithl of the usurped item is obligatory due to the verse 'So whoever transgresses...'. And if its mithl becomes interrupted, i.e., unavailable in the market, then its value is obligatory. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the day of litigation is considered, i.e., the day the judge gives the ruling. Imam Malik, Faqih Abu al-Layth, and most of Shafi'i's companions hold this view. According to Abu Yusuf, the value on the day of usurpation is obligatory. According to Muhammad, the value on the day the mithl became interrupted is obligatory. Imam Zufar, Imam Ahmad, and some of Shafi'i's companions hold this view.

His statement: 'The proof for Abu Yusuf...' - Abu Yusuf's proof: when its mithl became interrupted, it joins non-mithli items, so the value on the day the cause (usurpation) occurred is considered.

Muhammad's proof: the mithl is obligatory on the usurper's liability, and due to interruption, the mithl transfers to value, so the value on the day of interruption is considered. Imam (Abu Hanifa) says: the transfer of the obligatory mithl to value does not occur merely due to interruption; that is why if the owner waits until the mithl is found and takes its mithl, he has that option. Rather, transfer to value occurs by the judge's ruling. So the value on the day of litigation is considered. Unlike something that has no mithl, because in that case the claim for value is established from the original cause (usurpation), so the value at that time is considered. In Khizanah, Imam's statement is said to be the most correct; in Sharh al-Wiqayah, Abu Yusuf's statement is said to be more just; in al-Nihayah, it is said to be the chosen view; and in Dhakhirat al-Fatawa, Muhammad's statement is said to be the mufta bihi.

Benefit: Here Sahib al-Hidayah, contrary to his habit, presented the proof of Abu Yusuf first in the reasoning, whereas the right of his proof was to mention it between the statements of the two sides. Sahib al-Inayah gave two reasons: first, it is possible that in his view, in terms of the strength of proof, the statement of Abu Yusuf is preferred, in the sense that it establishes the ruling with regard to the establishment of the obligating cause, because the usurped item entered the liability of the usurper from the time of usurpation itself, so the value should also be considered from the time of usurpation. Second, the presentation of the three statements is intended in accordance with chronological order: the first time is the day of usurpation, then the day of interruption, then the day of litigation; and bringing the mentioned statements in this order can only be by having Abu Yusuf's statement first, then Muhammad's, then Abu Hanifa's. However, Sahib al-Nata'ij criticized both reasons: the content of the mentioned proof does not indicate its strength, because the usurped mithli that enters the liability of the usurper at the time of usurpation enters with the guarantee of the mithl, then due to interruption, the guarantee transfers to value, as Sahib al-Hidayah himself clarified in mentioning Muhammad's proof. So how does it necessitate that the value be considered from the time of usurpation to imply strength of proof? And if the strength of proof is admitted, then according to Sahib al-Hidayah's habit, the proof of Abu Yusuf should be delayed, as his continuous habit is to delay the strong when mentioning proofs. As for the second reason, bringing the statements in chronological order has no fiqhi purpose. Therefore, changing his established style for this reason is not befitting of Sahib al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah deals with the ruling on usurped goods that have a standard measure (mithli), such as weighed or measured items. The author begins by stating the primary ruling: if a person usurps a mithli item and it is destroyed in his possession, he must return an identical item (mithl). The proof is the Quranic verse 'So whoever transgresses against you, then transgress against him with the like of what he transgressed against you' (2:194), which establishes reciprocity. Additionally, the mithl is more just because it considers both the genus and the monetary value, thus fully compensating the owner. 

Then the passage addresses a secondary situation: if the mithl is unavailable (e.g., the goods are no longer found in the market), the usurper must pay the value (qimah). However, there is a three-way disagreement among the Hanafi imams regarding which date's value should be used: 
- Abu Hanifa: the day of litigation (yawm al-khusumah), when the judge rules. 
- Abu Yusuf: the day of usurpation (yawm al-ghasb), when the item was taken. 
- Muhammad al-Shaybani: the day the mithl becomes interrupted (yawm al-inqita'), i.e., when it disappears from the market. 

Each imam provides a proof: Abu Yusuf argues that once the mithl is unavailable, the item becomes like non-mithli items, and the liability crystallizes at the moment of usurpation, so that date's value applies. Muhammad argues that the obligation is originally the mithl, and only due to interruption does it shift to value, so the value at the time of interruption is relevant. Abu Hanifa argues that the shift to value does not occur automatically by interruption; the owner may wait for the mithl, and only the judge's ruling effectuates the transfer to value, so the date of litigation/judgment governs. 

The commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah (Urdu) further explains each position and notes that later scholars have different preferences: some prefer Abu Hanifa's view (Khizanah), some Abu Yusuf's (Sharh al-Wiqayah), some Muhammad's (Dhakhirat al-Fatawa). It also discusses a methodological point: why the Hidayah author presented Abu Yusuf's proof first, contrary to his usual habit. The commentator provides two reasons from al-Inayah (chronological order and perceived strength) and then a critique from al-Nata'ij (not strength, and chronological order is irrelevant). 

This lesson illustrates the Hanafi school's internal diversity and the application of qiyas and istihsan in deriving rulings.

Key Terms
مثلی (mithli): An item that has a standard measure or weight and can be replaced by an identical example (e.g., wheat, dirhams).
غصب (ghasb): Unlawful seizure and possession of another's property without entitlement.
مثل (mithl): An identical item of the same species and quality as the usurped one.
قیمت (qimah): Monetary value or price paid as compensation when the mithl is not available.
یوم الخصومة (yawm al-khusumah): The day when the parties litigate and the judge passes a ruling.
انقطاع (inqita'): The state when the mithl becomes unavailable in the market or ceases to exist.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which day does Imam Abu Hanifa consider for calculating the value of a usurped mithli item when its mithl is unavailable?
A) Day of usurpation
B) Day of interruption
C) Day of litigation
D) Day of payment

Key Takeaway
For usurped mithli goods, the primary obligation is to return an identical item; if unavailable, the valuation date is disputed among Abu Hanifa (litigation day), Abu Yusuf (usurpation day), and Muhammad (interruption day), with no single operative view in the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.

Valuation Date for Usurped Mithli Items
Intra-Hanafi dispute on valuation date for usurped mithli items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the valuation date for usurped mithli items and evaluate the evidence for each.

Core Idea
The value of usurped fungibles is assessed on different dates depending on when the obligation to pay value arises.

This passage from Ashraf ul Hadaya presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: does the obligation to pay the value (qimat) arise at the moment of usurpation, when the mithl becomes unavailable, or only by a judge's decree? The three great Imams of the Hanafi school—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—disagree, and later authorities have favored different views. Understanding this dispute teaches you how Hanafi jurists reason about the transfer of an obligation from a specific item to its monetary substitute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State each Imam's ruling on the valuation date: Abu Yusuf (day of judgment), Muhammad (day of interruption), Abu Hanifa (day of litigation).
2
Understand the reasoning
For each position, identify what triggers the obligation to pay value: Abu Yusuf sees interruption as making it like non-mithli; Muhammad sees the obligation transferring at interruption; Abu Hanifa requires a judge's decree.
The reasoning is based on the nature of the obligation (dhaman) and when it shifts from mithl to value.
3
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: compensation amount varies with price fluctuations between usurpation, interruption, and litigation dates.
This shows how legal theory directly affects real-world outcomes.
4
Examine the later tarjih
Later authorities favored different views: Khizanah prefers Abu Hanifa, Sharh Wiqayah and Nihayah prefer Abu Yusuf, Dhakhirat al-Fatawa prefers Muhammad.
There is no single mufta bihi; the dispute remains active.
5
Critically analyze the ordering in Hidayah
The author of Hidayah presented Abu Yusuf's view first, contrary to his habit. Two justifications are given and critiqued. Consider whether the ordering reflects strength of proof or temporal sequence.
This is a lesson in scholarly critique and the art of commentary.

مقررہ اسلوب کو بدلنا صاحب ہدایہ کے شایان شان نہیں ہے۔
Book of Usurpation. These are the opinion holders. Saying: For Abu Yusuf... etc. - Imam Abu Yusuf's proof: When its mithl is interrupted, it becomes attached to non-mithli items, so the value on the day of the contract (of judgment) is considered. Imam Muhammad's proof: The usurper owes the mithl, and due to interruption, the mithl transfers to value, so the value on the day of interruption is considered. Imam Abu Hanifa says: The transfer of the obligation of mithl to value does not occur solely due to interruption; if the owner waits to receive the mithl, he has the option; rather, transfer occurs by the judge's decree, so the value on the day of litigation is considered. Unlike items whose value is established from the time of usurpation. In Khizanah, Imam Abu Hanifa's view is called more correct; in Sharh Wiqayah, Abu Yusuf's view is called more just; in Nihayah, it is chosen; in Dhakhirat al-Fatawa, Muhammad's view is given for fatwa. Benefit: Here the author of Hidayah, contrary to his habit, placed Abu Yusuf's view first. The author of Inayah gives two reasons: (1) Perhaps in his view Abu Yusuf's proof is stronger because it establishes the ruling based on the cause from the time of usurpation; (2) The three views correspond to the temporal order: usurpation, interruption, litigation. But the author of Nata'ij critiques: The content of the proof does not indicate strength, and the temporal order has no fiqhi purpose; changing the style is unbefitting.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the valuation date for usurped mithli (fungible) items when the mithl becomes unavailable. The three positions are: Abu Yusuf says value on the day of judgment (when the court awards compensation), Muhammad says value on the day the mithl becomes unavailable, and Abu Hanifa says value on the day of litigation (when the case is brought). The commentary explains each reasoning, then cites later authorities who favor different views. The author then notes that the Hidayah's author unusually presented Abu Yusuf's view first, and critiques two justifications for this ordering. The key point is that the dispute hinges on whether the obligation to pay value arises at the moment of usurpation, interruption, or litigation.

Key Terms
مثل (mithl): An item that has an exact equivalent in the market, such as commodities sold by weight or measure.
قیمت (qimat): Market value or monetary compensation for a lost or damaged item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, on which date is the value of a usurped mithli item assessed when its mithl is interrupted?
A) Day of usurpation
B) Day of interruption of mithl
C) Day of litigation (court hearing)
D) Day of judgment (court decree)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has three distinct opinions on the valuation date for usurped fungibles, each based on a different legal reasoning about when the obligation to pay value crystallizes.

Classification of Property and Valuation of Non-Mithli Items
Ruling on valuation of non-mithli usurped items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify items as mithli or qimi (non-mithli) based on Hanafi criteria and state the valuation rule for non-mithli items.

Core Idea
Non-mithli items are compensated by their value on the day of usurpation, not by replacement.

This lesson explains how Hanafi fiqh classifies property into mithli (items with a close substitute) and qimi (items without a like). The valuation date for usurped non-mithli items is fixed at the day of usurpation to prevent hardship. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying compensation rules in cases of ghasb (usurpation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of countable items
Countable items are divided into uniform (متقارب) and non-uniform (متفاوتة). Uniform items are treated as mithli; non-uniform items are non-mithli (qimi).
Example: eggs are uniform, livestock are non-uniform.
2
Note the ruling for uniform items
Uniform countable items are like measured items—they require replacement in kind (mithl), because the difference between individual items is small.
This follows from the general principle that mithli is compensated by mithl.
3
Understand the rule for non-uniform items
Non-uniform items have no exact like, so the right cannot be preserved in the genus. Therefore compensation is based on monetary value alone, assessed on the day of usurpation.
The value is fixed at the time of usurpation to avoid speculation.
4
Apply to a mixed example
Barley mixed with wheat has no like, so its value must be paid. This illustrates that even hybrid items fall under the non-mithli rule.
Purity of type affects classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس کی مثل موجود نہیں اس کی غصب کے دن کی قیمت لازم ہے
قال وما لا مثل له فعليه قيمته يوم غصبه معناه العدديات المتفاوتة لانه لما تعذر مراعاة الحق في الجنس فيراعى فى المالية وحدها دفعا للضرر بقدر الامكان اما العددى المتقارب فهو كالمكيل حتى يجب مثله لقلة التفاوت وفى البر المخلوط بالشعير القيمة لانه لا مثل له قال و على الغاصب رد العين المغصوبة معناه مادام قائما لقوله عليه السلام على اليد ما اخذت حتى ترد وقال عليه السلام لا يحل لاحد ان يأخذ متاع اخيه لاعباً ولا جادًا، فان اخذه فليرده عليه، ولان اليد حق مقصود وقد فوّتها عليه، فيجب اعادتها بالرد اليه، وهو الموجب الاصلى على ما قالوا ورد القيمة مخلص خلفا لانه قاصر اذ الكمال في رد العين والمالية وقيل الموجب الاصلى القيمة ورد العين مخلص ويظهر ذلك فى بعض الاحكام والواجب الرد في المكان الذى غصبه لتفاوت القيم بتفاوت الاماكن فان ادعى هلاكها حبسه الحاكم حتى يعلم انها لو كانت باقية لاظهرها او تقوم بينة، ثم قضى عليه ببدلها لان الواجب رد العين والهلاك بعارض فهو يدعى امرًا عارضا خلاف الظاهر فلا يقبل قوله كما اذا ادعى الافلاس وعليه ثمن متاع فيحبس الى ان يعلم ما يدعيه فاذا علم الهلاك سقط عنه رده فیلزمه رد بدله وهو القيمة
For that which has no like, its value on the day of usurpation is obligatory. Meaning: non-uniform countable items. Because when observing the right in the genus becomes difficult, it is observed only in the monetary value, to avoid harm as much as possible. As for uniform countable items, they are like measured items, so their mithl is obligatory due to little difference. In wheat mixed with barley, value is due because it has no like. And upon the usurper is the return of the usurped object, meaning as long as it exists, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "The hand is liable for what it took until it returns." And he said: "It is not lawful for anyone to take his brother's property, jestingly or seriously; if he takes it, let him return it." And because possession is a sought right, and he has caused it to be lost, so it must be restored by returning it. This is the primary obligation according to them, and returning value is a substitute as a successor because it is deficient, for perfection is in returning the object and its monetary value. And it is said: the primary obligation is value and returning the object is a substitute; this appears in some rulings. And it is obligatory to return it in the place where he usurped it, due to variation of values by locations. Then if he claims its destruction, the judge imprisons him until he knows that if it had remained, he would have produced it, or a proof is established. Then the judge decrees compensation for it, because the obligation is return of the object, and destruction is an incidental matter; he claims an incidental matter contrary to the apparent state, so his statement is not accepted, just as if the buyer claims insolvency while he owes the price of goods; he is imprisoned until what he claims is known. When destruction is known, the obligation of return is dropped, and he must return its substitute, which is the value.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage presents three connected rulings from the chapter on usurpation. First, for non-mithli items (items that have no exact market equivalent, e.g., gems or custom-made goods), the value is assessed on the day of usurpation, not later. The reasoning is that since the right cannot be preserved in the specific genus, it is preserved only in monetary value. Uniform countable items (like eggs or standard manufactured parts) are treated like measured items and require replacement in kind. Second, the usurper is obligated to return the actual object as long as it exists, based on clear hadith. The return of the object is the primary obligation; paying value is a substitute. Third, if the usurper claims the object has been destroyed, the judge must imprison him until the truth is known, because the claim contradicts the apparent state (that the object is still in his possession). Once destruction is confirmed, the obligation shifts to paying its value. This procedure parallels the case of a buyer who claims insolvency.

Key Terms
عددی متفاوتہ (adadiyyat mutafawita): Countable items that are non-uniform (e.g., livestock, gems), thus considered non-mithli.
مثل (mithl): An exact substitute in kind; a similar item of the same type and quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are uniform countable items treated like measured items?
A) Because they are weighed.
B) Because the difference between individual items is small.
C) Because they are non-mithli.
D) Because they have no like.

Key Takeaway
Non-uniform countable items are non-mithli and require compensation by value on the day of usurpation.

Return of the Usurped Object and Procedure on Claim of Destruction
Rulings on return of usurped property and procedure on destruction claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why returning the actual object is the primary obligation and describe the judge's procedure when the usurper claims destruction.

Core Idea
The usurper must return the actual object; if he claims it is destroyed, the judge detains him until the truth is known.

This lesson covers the core obligation of returning the usurped item (ayn maghsubah) and the procedural steps when the usurper alleges it has been destroyed. The hadith 'on the hand is what it took until it returns' establishes strict liability. The judge's detention balances the presumption of continued possession with the need for proof of destruction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary obligation
The usurper must return the actual object (ayn) as long as it exists. This is the original (asli) obligation based on hadith and the principle of restoring lost rights.
Returning value is only a substitute (khalaf) if the object is gone.
2
Examine the hadith proofs
The Prophet said: 'The hand is liable for what it took until it returns' and 'It is not lawful to take a brother's property... if he takes it, let him return it.' These indicate an imperative to restore the property itself.
The hadith are ahad but clear in meaning (qat'i dalala).
3
Understand the substitute nature of value
Paying value is a secondary obligation (badal) that only applies when the ayn cannot be returned. Some scholars considered value the primary obligation, but the majority view (zahir al-riwayah) treats return of the ayn as primary.
The passage mentions an alternative opinion but does not dismiss it.
4
Analyze the procedure when destruction is claimed
If the usurper claims the object is destroyed, the judge detains him until it becomes clear whether the object would have been produced if it existed, or until evidence of destruction is established.
The claim is contrary to the apparent state (property is in his possession), so it is not accepted without proof.
5
Draw analogy with insolvency claim
The procedure mirrors that of a buyer who claims insolvency while owing the price. In both cases, the claim contradicts the outward state, so detention is ordered until the truth is known.
This analogy (qiyas) reinforces the Hanafi rule that claims contrary to the apparent are not accepted prima facie.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

As for uniform countable items, they are like measured items, so their mithl is obligatory due to little difference. In wheat mixed with barley, value is due because it has no like. Goods Without Equivalent and the Obligation to Return
Explaining the value obligation for non-uniform goods and the primary duty to return the property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between homogeneous and heterogeneous countable properties and state the obligation (value vs. like) for each, and explain why the primary duty is return of the property.

Core Idea
Heterogeneous goods require value; homogeneous goods require like; but the core obligation is returning the very property.

This passage from Al-Hidayah tackles a key nuance in ghasb (usurpation) law: how to compensate when there is no exact equivalent. It distinguishes between items whose individuals vary in value (like melons) and those that are nearly identical (like eggs). You will also understand the primary duty of returning the property itself and an intra-Hanafi disagreement about whether the original obligation is the property or its value.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the usurped property
Identify whether the property falls into 'means that have a like' (mithliyyat) or 'what has no like' (ma la mithla lahu). Homogeneous countable items (e.g., walnuts, eggs) are like measured goods; heterogeneous countable items (e.g., melons, pomegranates) have no like.
Imam Zufar considers all countable as having no like, but the relied-upon Hanafi view distinguishes.
2
Determine the obligatory compensation
For homogeneous items, the like (mithl) is due. For heterogeneous items, the monetary value (qimah) at the time of usurpation is due. A special case: wheat mixed with barley has no like, so only value.
3
Understand the primary obligation: return the property
As long as the property exists, the usurper must return the very item (radd al-ayn). This is supported by the hadith: 'The hand is responsible for what it has taken until it returns it.' Possession is an intended right that must be restored.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
The mashayikh (majority) hold that the original obligation is to return the property; value is a substitute when it is destroyed. A minority view says the original obligation is the value, and returning the property is a release. The practical difference appears if the usurper is released from liability while the property still exists.
The relied-upon position is the majority view.
5
Apply the procedure for destruction claims
If the usurper claims the property is destroyed, the judge imprisons him until proof is established. Since destruction is contrary to the apparent presumption of possession, the claim is not accepted without evidence. Once destruction is proven, obligation shifts to paying value.
This mirrors the rule for insolvency claims in other debts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وما لا مثل له فعليه قيمته يوم غصبه معناه العدديات المتفاوتة لانه لما تعذر مراعاة الحق في الجنس فيراعى فى المالية وحدها دفعا للضرر بقدر الامكان اما العددى المتقارب فهو كالمكيل حتى يجب مثله لقلة التفاوت وفى البر المخلوط بالشعير القيمة لانه لا مثل له قال و على الغاصب رد العين المغصوبة معناه مادام قائما لقوله عليه السلام على اليد ما اخذت حتى ترد وقال عليه السلام لا يحل لاحد ان يأخذ متاع اخيه لاعباً ولا جادًا، فان اخذه فليرده عليه، ولان اليد حق مقصود وقد فوّتها عليه، فيجب اعادتها بالرد اليه، وهو الموجب الاصلى على ما قالوا ورد القيمة مخلص خلفا لانه قاصر اذ الكمال في رد العين والمالية وقيل الموجب الاصلى القيمة ورد العين مخلص ويظهر ذلك فى بعض الاحكام والواجب الرد في المكان الذى غصبه لتفاوت القيم بتفاوت الاماكن فان ادعى هلاكها حبسه الحاكم حتى يعلم انها لو كانت باقية لاظهرها او تقوم بينة، ثم قضى عليه ببدلها لان الواجب رد العين والهلاك بعارض فهو يدعى امرًا عارضا خلاف الظاهر فلا يقبل قوله كما اذا ادعى الافلاس وعليه ثمن متاع فيحبس الى ان يعلم ما يدعيه فاذا علم الهلاك سقط عنه رده فیلزمه رد بدله وهو القيمة
He said: And what has no like, then upon him is its value on the day he usurped it. Its meaning is heterogeneous countable items because when observance of the right in the genus becomes impossible, it is observed in the monetary value alone to repel harm as much as possible. As for the homogeneous countable, it is like the measured, so its like is obligatory due to little variation. And in wheat mixed with barley, the value is due because there is no like for it. He said: And upon the usurper is the return of the usurped property. Its meaning is as long as it remains, because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'The hand is responsible for what it has taken until it returns it.' And he, peace be upon him, said: 'It is not lawful for anyone to take his brother's property playfully or seriously; if he takes it, let him return it to him.' And because possession is an intended right which he has caused to be lost, so its restoration by returning to him is obligatory. And it is the original obligation according to what they said. And returning the value is a substitute as a successor because it is deficient, since perfection lies in returning the property and the monetary value. And it was said: The original obligation is the value, and returning the property is a release from liability. And that appears in some rulings. And the obligation is to return in the place where he usurped it, due to the variation of values with variation of places. Then if he claims its destruction, the judge will imprison him until it is known that if it had remained, he would have produced it, or evidence is established. Then he rules against him for its replacement, because the obligation is to return the property, and destruction is accidental. So he claims an accidental matter contrary to the apparent, so his statement is not accepted, just as if one claims insolvency while he is liable for the price of goods, he is imprisoned until his claim is known. So when destruction is known, his return drops, and he is obligated to return its replacement, which is the value.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah discusses the ruling for usurped goods that have no exact equivalent. The author first defines 'what has no like' (ma la mithla lahu) as heterogeneous countable items (e.g., melons, pomegranates, eggs). Since their individual values differ, it is impossible to require exact replacement; therefore, the obligation is to pay the monetary value at the time of usurpation. In contrast, homogeneous countable items like walnuts or eggs (according to the three Imams) are treated like measured goods, so the like (mithl) is obligatory because their values are close. A special case: wheat mixed with barley has no like, so only the value applies.

Next, the passage addresses the primary obligation: the usurper must return the very property as long as it exists, supported by the hadith 'The hand is responsible for what it has taken until it returns it' and another hadith prohibiting taking a brother's property. Possession is an intended right; usurpation destroys it, so restoration is obligatory. The mashayikh hold that returning the property is the original obligation, and paying value is merely a substitute (khalifah) for release from liability. Another view says value is the original obligation, and returning property is a release. The practical difference appears in certain rulings: e.g., if the usurper is released from liability while the property is still in his possession, that is valid only if value is the original obligation, because release from the property itself is invalid.

The place of return must be the location where the usurpation occurred, because market values vary by location. If the usurper claims the property has perished, the judge will imprison him until it becomes clear (either he produces it or evidence confirms destruction). The claim of destruction is contrary to the apparent presumption (that the property is still in his possession), so it is not accepted without proof. Once destruction is established, the obligation to return the property drops and he must pay its value.

Key Terms
ما لا مثل له (mā lā mithla lahu): Good that has no exact equivalent; specifically heterogeneous countable items like melons and pomegranates.
العددى المتقارب (al-‘adadī al-mutaqārib): Homogeneous countable items with little variation in value between individuals, e.g., walnuts, eggs.
رد العين (radd al-‘ayn): Returning the very property that was usurped.
القيمة (al-qīmah): Monetary value assessed at the time of usurpation, paid when the property is destroyed or has no like.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mashayikh view), what is the original obligation upon a usurper when the property is still in existence?
A) Pay the value of the property
B) Return the exact property to the owner
C) Imprison the usurper until he pays
D) Give an equivalent in kind

Key Takeaway
For usurped property, the primary duty is to return the exact item; if it has no like, value substitutes, but if it has a like (homogeneous countable), an equivalent item is due instead of value.

intermediate
6 min
Non-Mithli Items: Value Due on Day of Usurpation
Explains ruling and reasoning for non-mithli items in ghasb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation for usurped non-mithli items and explain the talil (legal reasoning) for assessing value on the day of usurpation.

Core Idea
When a usurped item has no exact equivalent, the usurper must pay its value on the day of usurpation.

In ghasb (usurpation), the primary remedy is restitution of the item itself. But when the item has no mithl (identical substitute), the law requires compensation in value. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position that value is assessed on the day of usurpation, not loss, and the reasoning rooted in preventing harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is ghasb of a non-mithli item; the ruling is the obligation (wujub) to pay its qima (value).
Check the passage for the explicit ruling: 'غاصب پر اس کی وہ قیمت واجب ہوگی جو غصب کرنے کے روز تھی'.
2
Understand the definitions
Distinguish mithli (items with uniform units) from qimi (items with variance). The passage references al-Quduri's definition of 'la mithla lahu' as countable items with differing individuals.
Examples: mithli = wheat (weight), qimi = unique fruits like pomegranates.
3
Locate the proof (talil)
The author provides the legal reason: 'جب حق مالک کی نگہداشت جنس معلوم میں مستعد رہو گئی تو خالی مالیت میں ملرظ رکھی جائے گی' – when the owner's right cannot be preserved in the specific genus, it is replaced by monetary value.
This is a qiyas-based argument: the value substitutes to repel harm.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a unique item usurped on day X and damaged on day Y, the value is fixed on day X.
The assessment date is critical; later market fluctuations are ignored.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشريح قوله وما لا مثل له .. الخ - اگر مغصوب ایسی چیز ہو جس کا مثل نہیں ہے تو غاصب پر اس کی وہ قیمت واجب ہوگی جو غصب کرنے کے روز تھی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری کے قول لامثل لہ سے مراد گنتی کی چیزیں ہیں جن کے افراد میں تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے بلخ، رمان ، سفر جل ، وجوب قیمت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جب حق مالک کی نگہداشت جنس معلوم میں مستعد رہو گئی تو خالی مالیت میں ملرظ رکھی جائے گی تا کہ جہاں تک ممکن ہے ضرر کا دفعیہ ہو جائے۔
Explanation of his statement 'and what has no similar...' - If the usurped item is something that has no similar (mithl), then the usurper is obliged to pay its value (qima) that it had on the day of usurpation. The author of al-Hidayah states that al-Quduri's statement 'la mithla lahu' refers to countable items whose individuals differ, like [types of fruits]. The reason for the obligation of value is that when the owner's right cannot be preserved in the specific genus, it is replaced by its monetary value so that harm is repelled as much as possible.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling for items that have no exact equivalent (mithl) in the market, such as unique or custom-made goods. The Hanafi ruling is that the usurper must pay the item's value on the day of usurpation, not on the day of loss. The reasoning is that the owner's right cannot be fulfilled by returning a similar item, so value payment is the only way to compensate. This is a talil (legal reasoning) based on necessity.

Key Terms
مثل (mithl): An item of the same type and similar quality, available for restitution.
قیمت (qima): Monetary value of the item, to be paid when mithl is unavailable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The value of a non-mithli usurped item is assessed on the day of usurpation, not the day of loss, to ensure just compensation.

Countable Items with Similar Individuals: Treated as Mithli
Ruling with proof via talil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for adadi mutaqarib items (like walnuts and eggs) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
Countable items with little individual variation are treated as mithli; mithl is wajib.

In ghasb (usurpation), items are classified as mithli (fungible) or qimi (non-fungible). The general rule is that mithli items require restitution of mithl (a similar item), while qimi items require payment of value. But what about countable items like eggs or walnuts, where individuals are nearly identical? The Hanafi school has a specific category for these: adadi mutaqarib. This lesson examines their ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that adadi mutaqarib refers to countable items whose individuals are closely similar, such as walnuts, eggs, and small coins (fulus).
These are distinct from adadi mutafawit (e.g., animals) where individuals differ greatly.
2
State the Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad (the three Imams) and most scholars, these items are like mithli. Therefore, the usurper must return a similar item (mithl), not its value.
The burden of restitution is wajib, not merely recommended.
3
Explain the reasoning (illah)
The underlying reason is that the value of such items varies little between individuals, making it possible to demand a like item. This is based on talil (legal reasoning).
If the variation were significant, they would be qimi.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar diverges: he holds that even these items are qimi because they are not perfectly equal (amthal mutasawiya). So he requires payment of value (qima).
The text does not cite explicit proof for Zufar; his view is based on strict equality.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the three Imams: restitution of mithl is obligatory. If the exact item is unavailable, the usurper must wait until a similar item is found (فَيَصْبِرُ حَتَّى يُوجَدَ مِثْلُهُ).
This majority view carries greater authority (zahir al-riwayah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله اما العددى المتقارب ... الخ ۔ رہی گنتی کی وہ چیزیں جن کے افراد متفاوت نہیں ہوتے جیسے جوز (اخروٹ ) بیض ( انڈے ) اور فلوس وغیرہ تو وہ ہمارے ائمہ ثلثہ اور اکثر علماء کے نزدیک مثلی کی طرح ہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ ان کا مثل واجب ہوگا کیونکہ ان کی مالیت میں تفاوت کم ہوتا ہے۔ امام زفر کے نزدیک ان میں بھی قیمت واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ وہ امثال متساوی نہیں ہیں۔ اہل مدینہ اور اصحاب ظاہر کے نزدیک ان کا مثل واجب ہوگا۔ فیصبر حتی يوجد مثله
His statement: 'As for countable items with close similarity...' - As for countable items whose individuals do not differ, such as walnuts, eggs, and small coins, they are like mithli (items with similar) according to our three Imams and most scholars. So their mithl is obligatory because their value differs little. Imam Zufar holds that even for these, value is obligatory because they are not completely equal. The people of Madinah and the Zahiris hold that their mithl is obligatory. So he waits until a similar item is found.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage discusses the category of items that are countable but have minimal variation between individuals, like walnuts or eggs. The majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) treats them as mithli, so the usurper must return a similar item. Imam Zufar disagrees and requires value because he considers them qimi due to slight differences. The practical effect: the usurper must wait until a like item is available.

Key Terms
عددى متقارب (adadi mutaqarib): Countable items with closely similar individuals (e.g., nuts, eggs).
مثلی (mithli): Fungible items that can be replaced by similar items without material difference.
قیمی (qimi): Non-fungible items that must be compensated by value because they are unique or vary greatly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the three Hanafi Imams, what must a usurper do if he takes a dozen eggs (adadi mutaqarib) and no similar eggs are currently available?
A) Pay the market value immediately
B) Wait until similar eggs are available, then return them
C) Pay double the value
D) Do nothing; eggs are not compensable

Key Takeaway
For adadi mutaqarib items, the Hanafi mufta bihi is restitution of mithl, based on the majority of the three Imams, and if unavailable, one must wait.

Obligation to Return the Specific Object if It Exists
Default ruling: return of the usurped 'ayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when usurped property still exists and identify the textual evidence (hadith) that establishes the obligation.

Core Idea
If the usurped property still exists, it must be returned — the possession right must be restored fully.

This lesson clarifies the primary obligation in cases of usurpation (ghasb): returning the specific item, not its value, if it remains in existence. The passage from Al-Hidayah lays down this default rule and supports it with two hadith. Understanding this foundational principle is essential before considering cases where the item is destroyed or damaged.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine whether the usurped property (al-maghsub) still exists in its original form ('ayn) or has perished (talif). The ruling depends on this distinction.
This passage deals only with the existing item scenario.
2
State the ruling
If the item still exists, the usurper is obligated (wajib) to return that exact item to the owner. No substitution or compensation is permissible while the 'ayn remains.
The ruling is wajib, not fard, due to the dalil being zanni.
3
Cite the hadith proofs
Two hadith are quoted: (1) 'The hand is responsible for what it took until it returns it'—this establishes liability for the exact item. (2) 'Let none of you take his brother's property... and if he takes his brother's stick, let him return it'—this emphasizes returning even a trivial item.
Both hadith are ahad (single-narrator), hence zanni al-thubut.
4
Explain the rationale
The owner's possession (qabd) is a desired right (haqq maqsud). The usurper nullified this possession, so restoration requires returning the same item, not merely compensating its value.
This is a rational argument (ma'qul) supporting the textual evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وعلى الغاصب ... الخ ۔ مذکورہ تفصیل تو اس وقت ہے جب مغصوب تلف ہوگئی ہو۔ اور اگر وہ بعینہ باقی ہو تو اس کو واپس کرنا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے۔ على اليد ما اخذت حتى تؤدى (سنن اربعہ احمد ، طبرانی ، حاکم ، ابن ابی شیبہ عن سمرة ) اسی طرح آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے ۔ "لا يا خذن احدكم متاع اخيه جاد اولا لاعباً واذا اخذ احدكم عصا اخيه فليردها " ( ابوداؤد، ترندی، احمد ، ابن ابی شیبہ، ابن راہویہ، ابو داؤد طیالسی، حاکم ، بخاری فی المفرد عن یزید بن السائب ) نیز اس لئے بھی کہ آدمی کا قبضہ ایک حق مقصود ہوتا ہے کہ اس سے ہر طرح انتفاع کر سکتا ہے اور غاصب نے یہ قبضہ مٹادیا تو اس قبضہ کا اعادہ اس طرح ضروری ہے کہ اس کو وہی چیز واپس کر دے۔
His statement: 'And upon the usurper...' - The aforementioned detail applies when the usurped item has perished. If it still exists in kind, returning it is obligatory because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The hand is responsible for what it took until it returns it.' (reported in Sunan Arba'a, etc.) Similarly, the Prophet said: 'Let none of you take his brother's property, seriously or jokingly; and if he takes his brother's stick, let him return it.' (Abu Dawood, etc.) Also because a person's possession is a desired right from which he can benefit in all ways, and the usurper has nullified this possession, so restoration is necessary by returning the same item.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage establishes the primary ruling: if the usurped property remains in existence, the usurper must return it in its original form. The proof is two hadiths: 'al-yad ma akhadhat hatta tu'adda' and the prohibition of taking a brother's property even playfully. The reasoning is that the owner's right of possession must be restored fully. The usurper cannot refuse return if the property still exists.

Key Terms
عین (ayn): The specific physical property that was usurped.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the obligation of the usurper if the usurped property still exists?
A) Pay its value
B) Return the same item
C) Compensate with profit
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The primary obligation in ghasb when the item exists is to return that specific item; this is wajib based on hadith and the principle of restoring possession.

Primary Obligation in Ghasb: Return of 'Ayn or Value?
Discusses two scholarly views on the primary obligation in ghasb and its practical consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi views on the primary obligation in ghasb (return of 'ayn vs. value) and explain the practical consequences (thamarah) of each view.

Core Idea
The primary obligation in ghasb is either the specific item or its value—the difference matters for ibra, kafala, and zakat.

This passage presents a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement about the nature of the usurper's duty. Some masters hold that the core obligation is to return the very object, while others argue that the obligation is the monetary value. The author of al-Hidayah then shows how this theoretical difference yields real legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing views
Find the two positions presented in the text: some mashayikh hold that the primary obligation (mujib asli) is return of the specific 'ayn; others hold that it is the value (qimah).
The text uses 'بقول مشائخ' to introduce each view.
2
Examine the legal reasoning behind each view
Reflect on why each view considers its position primary. The 'ayn-primary view sees return of the specific item as complete performance; the value-primary view sees value as the real liability that return of the item merely fulfills.
The text calls one 'کامل' (complete) and the other 'ناقص' (deficient).
3
Trace the practical consequences (thamarah)
The author of al-Hidayah lists three rulings that flow from the dispute: ibra (release), kafala (suretyship), and zakat. For each, determine which view the ruling supports.
The text uses 'يظهر ذلك' to introduce the evidence.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Based on the thamarah, conclude that the value-primary view is the one that aligns with the legal system's coherence, as the rulings on ibra and kafala depend on the obligation being a monetary debt.
The Hidayah does not explicitly choose, but the inference is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وهو الموجب الاصلی انخ - پھر بقول مشائخ غصب کا اصلی حکم یہی ہے کہ بعینہ وہی چیز واپس کی جائے ۔ رہا قیمت واپس کرنا سو یہ چھٹکارا پانے کے لئے اس کا خلیفہ ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ناقص ادائیگی ہے۔ کامل ادائیگی تو یہی ہے کہ عین بھی مع مالیت واپس کی جائے ۔ اور بقول مشائخ غصب کا اصلی حکم رد قیمت ہے اور ردعین مخلص ہے۔ قوله ويظهر ذلك ..... الخ - صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس اختلاف کا ثمرہ بعض احکام میں ظاہر ہوتا ہے مثلاً : ا۔ اگر غاصب کو تاوان سے بری کر دیا تو یہ صحیح ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر اس کے بعد تلف ہو جائے تو ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اگر موجب اصلی قیمت نہ ہوتی تو ابرا صحیح نہ ہوتا۔ لان الابراء عن العين لا يصح۔ مغصوب کی کفالت صیح ہے۔ معلوم ہوا کہ اصلی موجب قیمت ہے ورنہ ظاہر ہے کہ عین کی کفالت صحیح نہیں ہوتی ۔ ۳۔ اگر غاصب کی ملک میں نصاب ہو اور اس نے کوئی چیز غصب کی ہو تو اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی جب کہ قیمت مغصوب کے مقابلہ میں وہ نصاب کم ہوتا ہو۔
His statement: 'And it is the primary obligatory...' - According to some mashayikh, the primary ruling of ghasb is to return the specific item. As for returning value, it is a substitute to obtain release. Because it is a deficient performance. Complete performance is to return the specific item along with its value. And according to other mashayikh, the primary ruling is return of value, and return of the specific item is the means of release. His statement: 'And that becomes apparent...' - The author of al-Hidayah says that the fruit of this difference appears in some rulings, e.g.: 1. If the usurper is freed from liability (ibra) while the item still exists, it is valid; if later it perishes, no compensation is due. If the primary obligation were not value, ibra would not be valid, because ibra from a specific item is not valid. 2. Suretyship (kafala) for the usurped item is valid. This shows that the primary obligation is value; otherwise, suretyship for a specific item is not valid. 3. If the usurper possesses a nisab and has usurped something, zakat is not obligatory on him if the value of the usurped item reduces the nisab below the threshold.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi theoretical dispute about the nature of the usurper's obligation. Some scholars (mashayikh) argue that the primary duty is to return the 'ayn (specific object), while the payment of value is a secondary substitute. Others argue the opposite: the primary duty is value, and returning the 'ayn is a means of fulfilling that value obligation. The author of al-Hidayah then shows the practical consequences: if the primary obligation were return of the 'ayn, then releasing the usurper from liability (ibra) while the 'ayn exists would be invalid because ibra from a specific item is not legally recognized; but if the primary obligation is value, ibra is valid. Similarly, suretyship for a ghasb case is valid only if the obligation is value. Also, the effect on zakat: if the usurper's wealth plus the value of the usurped item meets nisab, but the item's value reduces it, no zakat is due, indicating that the obligation is considered part of liability.

Key Terms
موجب اصلی (mujib asli): The primary legal obligation that directly arises from the act of ghasb.
ابرا (ibra): Release from liability, a legal discharge of debt.
کفالة (kafala): Suretyship, a contract where a third party guarantees the obligation of the usurper.
زکاة (zakat): Obligatory alms on wealth, calculated based on nisab threshold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is suretyship (kafala) for a usurped item considered valid according to one view?
A) Because the primary obligation is return of the specific item
B) Because the primary obligation is value
C) Because the item is fungible
D) Because of necessity

Key Takeaway
The primary obligation in ghasb is not simply the return of the item; the Hanafi school has a nuanced debate, and the practical effects point to value as the primary obligation.

Return of Usurped Property and Procedure for Claim of Loss
Ruling with proof via qiyas on procedure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a usurped item must be returned at the place of usurpation and apply the Hanafi procedure when the usurper claims loss without evidence.

Core Idea
The usurper's claim of loss is not accepted without evidence; imprisonment compels truth.

When property is unlawfully taken (ghasb), Islamic law obligates the precise return of the item. This lesson examines two key rules: first, the item must be returned at the original location because market values differ by place. Second, if the usurper claims the item perished, his word alone is insufficient—the judge must imprison him until evidence is produced or the truth emerges. The analogy to a buyer claiming insolvency reinforces the principle that claims contrary to the apparent state require proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary obligation
Determine that the usurper must return the specific item at the exact place it was taken.
The reason given is that values differ by location.
2
Understand the reason for location-specific return
Recognize that the ruling is based on the fact that the price of goods can vary between places, so returning elsewhere could cause loss.
3
Examine the procedure when loss is claimed
If the usurper claims the item perished, the judge does not accept this claim without evidence; instead, he imprisons the usurper as a coercive measure.
Imprisonment is procedural, not punitive.
4
Analyze the parallel to buyer's insolvency
The passage draws an analogy: a buyer who must pay the price but claims insolvency is not believed without proof; similarly, the usurper's claim of loss is suspect.
Both are claimants of an event contrary to the default presumption.
5
Conclude the shift from specific return to compensation
Once loss is established (by evidence or prolonged imprisonment), the obligation shifts from returning the specific item to paying its value.
Compensation is the value (qimah) at the time and place of usurpation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله والواجب الرد .... الخ - پھر جہاں سے غاصب نے اس کو غصب کیا تھا وہیں واپس کرنا ضروری ہے کیونکہ اماکن کے اختلاف سے قیمتیں مختلف ہوتی ہیں۔ اب اگر غاصب نے یہ دعویٰ کیا کہ مال مغصوب تلف ہو گیا ، تو حاکم اس کو قید رکھے ۔ یہاں تک کہ یہ بات کھل جائے کہ اگر وہ مال باقی ہوتا تو وہ مشقت قید سے چھوٹنے کے لئے ضرور ظاہر کر دیتا۔ یا پھر غاصب اس کے تلف ہو جانے پر بینہ قائم کرے۔ اگر یہ نہ ہو تو قاضی اس غاصب پر مال مغصوب کے عوض کا حکم دے دے گا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ غاصب پر بعینہ مال واپس کرنا ضروری اور واجب تھا اور تلف ہو جانا عارضی امر ہے۔ پس وہ خلاف ظاہر امر عارض کا مدعی ہو لہذا خالی اس قول کا مقبول نہ ہوگا جیسے ایک خریدار جس پر مبیع کا ثمن لازم ہے وہ اپنے افلاس کا دعوی کرے تو خالی دعوئی مقبول نہیں ہوتا۔ بلکہ اس کو تعزیر کیا جاتا ہے پھر جب مال مغصوب کا تلف ہونا معلوم ہو جائے تو عین مغصوب واپس کرنا اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو جائے گا اور اس کا عوض واپس کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور عوض دہی قیمت ہے۔
His statement: 'And the obligatory return...' - Then it is necessary to return it to the same place from where the usurper usurped it, because values differ depending on location. Now if the usurper claims that the usurped property perished, the judge should imprison him until it becomes clear that if the property existed, he would have produced it to avoid the hardship of prison. Or the usurper should provide evidence (bayyinah) of its loss. If not, the judge will order him to pay compensation for the usurped property. The reason is that returning the specific property was obligatory upon the usurper, and loss is a supervening event. So he is a claimant of something contrary to the apparent state; hence, his mere statement is not accepted, just as a buyer who is obliged to pay the price of a purchase claims insolvency - his mere claim is not accepted, but he is chastised. Then when the loss of the usurped property is known, the obligation to return the specific item falls from his liability, and compensation becomes necessary, and the compensation is value.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage explains two procedural rules: first, the usurped item must be returned at the same location where it was taken, because market values vary by region. Second, if the usurper claims the item was lost, the judge does not accept his word without evidence. The usurper is imprisoned as a coercive measure to reveal the truth, because the default assumption is that the item still exists. This is analogous to a buyer who claims insolvency - the claim is not accepted without proof. Once loss is established, the obligation shifts to payment of value. This shows the strong presumption in favor of the existence of the usurped property.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence, usually two witnesses, to prove the loss of the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the judge do if the usurper claims the item perished without evidence?
A) Accept the claim and order value
B) Imprison him until proof
C) Free him
D) Fine him

Key Takeaway
The usurper's unsupported claim of loss does not discharge liability; the judge uses imprisonment to extract the truth, and only when loss is established does compensation replace specific return.

Ghasb: Limited to Movable Property – The Hanafi Position and Its Proof
Establishes that ghasb is defined over movable properties, with disagreement on immovable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghasb of immovable property and evaluate the opposing argument from Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Ghasb requires physical transfer; thus, taking immovable property does not create liability for its destruction in Hanafi law.

This passage from al-Hidayah tackles a fundamental definition: what counts as ghasb (usurpation)? The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, restricts ghasb to movable property. But Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i disagree. Let's examine the reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is usurping immovable property ('aqar). The ruling from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: no liability if it perishes in the usurper's hands.
This is the majority Hanafi view.
2
Understand the hanafi definition
Ghasb requires physical removal (naql) of the property itself from the owner's possession. This is possible only with movable property.
The definition is based on the act of transfer, not mere control.
3
Examine the opposing argument
Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i argue that mere physical control suffices because two possessions cannot co-exist; thus, establishing control necessarily removes the owner's possession.
They equate control with ghasb.
4
Analyze the hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that control over immovable is an act on the owner (removing him), not an act on the property itself. Therefore, it does not fulfill the definition of ghasb.
The analogy to denial of deposit is also refuted.
5
Determine the practical difference
If the property perishes, the Hanafi mufta bihi says no liability; the opposing view says liability applies. This affects compensation claims in real-world cases.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و الغصب فيما ينقل ويحول لان الغصب بحقيقته يتحقق فيه دون غيره لان ازالة اليد بالنقل، واذا غصب عقارا فهلك فى يده لم يضمنه وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف، وقال محمد يضمنه وهو قول ابى يوسف الاول وبه قال الشافعى لتحقق اثبات اليد، ومن ضرورته زوال يد المالك لاستحالة اجتماع اليدين على محل واحد في حالة واحدة، فيتحقق الوصفان وهو الغصب على ما بيناه، فصار كالمنقول وجحود الوديعة لهما ان الغصب اثبات اليد بازالة يد المالك بفعل فى العين وهذا لا يتصور في العقار لان يد المالك لا تزول الا باخراجه عنها، وهو فعل فيه لا فى العقار، فصار كما اذا بعد المالك عن المواشى وفى المنقول النقل فعل فيه، وهو الغصب ومسالة الجحود ممنوعة ولو سلمت فالضمان هناک بترك الحفظ الملتزم وبالجحود تارك لذلك
ترجمہ اور غصب اسی میں ہوتا ہے جو منتقل ومحول کی جا سکے کیونکہ غصب در حقیقت اس میں متحقق ہوتا ہے نہ کہ اس کے علاوہ میں کیونکہ قبضہ کا ازالہ بذریعہ نقل ہی ہوتا ہے۔ اگر کوئی عقد غصب کیا اور وہ اس کے قبضہ میں تلف ہو گیا تو غاصب اس کا ضامن نہ ہوگا یہ شیخین کے نزدیک ہے۔ امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ ضامن ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف کا پہلا قول یہی ہے اور امام شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں ۔ قبضہ ثابت کرنا محقق ہونے کی وجہ سے جس سے ضروری ہے مالک کے قبضہ کا زائل ہونا کیونکہ بحالت واحد محل واحد پر دو قبضوں کا جمع ہونا محال ہے پس دونوں وصف متحقق ہو گئے اور یہی غصب ہے پس یہ غصب منقول اور انکار ودیعت کی طرح ہو گیا۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ غصب اپنا قبضہ ثابت کرنا ہے۔ مالک کا قبضہ زائل کر کے عین میں کسی فعل کے ساتھ اور یہ بات عقار میں غیر متصور ہے۔ کیونکہ مالک کا قبضہ زائل نہیں ہوگا۔ مگر اس کو عقار سے نکالنے کے ساتھ اور یہ فعل مالک میں ہو گا نہ کہ عین مال میں تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے مالک کو گلہ مویشی سے دور ہٹا دے اور منقول کو منتقل کرنا خود اس مال میں فعل ہے اور یہی غصب ہے اور انکار ودیعت کا مسئلہ ممنوع ہے اور اگر تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو وہاں تاوان اس حفاظت کے چھوڑنے کی وجہ سے ہے ۔ جس کا التزام کیا تھا اور انکار سے اسی کو ترک کرنے والا ہے۔ تشريح قوله والغصب فيما ينقل .. الخ - اس قول کا اصل مقصد یہ بیان کرنا ہے کہ غصب کا تحقق صرف اشیاء منقولہ میں ہوتا ہے جن کو ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ رکھنا تمکن ہوا اور غیر منقول میں غصب محقق نہیں ہوتا۔ صرف حقق غصب فی المنقول کا بیان
He said: And ghasb applies to what is movable and transferable, because ghasb in its reality occurs in it and not in others, since removal of possession is by transfer. If someone usurps immovable property (aqar) and it perishes in his hands, he is not liable – this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said he is liable, and this was Abu Yusuf's first opinion, and al-Shafi'i agreed with it, because there is actual establishment of hand possession, and necessarily the owner's possession is removed, since it is impossible for two hand-possessions to co-exist on one place simultaneously. Thus the two attributes are realized, which is ghasb, as we explained. So it becomes like movable property and the denial of deposit. For them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), ghasb is the establishment of possession by removing the owner's possession through an act on the 'ayn, and this is not conceivable in immovable property because the owner's possession does not end except by removing him from it, which is an act on him, not on the property. So it is like if the owner is distanced from livestock. And in movable property, the transfer is an act on the property itself, and that is ghasb. The issue of denial of deposit is refuted; even if conceded, the liability there is due to abandoning the pledged care, and denial abandons that.
Translation: And ghasb occurs only in what can be moved and transferred, because ghasb in reality is realized in it and not in others, because removal of possession is by transfer. If someone usurps immovable property (aqar) and it perishes in his possession, the usurper is not liable – this is according to the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Imam Muhammad says he is liable, and this was Abu Yusuf's first opinion, and Imam al-Shafi'i also held this view, due to the actual establishment of possession, which necessitates the removal of the owner's possession, because it is impossible for two possessions to be on one place at the same time. So both attributes are realized, and that is ghasb, so it becomes like movable property and the denial of deposit. The evidence of the two Shaykhs is that ghasb is establishing one's own possession by removing the owner's possession through an act on the 'ayn, and this is not conceivable in immovable property, because the owner's possession does not end except by removing him from it, and that is an act on him, not on the property. So it is like the case where the owner is removed from livestock. And in movable property, the transfer is an act on the property itself, and that is ghasb. The matter of denial of deposit is rejected; even if accepted, the liability there is due to abandoning the committed care, and denial abandons that. Explanation of his statement 'and ghasb applies to movable property' – the main purpose of this statement is to explain that ghasb is realized only in movable items that can be moved from one place to another, and in immovable property ghasb is not realized. Only the realization of ghasb in movable property is explained.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage addresses a foundational definition: ghasb (usurpation) is legally applicable only to movable property (manqul). The reason is that the essence of ghasb involves physically seizing an item and removing it from the owner's possession by transferring it. For immovable property ('aqar), such physical transfer is impossible – the owner's possession is only removed by physically removing the owner. Thus, the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) holds that there is no liability for the destruction of immovable property in a usurper's hands. However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that mere physical control without transfer suffices to establish ghasb and liability. The text also refutes an analogy to denial of deposit (juhud al-wadi'ah), arguing that liability there stems from breaching a duty of care, not from the act of taking.

Key Terms
منقول (manqul): Movable property that can be physically transferred from one location to another.
عقار ('aqar): Immovable property such as land and buildings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if someone usurps an immovable property and it perishes in his hands, what is the ruling?
A) He is liable for its value
B) He is not liable
C) He must return a similar immovable
D) He pays double

Key Takeaway
Ghasb in Hanafi law is defined by physical transfer (naql), so it applies only to movables; for immovables, no liability arises from mere possession.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ghasb in Immovables
Explains the ruling that ghasb applies only to movables and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on immovables

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ghasb in immovables, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to scenarios involving immovable property.

Core Idea
Ghasb requires physical transfer; immovables cannot be transferred, so no liability.

This passage from the Book of Usurpation delves into a key intra-Hanafi disagreement: does the legal category of ghasb (usurpation) apply to immovable property like land and buildings? While the majority of the school holds that it does not, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani dissents. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between legal categories based on the nature of the property and the type of act required for liability.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
Identify the general rule from the text: ghasb occurs only in movables (manqul) because it requires physical transfer (naql). Immovables ('aqar) cannot be transferred, so the usurper is not liable if the property perishes naturally.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, which is the mufta bihi.
2
Identify the opposing view
Note that Imam Muhammad (and initially Abu Yusuf) holds that ghasb does apply to immovables because taking possession necessarily removes the owner's hand, establishing both elements of ghasb.
3
Analyze the proofs
Examine the two proofs: (1) Muhammad relies on the impossibility of two hands on one place and analogizes to movables and denial of deposit; (2) The Shaykhayn require an act upon the property itself (فعل في العين) and argue that expelling the owner is an act upon the owner, not the property.
The hadith about usurping land is interpreted metaphorically by the Shaykhayn.
4
Understand the rebuttal
The text explains why the hadith does not establish worldly liability: it speaks of punishment in the Hereafter, and the word 'ghasb' in the hadith is metaphorical. The Shaykhayn also refute the analogy with denial of deposit.
This is a classic example of qiyas khafi (subtle analogy).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied‑upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: no liability for immovables. This is the view upheld by al‑Marghinani and later Hanafi authorities.
Practical consequence: if a house collapses naturally, the usurper does not pay its value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الغصب
اشرف الله : یہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ کہ یہ بات کھل جائے کہ اگر وہ مال باقی ہوتا تو وہ مشقت قید سے چھوٹنے کے لئے ضرور ظاہر کر دیتا۔ یا پھر غاصب اس کے تلف ہو جانے پر بینہ قائم کرے۔ اگر یہ نہ ہو تو قاضی اس غاصب پر مال مغصوب کے عوض کا حکم دے دے گا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ غاصب پر بعینہ مال واپس کرنا ضروری اور واجب تھا اور تلف ہو جانا عارضی امر ہے۔ پس وہ خلاف ظاہر امر عارض کا مدعی ہو لہذا خالی اس قول کا مقبول نہ ہوگا جیسے ایک خریدار جس پر مبیع کاشن لازم ہے وہ اپنے افلاس کا دعوی کرے تو خالی دعوئی مقبول نہیں ہوتا۔ بلکہ اس کو تنبوس کیا جاتا ہے پھر جب مال مغصوب کا تلف ہونا معلوم ہو جائے تو عین مغصوب واپس کرنا اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو جائے گا اور اس کا عوض واپس کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور عوض دہی قیمت ہے۔

قال و الغصب فيما ينقل ويحول لان الغصب بحقيقته يتحقق فيه دون غيره لان ازالة اليد بالنقل، واذا غصب عقارا فهلك فى يده لم يضمنه وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف، وقال محمد يضمنه وهو قول ابى يوسف الاول وبه قال الشافعى لتحقق اثبات اليد، ومن ضرورته زوال يد المالك لاستحالة اجتماع اليدين على محل واحد في حالة واحدة، فيتحقق الوصفان وهو الغصب على ما بيناه، فصار كالمنقول وجحود الوديعة لهما ان الغصب اثبات اليد بازالة يد المالك بفعل فى العين وهذا لا يتصور في العقار لان يد المالك لا تزول الا باخراجه عنها، وهو فعل فيه لا فى العقار، فصار كما اذا بعد المالك عن المواشى وفى المنقول النقل فعل فيه، وهو الغصب ومسالة الجحود ممنوعة ولو سلمت فالضمان هناک بترك الحفظ الملتزم وبالجحود تارك لذلك
