تشريح قوله والغصب فيما ينقل .. الخ - اس قول کا اصل مقصد یہ بیان کرنا ہے کہ غصب کا تحقق صرف اشیاء منقولہ میں ہوتا ہے جن کو ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ رکھنا تمکن ہوا اور غیر منقول میں غصب محقق نہیں ہوتا۔ صرف حقق غصب فی المنقول کا بیان مقصود نہیں ہے کیونکہ نہ تو اس میں کوئی خلاف ہے نہ ہی اشتباہ، خلاف داشتباہ تو غیر منقول میں غصب کے متحقق نہ ہونے میں ہے۔ پر اترکیب مذکور و الغصب فيما ينقل ويحول میں قصر و حصر معتبر ہے جیسا کہ تاج الشریعہ صاحب عنایہ نے بلکہ خود صاحب بدایہ نے بھی اس کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے ۔ " حيث قال لان الغصب بحقيقته يتحقق فيه دون غيره “ اب رہی یہ بات کہ ترکیب میں اداة حصر کیا ہے؟ سو وہ غالبا لام جنس کے ساتھ مسند الیہ کی تعریف ہے کہ یہ مسند پر قصر مسند الیہ کا فائدہ دیتی ہے جس کی تصریح علم معانی میں موجود ہے۔ و شکوہ بخو التوکل علی اللہ، الكرم فی العرب الائمة من قریش ، قول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شیخین کے نز د یک غصب صرف اشیاء منقولہ میں ہوتا ہے کیونکہ غصب در حقیقت اعیان منقولہ ہی میں ہوتا ہے غیر منقولہ میں نہیں ہوتا اس لئے که غصب ازالہ کید کے بغیر نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اور یہ مالک کا ازالہ اسی وقت ہوگا جب منقول کو منتقل کر لیا جائے ۔ حالانکہ عقار میں نقل و تحویل ناممکن ہے۔
قوله اذا غصب عقارا .... الخ - یہ مسئلہ اصل مذکور پر متفرع ہے اس لئے واؤ کے بجائے فاء کے ساتھ فاذا غصب کہنا چاہیے۔ چنانچہ دیگر عام کتب میں اس موقع پر کلمہ کا اور محط میں کلمہ حتی لایا گیا ہے اور تعجب کی بات یہ ہے کہ یہاں مختصر القدوری میں کلمہ فاء ہی تھا مگر صاحب ہدایہ نے بدایہ اور ہدایہ دونوں میں فاء کو واؤ سے بدل دیا۔
بہر کیف مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے عقار وزمین ، درخت، دار عمارت وغیرہ) کو غصب کیا اور اس کے پاس کسی آفت سماویہ سے ہلاک ہوگئی ۔ مثلاً سیلاب کے غلبہ سے زمین ڈوب گئی ۔ یا زلزلہ سے مکان منہدم ہو گیا یا عمارت سیلاب کی زد میں آگئی تو شیخین کے نزدیک اس پر عضمان نہ ہوگا۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک چونکہ غصب کا تحقق غیر منقولہ میں بھی ہوتا ہے اس لئے ان کے یہاں منمان ہوگا۔ امام زفر اور ائمہ ثلاثہ بھی یہی فرماتے ہیں۔ امام ابو یوسف کا بھی پہلا قول یہی ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ جب اس نے دوسرے کی زمین لے کر قبضہ جمالیا تو لا محالہ مالک کا قبضہ زائل ہو گیا کیونکہ بحالت واحدہ ایک محل پر دو قبضوں کا جمع ہونا محال ہے۔ پس دونوں وصف متحقق ہو گئے یعنی ازالہ یہ مققہ اور اثبات ید مبطلہ ، اور یہی غصب ہے تو عقار کا حکم ایسا ہو گیا جیسے مال منقول کو غصب کرنا ودیعت کا انکار کرنا کہ ان میں بالا تفاق ضامن ہوتا ہے نیز حدیث میں ہے کہ "جو شخص کسی کی بالشت بھر زمین غصب کرے گا حق تعالیٰ قیامت کے روز اس کی گردن میں سات طبق نو مین کا طوق ڈالی گا۔ (صحیحین)
قوله ولهما ان الغصب ... الخ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ غصب کے لئے ازالہ یہ محققہ اور اثبات ید مبطلہ کے ساتھ عین مغصوب میں غاصب کا تصرف بھی ضروری ہے اور یہ بات زمین میں غیر متصور ہے۔ کیونکہ ازالہ ید مالک کی صورت یہی ہے کہ اس کو زمین سے نکال دیا جائے اور ظاہر ہے کہ نکالنا صرف تصرف فی المالک ہے نہ کہ تصرف فی المغصوب ۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا۔ جیسے مویشی کے گلہ سے اس کے مالک کو دور ہٹا دے کہ اس صورت میں اگر گلہ تلف ہو جائے تو غصب نہیں ہوتا رہی حدیث مذکور سودہ مدعا پر ولالت نہیں کرتی اس لئے کہ اس میں آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے غصب ارض کی جزاء تطویق بیان کی ہے ۔ اگر ضمان واجب ہوتا تو اس کو بیان فرماتے ۔ کیونکہ ضمان دنیاوی احکام میں سے ہے۔ نیز حدیث میں زمین پر لفظ غصب کا اطلاق مجازا ہے جیسے حدیث من باع حراھ میں بیچ حر کے لئے لفظ بیع بولا گیا والا لزم تحقق البيع فى الحر علاوه ازین صحیحین میں غصب شبرا “ کے بجائے اخذ شبراً " ہے۔۔
Book of Usurpation. Ashraf Allah: This is the Urdu commentary of Hidayah volume 12, such that it becomes clear that if that property had remained, he would have definitely shown that hardship to be released from imprisonment. Or the usurper should bring evidence for its destruction. If not, the judge will order the usurper to pay compensation for the usurped property. The reason is that returning the exact property was necessary and obligatory upon the usurper, and destruction is an incidental matter. So he is claiming an incidental matter contrary to the apparent, therefore his mere statement will not be accepted, just as a buyer upon whom the delivery of the sold item is obligatory, if he claims his own insolvency, his mere claim is not accepted, rather he is warned. Then when the destruction of the usurped property becomes known, returning the exact property falls from his responsibility, and returning its compensation becomes necessary, and compensation is the price. Usurpation occurs in movable and transferable things. He said: And ghasb is in that which is movable and transferable, because ghasb in its reality is realized in it and not in other, because removal of the hand is by transfer. And if he usurped an immovable and it perished in his hand, he does not guarantee it, and this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: He guarantees it, and this is the first opinion of Abu Yusuf, and al-Shafi'i also said it, due to the realization of establishing the hand, and from its necessity is the removal of the owner's hand because it is impossible for two hands to be on one place at one time, so both descriptions are realized, which is ghasb as we explained, so it becomes like movable and denial of deposit. Their (the two shaykhs') argument is that ghasb is establishing the hand by removing the owner's hand through an act upon the substance (ayn), and this is not conceivable in immovables because the owner's hand is not removed except by expelling him from it, and that is an act upon him, not upon the substance, so it becomes like when the owner is removed from livestock. And in movables, transfer is an act upon it, and that is ghasb. And the case of denial of deposit is prevented, and if it is granted, then liability there is due to abandoning the preservation that was undertaken, and by denying it, one is abandoning that. Translation: And ghasb occurs only in that which can be moved and transferred, because ghasb in reality is realized in it and not in others, because removal of possession is through transfer. If someone usurped an immovable and it perished in his possession, the usurper will not be liable, according to the two shaykhs. Imam Muhammad says he will be liable. This is the first opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Shafi'i also holds it. Because establishing possession is realized, from which necessarily follows the removal of the owner's possession, because it is impossible for two possessions to be on one place at one time. So both descriptions are realized, and this is ghasb. So this becomes like movable and denial of deposit. The proof of the two shaykhs is that ghasb is establishing one's own possession by removing the owner's possession through an act upon the substance, and this is not conceivable in immovables, because the owner's possession will not be removed except by expelling him from the immovable, and this is an act upon the owner, not upon the property. So it becomes like removing the owner from a herd of livestock. And in movables, transfer is an act upon the property itself, and that is ghasb. And the case of denial of deposit is rejected; and if it is accepted, then liability there is due to abandoning the preservation that was undertaken, and by denying, one is abandoning that. Exegesis: The saying 'wa al-ghasb fima yunqalu...' - the real purpose of this statement is to state that ghasb is realized only in movable things that can be moved from one place to another, and in immovables ghasb is not realized. It is not intended to merely state that ghasb is realized in movables because there is no disagreement or ambiguity in that; the disagreement and ambiguity are in the non-realization of ghasb in immovables. In the mentioned construction 'al-ghasb fima yunqalu wa yuhawwalu', there is consideration of restriction and limitation, as Taj al-Shari'ah, the author of al-'Inayah, and even the author of al-Bidayah himself have pointed to this. Where he said: 'because ghasb in its reality is realized in it and not in other.' Now what is the particle of restriction in the construction? So it is mostly the definition of the subject (musnad ilayh) with lam al-jins, which gives the benefit of restricting the predicate (musnad) to the subject, as is explained in the science of meanings. And 'wa shakuhu bikhawu al-tawakkuli ala Allah, al-karim fi al-arab al-aimmah min quraysh,' the meaning of the statement is that according to the two shaykhs, ghasb is only in movable things, because ghasb in reality occurs in movable things, not in immovables, because ghasb cannot be without removal of the hand. And this removal of the owner will only happen when the movable is transferred, whereas in immovables, transfer and moving are impossible. His saying: 'idha ghasaba 'aqaran...' - this issue is a branch of the mentioned principle, so instead of waw it should be fa' with 'fa-idha ghasaba'. Thus in other common books, at this place the word 'ka' and in some places the word 'hatta' is brought, and it is surprising that here in Mukhtasar al-Quduri the word fa' was there, but the author of al-Hidayah in both al-Bidayah and al-Hidayah changed fa' to waw. In any case, the issue is that if someone usurped an immovable (land, tree, house, building, etc.) and it is destroyed in his possession by a heavenly calamity, e.g., the land sank due to flood, or the house collapsed due to earthquake, or the building came under flood, then according to the two shaykhs there will be no liability. According to Imam Muhammad, since ghasb is realized in immovables as well, there will be liability. Imam Zufar and the three imams also say this. This is also the first opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf. The reason is that when he took someone else's land and took possession, necessarily the owner's possession was removed because it is impossible for two possessions to be on one place at one time. So both descriptions are realized: removal of the usurper's hand and establishment of the usurper's hand, and this is ghasb. So the ruling on immovables becomes like usurping movable property and denial of deposit, in which there is liability by agreement. Also there is a hadith: 'Whoever usurps a span of land, Allah will place a collar of seven layers of heavens around his neck on the Day of Judgment.' (Sahihayn) His saying: 'wa lahum anna al-ghasb...' - the proof of the two shaykhs is that for ghasb, along with actual removal and actual establishment of the hand, a direct act by the usurper upon the substance of the usurped property is also necessary, and this is not conceivable in land. Because the removal of the owner's hand can only be by expelling him from the land, and clearly expelling is an act upon the owner, not upon the usurped property. So this becomes like removing the owner from a herd of livestock; in that case if the herd is destroyed, there is no ghasb. As for the mentioned hadith, it does not indicate the claimed point because in it the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم mentioned the punishment of collar for usurping land. If liability were obligatory, he would have stated it, because liability is among worldly rulings. Also, in the hadith, the word 'ghasb' is used metaphorically for land, just as in the hadith 'man ba'a hurran' the word 'bay' is used for selling a free person, but the ruling of sale is not realized for a free person. Moreover, in the Sahihayn, instead of 'ghasb shibran', it is 'akhadha shibran'.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from 'Kitab al-Ghasb' (Book of Usurpation) discusses a core Hanafi ruling: that the legal category of ghasb (usurpation) only applies to movable property (manqul), not to immovables ('aqar). The author begins by clarifying that ghasb by definition requires the removal of the owner's hand (yad) through physical transfer (naql), which is only possible in movables. The main body of the text presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability (daman) of a usurper of immovable property if it perishes in his hand due to a natural calamity. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf (the relied-upon position), the usurper is not liable. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, holds that he is liable, and this was also the first opinion of Abu Yusuf and the view of Imam al-Shafi'i. The passage then presents the proofs: Muhammad argues that by taking possession, the owner's hand is necessarily removed, establishing both elements of ghasb, analogizing it to movables and to denial of a deposit. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf counter that ghasb requires a direct act upon the property itself (فعل في العين), not merely an act upon the owner, such as expelling him from the land. They compare this to driving the owner away from his livestock, which does not constitute ghasb of the livestock even if it perishes. They also address the hadith about usurping land, interpreting it metaphorically as a threat for the Hereafter, not as establishing worldly liability. The practical consequence (thamarah) of this difference is that if someone occupies a house and it collapses, he does not have to pay its value according to the mufta bihi view of the Shaykhayn.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation: taking another's property by force and asserting ownership, requiring removal of the owner's hand and establishment of one's own hand through an act upon the property.
عقار ('aqar): Immovable property such as land, buildings, trees that cannot be moved without destruction of their nature.
ضمان (daman): Legal liability to compensate for loss or damage, specifically the obligation to pay the value of the usurped property if it perishes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), if someone usurps a house and it collapses due to an earthquake, what is the ruling?
A) The usurper must pay the value of the house.
B) The usurper must return the rubble but not pay unless he caused the collapse.
C) The usurper is not liable for compensation.
D) The usurper must pay half the value.

Key Takeaway
Ghasb in Hanafi law is limited to movables; for immovables, the usurper is not liable if the property perishes naturally, due to the requirement of a direct act upon the property.

intermediate
15 min
Dispute on Whether Ghasb Applies to Immovable Property
Intra-Hanafi dispute with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ghasb in immovable property and explain the ikhtilaf between Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad, including the evidence and the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Ghasb requires transfer of possession; thus it does not apply to land according to Shaykhayn, but Imam Muhammad disagrees — practical consequence: liability for natural calamities.

This lesson explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute: does the law of ghasb (usurpation) apply to immovable property like land and buildings? The answer determines whether someone who wrongfully occupies such property is liable for its destruction by a natural calamity. We will examine the arguments of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad, along with the evidence each side uses.

Guided Path
1
State the Shaykhayn's position
Identify what Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold: ghasb does not occur in immovable property, so no liability for destruction by calamity.
They define ghasb as requiring actual transfer of possession (naql wa tahwil).
2
Identify the opposing view
State Imam Muhammad's position: ghasb does occur in immovable, so liability applies. Note that Imam Zufar and the three other Imams agree.
Imam Abu Yusuf initially held this view but later retracted.
3
Analyze the Shaykhayn's proof
Examine their dalil: ghasb requires removal of the owner's possession (izalah al-yad) and the usurper's disposal (tasarruf) in the object itself. In immovable, only the owner is expelled, not the property transferred.
They compare it to driving away the owner from a herd of cattle.
4
Analyze Imam Muhammad's proof and response
Study his proof: taking possession inevitably removes the owner's possession, and the hadith about a handspan of land uses the word 'ghasb'. Then see the Shaykhayn's response: the hadith is metaphorical and only mentions afterlife punishment, not worldly liability.
The Shaykhayn also reject analogies to movable property and denial of deposit.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if land is destroyed by a flood, Shaykhayn say no compensation; Imam Muhammad says compensation is due. Later fatwa in waqf matters follows Imam Muhammad.
This shows that the operative ruling can shift based on context.

كتاب الغصب
مقصود نہیں ہے کیونکہ نہ تو اس میں کوئی خلاف ہے نہ ہی اشتباہ، خلاف داشتباہ تو غیر منقول میں غصب کے متحقق نہ ہونے میں ہے۔ پر اترکیب مذکور و الغصب فيما ينقل ويحول میں قصر و حصر معتبر ہے جیسا کہ تاج الشریعہ صاحب عنایہ نے بلکہ خود صاحب بدایہ نے بھی اس کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے ۔ " حيث قال لان الغصب بحقيقته يتحقق فيه دون غيره “ اب رہی یہ بات کہ ترکیب میں اداة حصر کیا ہے؟ سو وہ غالبا لام جنس کے ساتھ مسند الیہ کی تعریف ہے کہ یہ مسند پر قصر مسند الیہ کا فائدہ دیتی ہے جس کی تصریح علم معانی میں موجود ہے۔ و شکوہ بخو التوکل علی اللہ، الكرم فی العرب الائمة من قریش ، قول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شیخین کے نز د یک غصب صرف اشیاء منقولہ میں ہوتا ہے کیونکہ غصب در حقیقت اعیان منقولہ ہی میں ہوتا ہے غیر منقولہ میں نہیں ہوتا اس لئے که غصب ازالہ کید کے بغیر نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اور یہ مالک کا ازالہ اسی وقت ہوگا جب منقول کو منتقل کر لیا جائے ۔ حالانکہ عقار میں نقل و تحویل ناممکن ہے۔
قوله اذا غصب عقارا .... الخ - یہ مسئلہ اصل مذکور پر متفرع ہے اس لئے واؤ کے بجائے فاء کے ساتھ فاذا غصب کہنا چاہیے۔ چنانچہ دیگر عام کتب میں اس موقع پر کلمہ کا اور محط میں کلمہ حتی لایا گیا ہے اور تعجب کی بات یہ ہے کہ یہاں مختصر القدوری میں کلمہ فاء ہی تھا مگر صاحب ہدایہ نے بدایہ اور ہدایہ دونوں میں فاء کو واؤ سے بدل دیا۔
بہر کیف مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے عقار وزمین ، درخت، دار عمارت وغیرہ) کو غصب کیا اور اس کے پاس کسی آفت سماویہ سے ہلاک ہوگئی ۔ مثلاً سیلاب کے غلبہ سے زمین ڈوب گئی ۔ یا زلزلہ سے مکان منہدم ہو گیا یا عمارت سیلاب کی زد میں آگئی تو شیخین کے نزدیک اس پر عضمان نہ ہوگا۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک چونکہ غصب کا تحقق غیر منقولہ میں بھی ہوتا ہے اس لئے ان کے یہاں منمان ہوگا۔ امام زفر اور ائمہ ثلاثہ بھی یہی فرماتے ہیں۔ امام ابو یوسف کا بھی پہلا قول یہی ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ جب اس نے دوسرے کی زمین لے کر قبضہ جمالیا تو لا محالہ مالک کا قبضہ زائل ہو گیا کیونکہ بحالت واحدہ ایک محل پر دو قبضوں کا جمع ہونا محال ہے۔ پس دونوں وصف متحقق ہو گئے یعنی ازالہ یہ مققہ اور اثبات ید مبطلہ ، اور یہی غصب ہے تو عقار کا حکم ایسا ہو گیا جیسے مال منقول کو غصب کرنا ودیعت کا انکار کرنا کہ ان میں بالا تفاق ضامن ہوتا ہے نیز حدیث میں ہے کہ "جو شخص کسی کی بالشت بھر زمین غصب کرے گا حق تعالیٰ قیامت کے روز اس کی گردن میں سات طبق نو مین کا طوق ڈالی گا۔ (صحیحین)
قوله ولهما ان الغصب ... الخ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ غصب کے لئے ازالہ یہ محققہ اور اثبات ید مبطلہ کے ساتھ عین مغصوب میں غاصب کا تصرف بھی ضروری ہے اور یہ بات زمین میں غیر متصور ہے۔ کیونکہ ازالہ ید مالک کی صورت یہی ہے کہ اس کو زمین سے نکال دیا جائے اور ظاہر ہے کہ نکالنا صرف تصرف فی المالک ہے نہ کہ تصرف فی المغصوب ۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا۔ جیسے مویشی کے گلہ سے اس کے مالک کو دور ہٹا دے کہ اس صورت میں اگر گلہ تلف ہو جائے تو غصب نہیں ہوتا رہی حدیث مذکور سودہ مدعا پر ولالت نہیں کرتی اس لئے کہ اس میں آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے غصب ارض کی جزاء تطویق بیان کی ہے ۔ اگر ضمان واجب ہوتا تو اس کو بیان فرماتے ۔ کیونکہ ضمان دنیاوی احکام میں سے ہے۔ نیز حدیث میں زمین پر لفظ غصب کا اطلاق مجازا ہے جیسے حدیث من باع حراھ میں بیچ حر کے لئے لفظ بیع بولا گیا والا لزم تحقق البيع فى الحر علاوه ازین صحیحین میں غصب شبرا “ کے بجائے اخذ شبراً " ہے۔۔
قوله وفى المنقول النقل الخ - امام محمد کے قول فصار" کا لمنقول “ کا جواب ہے کہ بر خلاف منقول کے کہ مال منقول کو منتقل کرنا اس مال کے اندر ایک فعل ہے اور یہی غصب ہوتا ہے رہا انکار ودیعت کا مسئلہ سواول تو تسلیم نہیں بلکہ اگر کسی کے پاس عقار کو ودیعت رکھا۔ پھر وہ ودیعت سے منکر ہو گیا تو اصح قول پر بالا تفاق ضامن نہ ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ مبسوط میں مذکور ہے اور اگر ہم مان بھی لیں تب بھی ودیعت کی صورت میں وجوب ضمان اس لیے ہے کہ جس حفاظت کا اس نے التزام کیا تھا وہ چھوڑ دی۔ اور انکار ودیعت میں یہی لازم آتا ہے۔ بزار یہ میں قول شیخین کی تصحیح ہے لیکن بینی ، شرح کنز، من فتاوی ظہیر یہ وغیرہ میں رہے کہ باب وقف میں فتویٰ امام محمد کے قول پر ہے۔
Book of Ghasb. It is not intended because there is neither disagreement nor ambiguity. The disagreement and ambiguity are in that ghasb is not realized in immovable property. The mentioned construction 'al-ghasb fima yunqalu wa yahulu' contains restriction and limitation, as Taj al-Shari'ah and Sahib al-Hidayah indicated. They said: 'Because ghasb in its true reality is realized in that (movable) and not in other.' Now what is the particle of restriction in the construction? It is mostly the definition of the subject (musnad ilayh) with the article 'lam' of genus, which benefits restriction of the subject to the predicate, as detailed in the science of meanings. Wa shukuhu bakhw al-tawakkul 'ala Allah, al-karam fi al-'arab al-a'immah min quraysh. The meaning is that according to the two Shaykhs, ghasb occurs only in movable things because ghasb in reality occurs only in movable entities, not in immovable, because ghasb cannot happen without removal of ownership (izalah al-yad). And removal of ownership of the owner occurs only when the movable is transferred, whereas in real estate transfer is impossible. His statement: 'If he usurps real estate...' This issue is a branch of the original mentioned, so it should have been with 'fa' (if) instead of 'waw' (and). Accordingly, in other general books the word 'kama' and in some places 'hatta' is used. It is surprising that here in Mukhtasar al-Quduri it was with 'fa', but the author of al-Hidayah changed it to 'waw' in both al-Bidayah and al-Hidayah. In any case, the issue is: if someone usurps real estate (land, trees, house, building, etc.) and it perishes by a celestial calamity – e.g., land sinks due to flooding, or house collapses by earthquake, or building is struck by flood – then according to the two Shaykhs, there is no liability. According to Imam Muhammad, since ghasb is realized also in immovable, there is liability. Imam Zufar and the three Imams also say this. Imam Abu Yusuf's first opinion is also this. The reason is that when he took another's land and possessed it, inevitably the owner's possession is removed because it is impossible for two possessions to co-exist on one place at one time. So both descriptions are realized: removal of ownership and establishment of wrongful possession. And this is ghasb. Therefore the ruling for real estate becomes like usurping movable property or denying a deposit, where liability is unanimous. Also, there is a hadith: 'Whoever usurps a handspan of land, Allah will put around his neck seven layers of the earth on the Day of Resurrection.' (Sahihayn) His statement: 'And for both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) indeed ghasb...' The proof of the two Shaykhs is that ghasb requires, along with removal of ownership and establishment of wrongful possession, the usurper's disposal (tasarruf) in the usurped object itself, and this is inconceivable in land. Because removal of the owner's possession is only by expelling him from the land, and expulsion is only disposal in the owner, not disposal in the usurped object. So it is like driving away the owner from a herd of cattle; if the herd perishes, it is not ghasb. As for the mentioned hadith, it does not indicate the claim, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stated the punishment of 'tatweeq' for usurping land. If liability were obligatory, he would have mentioned it, because liability is among worldly rulings. Also, the word 'ghasb' is applied to land metaphorically, like in the hadith 'man ba'a harran' where 'sale' is used for selling a free person, but the sale of a free person is not realized. Moreover, in Sahihayn, instead of 'ghasaba shibran' it is 'akhadha shibran'. His statement: 'And in movable, transfer...' The response to Imam Muhammad's statement 'it became like movable' is that it is unlike movable because transferring movable property is an act within that property, and that is ghasb. As for the issue of denying a deposit, first it is not conceded; rather, if someone deposits real estate and then denies the deposit, he is not liable by agreement according to the sounder opinion, as stated in al-Mabsut. Even if we accept, in the case of deposit, liability is because he abandoned the protection he committed to, and denying the deposit necessitates that. In Bazaziyyah, the opinion of the two Shaykhs is confirmed, but in Bini, Sharh al-Kanz, and Fatawa Zahiriyyah etc., it is stated that in the chapter of waqf, the fatwa is on Imam Muhammad's opinion.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab dispute regarding the definition and scope of ghasb (usurpation) and whether it applies to immovable property ('aqar). The commentary opens by explaining that the definition 'al-ghasb fima yunqalu wa yahulu' (ghasb occurs in what can be moved and transferred) is restrictive, indicating that ghasb is confined to movables. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that ghasb does not apply to immovable property because the essence of ghasb requires removal of the owner's possession, which is only possible by physically transferring the object. Since real estate cannot be moved, the owner's possession is not truly removed; rather, the usurper merely expels the owner from the land, which is a disposal affecting the owner, not the property itself. Therefore, if the land perishes by a natural calamity, there is no liability because ghasb did not occur. Imam Muhammad, Imam Zufar, and the three other Imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) argue that ghasb does occur in immovable property because taking possession inevitably removes the owner's possession, fulfilling the two conditions of ghasb: removal of the owner's hand and establishment of wrongful possession. They also cite the hadith about usurping a handspan of land. The Shaykhayn respond to this hadith by stating that it merely mentions a punishment in the Hereafter, not worldly liability, and the word 'ghasb' is used metaphorically. The passage also addresses Imam Muhammad's analogy to movable property and denial of deposit. It concludes that in the context of waqf, the fatwa is on Imam Muhammad's opinion according to later sources, showing that the operative ruling can shift based on practicality.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation: taking another's property wrongfully and forcefully. The text debates whether it requires actual transfer of possession.
عقار (aqar): Immovable property: land, buildings, trees, etc., that cannot be moved.
منقول (manqul): Movable property: items that can be transferred from place to place.
ازالة يد (izalah al-yad): Removal of possession: one of the two essential components of ghasb.
ضمان (daman): Liability for compensation; in this context, financial responsibility for the usurped property or its damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), why is there no liability (daman) if usurped real estate is destroyed by a natural calamity?
A) Because the usurper did not physically transfer the property, so the essence of ghasb (removal of ownership via transfer) is not fulfilled.
B) Because real estate is not considered property in Islamic law.
C) Because the owner is still responsible for the property.
D) Because the hadith on usurping land explicitly exempts from liability.

Key Takeaway
Whether ghasb applies to immovable property determines liability for destruction by calamity; the Shaykhayn restrict ghasb to movables, while Imam Muhammad includes land, and later fatwa sometimes adopts Imam Muhammad's view for waqf.

Liability for Deficiency Caused by Usurper's Action or Dwelling
Ruling with qiyas proof for liability on usurper's act or dwelling causing deficiency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation for deficiency in usurped immovable property caused by the usurper's action or dwelling, and explain the qiyas reasoning that establishes this liability.

Core Idea
A usurper is liable for any deficiency in immovable property caused by his action or dwelling because it is destruction (atlaaf).

This passage from al-Hidayah deals with a fundamental issue in the law of ghasb: when must a usurper compensate for damage to immovable property? The text clarifies that both direct acts (such as moving soil or demolishing) and indirect causes (like dwelling that leads to collapse) trigger liability. It also introduces a dispute among the Hanafi imams regarding surplus from farming on usurped land.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is causing deficiency to usurped immovable property by action or dwelling. The ruling is that the usurper is liable (daman wajib).
This is the general rule stated at the beginning.
2
Locate the dalil
The text states: 'because it is destruction (atlaaf)'. The proof is a qiyas: just as moving soil (an act upon the substance) incurs liability, so does any act causing destruction.
The asl is moving soil; the far' is any act or dwelling causing deficiency.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is the act of destruction (atlaaf) upon the property. Both moving soil and causing deficiency by dwelling are subsumed under this illa.
The illa is jaliy (obvious) because destruction is directly harmful.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that surplus from farming must be given in charity; Abu Yusuf disagrees. The text promises to detail proofs later.
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement, not a cross-madhhab one.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The passage does not give a tarjih on the charity issue; it only presents the disagreement. Later authorities may resolve it.
For the main liability ruling, there is consensus among Hanafi imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غاصب نے عقار میں اپنے فعل یا سکونت سے کسی چیز کو ناقص کیا تو اس کا ضمان لا زم ہے
قال وما نقص منه بفعله او سكناه ضمنه في قولهم جميعا، لانه اتلاف والعقار يضمن به، كما اذا نقل ترابه لانه فعل فى العين ويدخل فيما قاله اذا انهدمت الدار بسكناه وعمله، فلو غصب دارا وباعها وسلّمها واقر بذلك والمشترى ينكر غصب البائع ولا بينة لصاحب الدار فهو على الاختلاف في الغصب هو الصحيح. قال وان انتقص بالزراعة يغرم النقصان لانه اتلف البعض فيأخذ راس ماله ويتصدق بالفضل قال وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابويوسف لا يتصدق بالفضل وسنذكر الوجه من الجانبين
ترجمہ اور عقار سے جو کچھ اس کے فعل یا سکوت سے ناقص ہو جائے اس کا ضامن ہوگا۔ سب کے قول میں، کیونکہ یہ تلف کرنا ہوا اور اس کی وجہ سے عقار کا ضمان ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے اس کی مٹی منتقل کرے، کیونکہ یہ فعل عین عقار میں ہے۔ اور جو ماتن نے کہا ہے اس میں بھی وہ داخل ہے۔ جب مکان اس کی سکونت یا اس کے عمل سے منہدم ہو گیا ، اگر مکان غصب کر کے فروخت کیا اور سپر د کر دیا پھر اس کے نصب کا اقرار کیا۔ حالانکہ مشتری بائع کے غصب کا منکر ہے اور مالک مکان کے پاس پینہ نہیں ہے تو یہ اس اختلاف پر ہے جو غصب میں ہے، یہی صحیح ہے۔ اگر زمین کاشت سے ناقص ہوگئی تو نقصان کا ضامن ہوگا ، کیونکہ اس نے بعض کو تلف کر دیا، پس وہ اپنا راس المال لے لے اور زائد کو صدقہ کر دے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ زائد کا صدقہ نہ کرے۔ اور ہم جانبین کی دلیل عنقریب بیان کریں گے۔
تشريح .. قوله وما نقص منه ... الخ مغصوب عقار میں سے جو کچھ مناصب نے اپنے فعل سے ناقص کرد یا یا وہ اس کی سکونت سے ناقص ہو گیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ، صاحبین ، امام شافعی کسب کے قول میں ضامن ہوگا۔ امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے قول پر تو وجوب منمان ظاہر ہے، اور یونہی شیخین کے قول پر بھی ، کیونکہ یہ تلف کرنا ہے اور تلف کرنے کی وجہ سے عقار کا ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے اگر عقار کی مٹی کاٹ کر منتقل کرے تو ضامن ہوتا ہے، کیونکہ یہ عین عقار میں اپنا فعل ہے۔
فائدہ نقصان دریافت کرنے کا طریقہ نصیر بن یحیی کے قول کے بموجب یہ ہے کہ دیکھا جائے کہ استعمال سے قبل وہ زمین کتنے میں اجارے پر ملتی تھی۔ اور استعمال کے بعد کتنے میں ملتی ہے، پس جو کچھ تفاوت ہو وہی نقصان ہے۔ اور محمد بن مسلمہ کے قول کے بموجب در یافت نقصان کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ دیکھا جائے کہ وہ زمین پہلے کتنے کوفروخت ہوتی تھی اور اب کتنے کوفروخت ہوتی ہے، ان میں جو فرق
If the usurper causes any deficiency in the real estate by his action or dwelling, he is liable for it.
He said: 'And whatever decreases from it by his action or dwelling, he is liable for it in all of their statements, because it is destruction (atlaaf) and real estate is liable for it, just as if he moves its soil, because it is an act upon the substance (ayn). And it includes what he said: when the house collapses by his dwelling or his work. So if he usurps a house, sells it, delivers it, and confesses to that, while the buyer denies the seller's usurpation and the owner has no evidence, then it is upon the disagreement about usurpation; this is the correct view. He said: And if it decreases by cultivation, he pays the deficiency because he destroyed part of it. So he takes his capital and gives the surplus in charity. He said: This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He does not give the surplus in charity. We will mention the reason from both sides.'
Translation: And whatever decreases from the real estate by his action or dwelling, he is liable for it, in all of their statements, because this is destruction, and due to that, liability for real estate is obligatory. Just as if he moves its soil, because this is an act upon the substance of the real estate. And what the author said is included in this: when the house collapses by his dwelling or his work. If he usurps a house, sells it, and delivers it, then confesses to his usurpation, while the buyer denies the seller's usurpation and the owner has no evidence, then this is upon the disagreement about usurpation; this is the correct view. If the land decreases by cultivation, he is liable for the deficiency because he destroyed part of it. So he takes his capital and gives the surplus in charity. The author of Hidayah says: This is according to both parties. Imam Abu Yusuf says: He does not give the surplus in charity. We will soon mention the proof from both sides.
Explanation... His statement: 'And whatever decreases from it...' Whatever the usurper causes to decrease from the usurped real estate by his action, or it decreases by his dwelling, then according to Abu Hanifa, the two companions, and Imam Shafi'i (in one saying), he is liable. According to Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i (in one saying), the obligation of liability is obvious. And similarly according to the two Shaykhs, because this is destruction, and due to destruction, liability for real estate is obligatory. Just as if he cuts and moves the soil of the real estate, he is liable, because this is his act upon the substance of the real estate.
Benefit: The method of ascertaining the deficiency according to Nasir ibn Yahya is to see how much the land used to rent for before use and after use; the difference is the deficiency. According to Muhammad ibn Muslimah, the method is to see how much the land used to sell for before and now; the difference.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling: if a usurper causes any deficiency in immovable property by his direct action (e.g., demolition) or even by dwelling (e.g., causing wear and tear or collapse), he is liable to compensate for the decrease in value. This ruling is unanimous among the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) because the action constitutes destruction (atlaaf) of part of the property. The text provides an analogy: if the usurper digs and moves soil from the land, he is clearly liable. The same applies if the house collapses due to his dwelling or his work. The passage also discusses a scenario where the usurper sells the house and confesses, but the buyer denies the usurpation; the correct view is that the ruling follows the disagreement about ghasb itself (i.e., whether ghasb occurred). If farming causes the land to become less fertile, the usurper must pay for the deficiency, but if the crops yield a surplus (more than the cost), there is a disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say give the surplus in charity (because it is illicit gain), while Abu Yusuf says he does not have to give charity. The text promises to detail both proofs later. A note provides methods for calculating the deficiency: either by comparing rental value before and after (Nasir ibn Yahya's method) or by comparing sale value (Muhammad ibn Muslimah's method).

Key Terms
نقصان (nuqsan): Deficiency, decrease in value or quality of the property.
اتلاف (atlaaf): Destruction; causing harm to property that reduces its value or utility.
سكنى (sukna): Dwelling; living in the property, which can cause wear and tear or even collapse.
رأس المال (ras al-mal): Capital; here the amount the usurper invested in cultivating the land (e.g., seeds, labor). He may take this back before giving the surplus in charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a usurper moves soil from the land, what is the ruling according to the passage?
A) No liability because soil is part of real estate.
B) Liable because it is an act upon the substance.
C) Liable only if the soil is sold.
D) No liability if the soil is replaced.

Key Takeaway
A usurper is liable for any deficiency in immovable property caused by his action or dwelling, based on the qiyas that destruction of any part of the substance triggers compensation.

intermediate
10 min
Liability for Damage to Usurped Real Property
Ruling on liability with subcases and intra-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for damage to real property by a usurper, identify the disputed subcases (sale and cultivation), and explain the intra-madhhab positions.

Core Idea
A usurper is liable for any damage caused by his act or residence; but surplus profit and the nature of ghasb of real property are disputed.

This lesson examines a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh: the liability of a usurper (ghasib) for damage to real property (aqar). The Hidayah establishes that any reduction caused by the usurper's act or residence must be compensated, drawing an analogy to moving soil. However, the passage also introduces key intra-Hanafi disputes: (1) whether ghasb of real property is established by sale, and (2) whether the usurper must give surplus profit from cultivation to charity. These disputes illustrate the subtlety of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling and its Basis
State the main rule: the usurper is liable for any diminishment caused by his act or residence. Note the proof: it is a form of destruction (itlaf), and real property is liable for destruction, just as moving its soil would be.
The ruling is unanimous among the Hanafi imams and even al-Shafi'i.
2
Apply to the House Collapse Subcase
Apply the general rule to the specific case: if a house collapses due to the usurper's residence or actions (e.g., woodwork), he is liable. Consider the exception: if the collapse is due to a natural calamity, no liability.
This clarifies that the usurper's direct or indirect act is the cause.
3
Analyze the Sale Dispute
When the usurper sells the property and confesses, but the buyer denies and the owner has no evidence, the Sheikhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say the usurper is not liable, while Imam Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i say he is. Understand the basis: the nature of ghasb in real property and the strength of the owner's claim.
Fatwa is given on Imam Muhammad's view in similar matters (e.g., waqf).
4
Evaluate the Cultivation Surplus Dispute
If land is diminished by cultivation, the usurper compensates the loss, takes his capital, and gives surplus to charity according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf says no charity because the surplus is profit not subject to guarantee. Compare the reasoning: purification of unlawful gain vs. no additional liability.
The full reasoning is promised later in the text.
5
Determine Practical Consequences
Recognize the practical difference: under Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, the usurper must donate surplus; under Abu Yusuf, he keeps it. Also, in the sale case, the mufta bihi position (Imam Muhammad) imposes liability on the usurper, protecting the owner.
The mufta bihi is the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Source Text

قوله و ان انتقص بالزراعة ... الخ - اگر مخصو بہ زمین ناصب کی کاشت سے نقصان پذیر ہوئی تو غاصب مالک کیلئے نقصان کا ضامن ہو گا، کیونکہ اس نے اس کے بعض کو تلف کیا ۔ " و العقار يضمن بالاتلاف بلا خلاف ، پس وہ اپنا راس المال لے لے۔ اور زیادتی کو صدقہ کر دے، یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ زیادتی کو صدقہ نہ کرے کیونکہ نہی عنہ تو اس کا نفع ہے جس کا ضمان نہیں دیا ، حالانکہ یہاں وہ ضائن ہو چکا ہے۔ جانبین کی دلیل آئندہ قول و من غصب عبدًا فاستغله فنقصته ان کے ذیل میں آرہی ہے۔
And whatever is diminished from it by his act or his residence, he is liable for it, in the saying of all of them, because it is destruction (itlaf) and real property is liable for destruction, just as if he moves its soil, because it is an action upon the property. And it includes what he said: when the house collapses due to his residence and his work. So if he usurped a house and sold it and handed it over and confessed to that, while the buyer denies the seller's usurpation and the owner has no evidence, then it is based on the disagreement regarding usurpation, and that is the correct view. He said: And if it diminishes due to cultivation, he pays the loss, because he destroyed part of it; so he takes his capital and gives the excess in charity. He said: This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He does not give the excess in charity, and we will mention the reasoning from both sides.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses the liability of a usurper (ghasib) for damage to real property (aqar). The passage type is a ruling with proof and includes subcases. The author first states the general rule: the usurper is liable for any reduction caused by his own act or by his residence. The proof is that this is a form of destruction (itlaf), and real property is subject to liability for destruction by analogy to moving its soil. This ruling is agreed upon by all (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and even al-Shafi'i according to some).

The author then expands to three subcases: (1) if the house collapses due to the usurper's residence or actions (like woodwork or building), he is liable; (2) if he sells the usurped property, hands it over, and confesses to the usurpation while the buyer denies it and the original owner has no evidence, then this falls under the existing disagreement on whether ghasb of real property is established — the Sheikhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that real property cannot be usurped in the full sense, so the seller is not liable, while Imam Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i hold he is liable, provided the owner has no proof; (3) if the land is diminished by cultivation, the usurper must compensate for the loss, and he takes his capital (i.e., the cost of cultivation) but gives any surplus profit to charity according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf says he does not give it to charity because the surplus is not subject to guarantee and he has already compensated for the loss.

The commentary also provides methods for measuring the loss: according to Nasir ibn Yahya, compare the rental value before and after use; according to Muhammad ibn Muslima, compare the sale price before and after. It is reported that Muhammad later reverted to the view of Nasir.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): The wrongful seizure and control over another's property without right, which may be established for movable and (with conditions) immovable property.
عقار (aqar): Immovable property, land and buildings.
ضمان (daman): Liability, guaranty, or compensation for loss or damage.
اتلاف (itlaf): Destruction or causing loss; a key basis for liability in torts.
فضل (fadl): Surplus, excess; in this context, profit from cultivation beyond the cost.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the general ruling in the passage, when is a usurper of real property NOT liable for damage?
A) When the damage is caused by the usurper's act.
B) When the damage is caused by the usurper's residence.
C) When the damage is caused by a natural calamity (like a storm) without the usurper's act or residence.
D) When the damage is caused by cultivation.

Key Takeaway
A usurper is liable for any damage to real property caused by his own act or residence, but the details—especially regarding sale and cultivation surplus—involve important intra-Hanafi disputes rooted in the nature of ghasb and compensation.

Liability for Movable Property Destroyed in Usurper's Hands
Ruling on liability for movable property in usurper's possession with rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for movable property destroyed in a usurper's hands and explain why the value is assessed at the time of usurpation.

Core Idea
The usurper is liable for destruction and diminution because the property enters his guarantee at the moment of seizure.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a core principle of ghasb: once the usurper takes possession, he becomes responsible for the property's full value. Even if the property perishes without his act, he must compensate. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the concept of daman al-ghasb and its differentiation from contractual guarantees.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine the act (movable property perishes in usurper's hand) and the ruling: the usurper is liable (daman).
The ruling applies whether the perishing is by his act or without his act.
2
Understand the Basis of Liability
The property entered the usurper's guarantee (daman) at the moment of seizure (qabd). This is the cause of liability.
Liability is fixed at the time of usurpation, not at destruction.
3
Distinguish Destruction from Diminution
If property is destroyed, usurper pays full value on the day of usurpation. If it diminishes but still exists, he pays the decrease.
The decrease must be due to loss of substance, not market price fluctuation.
4
Note Exceptions
Market price fluctuations (due to demand) are not compensated. For ribawi items, the usurper cannot combine return of the item with payment for damage (leads to riba).
This ensures the ruling aligns with broader Sharia principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منقولی چیز غاصب کے قبضے میں اس کے فعل یا بغیر فعل کے ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس کا ضمان لازم ہے
قال و اذا هلک النقلى فى يد الغاصب بفعله او بغير فعله ضمنه، وفي اكثر نسخ المختصر واذا هلک الغصب والمنقول هو المراد لما سبق ان الغصب فيما ينقل وهذا لان العين دخل في ضمانه بالغصب السابق اذهو السبب وعند العجز عن رده تجب رد القيمة او يتقرر بذلك السبب، ولهذا تعتبر قيمته يوم الغصب وان نقص فى يده ضمن النقصان لانه دخل جميع اجزائه في ضمانه بالغصب فما تعذر رد عينه يجب رد قيمته بخلاف تراجع السعر اذا رُدَّ فى مكان الغصب لانه عبارة عن فتور الرغبات دون قوت الجزء وبخلاف المبيع، لانه ضمان عقد اما الغصب فقبض والاوصاف تضمن بالفعل لا بالعقد على ما عرف، قال ومراده اده غير الربوى اما في الربويات لا يمكنه تضمين النقصان مع استرداد الاصل لانه يؤدى الى الربوا
ترجمہ جب ہلاک ہو گئی منقول چیز غاصب کے قبضے میں اس کے فعل سے یا اس کے فعل کے بغیر تو اس کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اکثر نسخوں
He said: And if the movable property perishes in the hand of the usurper, whether by his act or without his act, he is liable for it. In most copies of al-Mukhtasar: 'And if the usurped property perishes' and the intended meaning is movable property, because it was previously established that usurpation applies only to what is transportable. This is because the property has come into his guarantee (daman) by the prior usurpation, as that is the cause, and when unable to return it, the value must be returned or it is established by that cause. Hence its value is considered on the day of usurpation, and if it diminishes in his hand, he is liable for the diminution because all its parts have entered into his guarantee by the usurpation. Therefore, if returning the property itself is impossible, its value must be returned, contrary to the decrease in price if it is returned at the place of usurpation, because that is due to lack of demand rather than a loss of substance. And contrary to a sold item, because that is a contractual guarantee. As for usurpation, it is seizure (qabd), and attributes are guaranteed by act, not by contract, as is known. He said: His intended meaning is other than ribawi items. As for ribawi items, he cannot guarantee the diminution while retaining the principal, because that leads to riba.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya addresses the liability for movable property (manqul) that perishes in the hands of the usurper. The passage type is a ruling with proof using rational argument (talil) and analogy. The core ruling: whether the movable perishes by the usurper's direct act (e.g., breaking) or without his act (e.g., fire), he is liable because the property entered his guarantee (daman) at the moment of usurpation. The author explains that the value is assessed on the day of usurpation, not the day of destruction, because the liability crystallizes at that point. If the property decreases in value while in his hands (but still exists), he is liable for the decrease because all parts of the property are under his guarantee. When returning the property is impossible, he must pay its value. This differs from a price decrease due to market fluctuations (which is not compensated) because that is a loss of utility, not substance. It also differs from the guarantee in a sale contract, which is a contractual guarantee; ghasb is a guarantee by seizure (qabd). The author notes that this applies to non-ribawi items; for ribawi items (like gold, silver, food), the usurper cannot compensate for the loss while keeping the principal because that would involve riba (usury) by exchanging unequal quantities of the same genus.

Key Terms
منقول (manqul): Movable property that can be physically transported; the primary subject of ghasb.
ضمان (daman): Liability for compensation; the usurper is responsible for the value of the property and its attributes.
قبض (qabd): Physical seizure or possession; the basis of guarantee in ghasb.
ربويات (ribawiyyat): Riba-conducive items (e.g., gold, silver, wheat, barley, salt, dates) that are subject to riba rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On what day is the value of the usurped movable property assessed for compensation?
A) The day it was usurped.
B) The day it was destroyed.
C) The day of the court judgment.
D) The day the owner demands it back.

Key Takeaway
The usurper's liability for movable property is fixed at the moment of seizure; he is responsible for destruction and diminution, subject to exceptions for market fluctuations and ribawi items.

Liability for House Collapse Due to Usurper's Occupancy
Explains an additional case in Quduri's text on ghash

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on liability when a usurped house collapses and identify the condition that triggers liability.

Core Idea
A usurper is liable for house collapse only if caused by his own occupancy or work; natural calamity exempts.

In the chapter on ghash (usurpation), classical Hanafi texts discuss various scenarios of damage. This passage expands on Quduri's statement about 'what is lessened' to include a specific case: when a usurped house collapses due to the usurper's stay or work. Understanding the condition that triggers liability is crucial for distinguishing between cases where compensation is owed versus when it is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling from Quduri
Quduri's original text states that the usurper must compensate for 'what is lessened' from the usurped property. This is a general obligation to restore or pay damages.
2
Note the additional case by the commentator
The commentator (author of Hidayah) explains that this includes a house that collapses due to the usurper's occupancy (suknat) or his work (such as splitting or shortening). In such a case, the usurper is liable (madhmun).
The qualification 'by his stay and his work' is a restriction from the base text.
3
Understand the condition for liability
The key condition is that the destruction must be directly caused by the usurper's actions or presence. Merely being in possession is not enough; there must be a causal link.
4
Recognize the exception
If the house collapses due to a natural calamity (heavenly disaster) without any act of the usurper, he is not liable. This distinguishes between man-made and natural causes.
The word 'معضمان' (uncertain) may mean 'even with a guarantor', but the core is clear: no liability for natural causes.
5
Derive the practical consequence
In fatwa practice, the mufti must determine the cause of the collapse. If evidence shows the usurper's occupancy or work caused it, compensation is due; otherwise, not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ويدخل فيما قاله الخ - صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام قدوری کے قول وما نقص منہ میں یہ صورت بھی داخلہ ہے کہ مکان غاصب کی سکونت یا اس کے عمل ( حداوت و قصارت) سے منہدم ہو گیا تو وہ اس پر مضمون ہوگا۔ بسكناه و عملہ " کی قید اس لئے لگائی ہے کہ اگر مکان اس کی سکونت یا اس کے عمل کے بغیر کسی آفت سماویہ کی وجہ سے منہدم ہوا تو شیخ کے نزد یک معضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
He said: 'and enters into what he said...' – The author of Hidayah says that in Imam Quduri's statement 'What is lessened from it' this case is also included: that a house collapses due to the usurper's stay or his work (splitting and shortening), then he is liable for it. The qualification 'by his stay and his work' is made so that if the house collapses due to a heavenly calamity without his stay or work, then according to the Shaykh [Abu Hanifa?] it is not obligatory even if there is a guarantor?
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on Quduri's text. The commentator explains that when Quduri says 'what is lessened from it' (in the context of ghash), it includes a case where a usurped house collapses due to the usurper's own occupancy (suknat) or his actions (such as splitting or shortening the structure). In such a case, the usurper is liable (madhmun) for the loss. The phrase 'by his stay and his work' is a restriction: if the house collapses due to a natural calamity (like an earthquake) without any act of the usurper, then according to the Shaykh (likely Abu Hanifa), liability does not arise. The word 'معضمان' is uncertain in meaning; it may indicate that even if there is a guarantor, the usurper is not liable. This shows that the cause of liability is the usurper's direct contribution to the destruction.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Wrongful taking and seizure of another's property without legal right.
مضمون (madhmun): Liable or responsible for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for a usurper to be liable when a usurped house is destroyed?
A) The destruction must be by a natural calamity
B) The destruction must be caused by the usurper's own occupancy or work
C) The house must be returned before destruction
D) The owner must have evidence

Key Takeaway
A usurper is liable for property damage only if the damage is directly caused by his occupancy or his actions; natural calamities do not trigger liability.

Selling a Usurped House: Liability Dispute
Presents a dispute on liability when a usurped house is sold and the buyer denies the ghash.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether ghash applies to real estate and derive the ruling for a seller who confessed to usurping a house when the buyer denies and the owner has no evidence.

Core Idea
Ghash does not apply to real estate according to the two shaykhs — a seller of a usurped house is not liable in a dispute when the buyer denies and the owner lacks proof.

In this passage, the author of Al-Hidayah expands on a scenario from Al-Quduri regarding a usurper who sells a house. The dispute centers on whether the concept of ghash (usurpation) applies to immovable property. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial because it determines liability in a complex legal situation involving a seller, buyer, and original owner. This lesson dissects the opinions of the Hanafi masters and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes a usurper (ghasib) who usurps a house, sells it, and delivers it to the buyer. Later, the seller confesses to the ghash, but the buyer denies the seller committed ghash. The original owner has no evidence (bayyinah) that the house is his. Determine the ruling on the seller's liability.
2
State the ikhtilaf
The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that ghash does not apply to real estate (aqar), so the seller is not liable. Imam Muhammad, Zufar, and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that ghash applies to all property, so the seller is liable.
3
Analyze the condition
The dispute only arises when the owner has no evidence. If the owner has evidence, all agree the seller is not liable because the sale is valid.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, the ruling depends on which opinion a judge follows. Under Shaykhayn, the seller walks free; under the opposing view, he must compensate the owner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله فلو غصب دارا .. الخ ۔ یہ مسلہ مسائل اصل یعنی مبسوط میں سے ہے جس کو صاحب ہدایہ نے مسئلہ قدوری پر تفریح کے طریق سے ذکر کیا ہے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ غاصب نے ایک مکان غصب کر کے فروخت کیا اور مشتری کے سپرد کر دیا ، پھر اسکے غصب کا اقرار کیا جبکہ مشترکی اس امر سے منکر ہے کہ بائع نے غصب کیا ہے اور مالک مکان کے پاس اس پر مبینہ موجود نہیں کہ یہ میری ملک ہے تو اس میں بھی وہی اختلاف ہے جو غصب میں ہے، یعنی شیخین کے نزدیک عقار میں غصب نہیں ہوتا تو بائع ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ اور امام محمد و زفر اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ضامن ہو گا مگر اختلاف اسی وقت ہے جب مالک کے پاس بینہ نہ ہو ورنہ بالا تفاق مائع پر ضمان نہ ہوگا۔
He said: 'If he usurped a house...' – This issue is from the original Masail, i.e., the Mabsut, which the author of Hidayah mentioned by way of elaboration on Quduri's issue. The issue is: a usurper usurps a house, sells it, and hands it over to the buyer. Then he confesses to the ghash while the buyer denies that the seller committed ghash, and the owner has no evidence that the house is his. In this case, the same difference of opinion exists as in ghash: according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), there is no ghash in real estate (immovables), so the seller is not liable. According to Imam Muhammad, Zufar, and Imam al-Shafi'i, he is liable. But the difference is only when the owner has no evidence; otherwise, by agreement, there is no liability on the seller.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed scenario and the resulting ikhtilaf. The scenario: a person usurps a house (ghash in real estate, which is contested), then sells it to a buyer. Later, the usurper confesses to the ghash, but the buyer denies that the seller committed ghash. The original owner has no proof of ownership. The ruling here depends on the madhhab position on ghash in real estate. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that real estate cannot be usurped (ghash), so the seller is not liable for return of the house or damages. Imam Muhammad, Zufar, and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that ghash applies to real estate as well, so the seller is liable. However, this dispute only applies when the owner has no evidence (bayyinah). If the owner has evidence, all agree the seller is not liable because the sale was valid. This is a practical difference: in a Hanafi court following the Shaykhayn, a seller of a house would not be liable for ghash even if he admitted to usurping it, whereas in a court following Imam Muhammad or Shafi'i, he would be liable.

Key Terms
شیخین (Shaykhayn): The two shaykhs: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
عقار (aqar): Immovable property, real estate such as land and buildings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the ruling for a seller who usurped a house, sold it, and confessed to ghash?
A) The seller is liable because ghash applies to real estate
B) The seller is not liable because ghash does not apply to real estate
C) The seller is liable only if the buyer knew
D) The seller must return the sale price

Key Takeaway
In a dispute where a usurped house is sold and the buyer denies knowledge, the Shaykhayn hold the seller is not liable because ghash does not apply to real estate, differing from Muhammad and Shafi'i who deem it applicable to all property.

The Usurper's Excess Profit: Charity or Keep?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on charity for excess profit from usurped land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the excess profit from usurped cultivation, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a similar scenario.

Core Idea
Excess profit from usurped land: Abu Hanifa requires charity; Abu Yusuf allows keeping it.

When a usurper cultivates land and it yields profit beyond his expenses, a question arises: must he give that excess in charity, or may he keep it? This passage from al-Hidayah records an intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Imam Abu Yusuf. Understanding the reasoning behind each position sharpens your ability to analyze disputes within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
The core question: after the usurper recovers his expenses (ras al-mal), what must he do with the excess (ziyada)? One view says give charity; another says keep it.
Both sides agree on liability for damage; the dispute is only about the excess.
2
State each position with its authority
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: give the excess in charity. Abu Yusuf: do not give charity; the usurper keeps it.
These are all Hanafi imams; it's an internal dispute.
3
Trace the reasoning of each side
The majority: the excess is unlawful profit (since the land was usurped), so it must be cleansed by charity. Abu Yusuf: the profit was not guaranteed (daman) beforehand, and the usurper is already liable for the damage, so no charity needed.
The text defers full evidence to a later passage.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: under the majority, the usurper must give away the profit; under Abu Yusuf, he may keep it, despite liability for damage.
This affects the final outcome for the usurper's net gain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و ان انتقص بالزراعة ... الخ - اگر مخصو بہ زمین ناصب کی کاشت سے نقصان پذیر ہوئی تو غاصب مالک کیلئے نقصان کا ضامن ہو گا، کیونکہ اس نے اس کے بعض کو تلف کیا ۔ " و العقار يضمن بالاتلاف بلا خلاف ، پس وہ اپنا راس المال لے لے۔ اور زیادتی کو صدقہ کر دے، یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ زیادتی کو صدقہ نہ کرے کیونکہ نہی عنہ تو اس کا نفع ہے جس کا ضمان نہیں دیا ، حالانکہ یہاں وہ ضائن ہو چکا ہے۔ جانبین کی دلیل آئندہ قول و من غصب عبدًا فاستغله فنقصته ان کے ذیل میں آرہی ہے۔
He said: 'And if it is diminished by cultivation...' – If the usurped land is damaged by the usurper's cultivation, he is liable to the owner for the loss, because he destroyed a part of it. 'And real estate is guaranteed by destruction without dispute.' So he takes his capital (expenses) and gives the excess in charity. This is according to the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Imam Abu Yusuf says: He should not give the excess in charity, because he is prohibited from it – that excess is a profit for which no liability was incurred, whereas here he has already become liable. The evidence of the two sides will come under the upcoming statement 'He who usurps a slave and uses him and he is diminished'.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: a usurper cultivates the usurped land, causing damage (e.g., soil depletion). The ruling: the usurper must compensate the owner for the loss because destruction (itlaf) makes real estate liable without dispute. Then, the usurper recovers his expenses (ras al-mal) from the produce, but the excess (ziyada) – the profit beyond expenses – he must give in charity. This is the position of the 'two sides' (likely Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad). Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees: he argues that the excess should not be given in charity because the usurper is prohibited from retaining it; it is a profit for which he gave no guarantee (daman). However, in this case, the usurper has already become liable for the damage, so the reasoning for charity fails. The text postpones the full evidence for both views to a later passage about a usurped slave. This shows the nuanced approach: while the majority holds charity to cleanse the unlawful profit, Abu Yusuf sees it as unnecessary since the liability for damage already applies.

Key Terms
راس المال (ras al-mal): Capital or expenses incurred in cultivation.
زیادتی (ziyada): Excess profit beyond the capital expenses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the excess is small
B) Because the excess is profit for which no guarantee was given, and the usurper is already liable for damage
C) Because charity is not recommended in such cases
D) Because the owner should receive the excess

Key Takeaway
Intra-Hanafi disputes like this illustrate how different premises about guarantee (daman) lead to different rulings on purification of unlawful profit.

Liability for Movable Property in Usurpation
States and proves the general ruling on usurper's liability for movable property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a usurper's liability for destroyed movable property, explain the distinction between price decline and physical deficiency, and apply the exception for ribawi goods.

Core Idea
Usurper is liable for all movable property destroyed in his hands; price drop is not compensated but physical deficiency is.

When someone wrongfully takes another's movable property (ghash), the property enters his guarantee. If it is destroyed—whether by his act or not—he must compensate its value. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this rule, its limits, and the critical exception for ribawi goods to prevent riba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The passage first states the rule: movable property destroyed in the usurper's hand makes him liable. Note that destruction includes both his act and events beyond his control.
The liability is strict: no need to prove fault.
2
Trace the proof (dalil)
The reasoning is qiyas: the property entered his liability by the prior act of usurpation. Therefore any loss falls on him. Value is assessed at the day of usurpation.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on causation.
3
Distinguish price decline from physical deficiency
If the market price drops while the item is returned, no compensation is due because it's not a loss of a physical part. But if the item is damaged (naqs), the usurper must compensate the deficiency.
Price drop = slackening of demand; deficiency = loss of part.
4
Contrast with contract-based liability (sale)
In sale, liability is contractual; in ghash, it is possessory. Attributes are guaranteed by act, not contract.
This distinction clarifies why different rules apply.
5
Apply the ribawi exception
For ribawi goods (e.g., gold, wheat), you cannot take compensation for deficiency while returning the original, because that would be riba.
Preserves the prohibition of usury even in compensation claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و اذا هلک النقلى فى يد الغاصب بفعله او بغير فعله ضمنه، وفي اكثر نسخ المختصر واذا هلک الغصب والمنقول هو المراد لما سبق ان الغصب فيما ينقل وهذا لان العين دخل في ضمانه بالغصب السابق اذهو السبب وعند العجز عن رده تجب رد القيمة او يتقرر بذلك السبب، ولهذا تعتبر قيمته يوم الغصب وان نقص فى يده ضمن النقصان لانه دخل جميع اجزائه في ضمانه بالغصب فما تعذر رد عينه يجب رد قيمته بخلاف تراجع السعر اذا رُدَّ فى مكان الغصب لانه عبارة عن فتور الرغبات دون قوت الجزء وبخلاف المبيع، لانه ضمان عقد اما الغصب فقبض والاوصاف تضمن بالفعل لا بالعقد على ما عرف، قال ومراده اده غير الربوى اما في الربويات لا يمكنه تضمين النقصان مع استرداد الاصل لانه يؤدى الى الربوا
ترجمہ جب ہلاک ہو گئی منقول چیز غاصب کے قبضے میں اس کے فعل سے یا اس کے فعل کے بغیر تو اس کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اکثر نسخوں میں اذا ملک الغصب ہے اور مراد وہی منقول ہے کیونکہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ غصب منقول ہی میں ہوتا ہے ، اور یہ اس لئے ہے کہ مال عین اس کے ضمان میں داخل ہو گیا۔ غصب سابقہ کی وجہ سے کیونکہ غصب ہی سبب ہے اور اس کی واپسی سے عاجزی کے وقت قیمت کی واپسی ، اجب ہوئی یا قیمت مقرر ہو گئی اس سبب کی وجہ اس لئے معتبر ہوتی ہے اس کی قیمت غصب کے دن کی اور اگر ناقص ہو گئی اس کے قبضہ میں تو نقصان کا ضامن ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ اس کے جملہ اجزاء اس کے ضمان میں داخل ہو چکے غصب کی وجہ سے پس جو ببینہ واپس کرنا حعذر ہو اس کی قیمت واپس کرنا واجب ہوگا بخلاف بھاؤ گھٹ جانے کے جب کہ واپس کیا غصب ہی کی جگہ میں کیونکہ بھاؤ گھٹنا رغبتوں کے ست ہونے سے عبارت ہے نہ کہ جزء کے فوت ہونے سے اور بخلاف صبیح کے مکیونکہ وہ جنمان عقد ہے ۔ بہر حال غصب سوضمان قبض ہے ۔ اور اوصاف کی ضمانت فعل کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے نہ کہ عقد کی وجہ سے جیسا کہ معلوم ہو چکا صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مراد غیر بیاجی مال ہے۔ رہے بیاج والے مال سواصل واپس کرنے کے ساتھ نقصان کا ضامن بنا نا ممکن نہیں کیونکہ یہ بیاج کی طرف پہنچا دے گا۔ تشریح... قوله واذا هل ...... الخ - اگر غاصب کے قبضہ میں اس کے فعل سے یا اس کے فعل کے بغیر مال منقول تلف ہو گیا تو وہ قبضہ اس کا ضامن ہو گا صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اکثر نسخوں میں ”النقلی“ کے بجائے الغصب “ ہے۔ اور مراد وہی مال منقول ہے کیونکہ یہ بات پہلے معلوم ہو چکی کہ غصب کا تحقق ایسے ہی مال مین ہوتا ہے جو منقول ہو ۔ ضامن ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ غصب سابق کے ذریعہ سے وہ مال اس کی ضمانت میں داخل ہو گیا اس لیے کہ غصب ہی اسی کا سبب ہے اور جب اس کی واپسی سے عاجز ہو گیا تو اس کی قیمت کی واپسی واجب ہوئی یا جو لوگ یہ کہتے ہیں کہ قیمت واپس کرنا ہی اصل ہے تو اس سبب کی وجہ سے قیمت مقرر ہوگئی اور اسی وجہ سے غصب سابق ہی اس کا سبب ہوتا ہے وہ قیمت معتبر ہوتی ہے جو غصب کے روز تھی۔
He said: And if the movable property is destroyed in the hand of the usurper, by his act or without his act, he is liable for it. In most copies of al-Mukhtasar it says 'if the usurped property is destroyed' and movable property is intended, based on what preceded that ghash is only in movables. This is because the property entered into his liability by the prior ghash, for it is the cause, and when unable to return it, returning its value becomes obligatory, or the value is established by that cause. Therefore its value is considered as of the day of ghash. And if it becomes deficient in his hand, he is liable for the deficiency, because all its parts entered into his liability by ghash. So what is difficult to return in kind, its value must be returned. This is unlike the decline in price if it is returned at the place of ghash, because it is a slackening of desires, not the loss of a part. And unlike the sold item, because it is a contractual liability. As for ghash, it is a possessory liability. And attributes are guaranteed by act, not by contract, as has been known. He said: And his intention is non-ribawi property. As for ribawi property, it is not possible to impose liability for deficiency along with returning the original, because that leads to riba. Translation: When the movable property is destroyed in the hand of the usurper, by his act or without his act, he is liable. In most copies it says 'if the usurped property is destroyed' and the intended meaning is the same movable, because it has passed before that ghash only occurs in movables. And this is because the property entered into his liability due to the prior ghash, as the ghash is the cause. And when he is unable to return it, returning its value is obligatory, or the value is established by that cause. Therefore its value is considered as of the day of ghash. And if it becomes deficient in his hand, he is liable for the deficiency, because all its parts entered into his liability by ghash. So whatever cannot be returned in kind, its value must be returned. This is unlike the decline in price if it is returned at the place of ghash, because the decline in price is a slackening of desires, not the loss of a part. And unlike the sold item, because it is a contractual liability. In any case, ghash is possessory liability. And attributes are guaranteed by act, not by contract, as has been known. The author of Hidayah says that his intention is non-ribawi property. As for ribawi property, it is not possible to impose liability for deficiency along with returning the original, because that leads to riba. Elaboration: He said: 'And if it is destroyed...' etc. - If movable property in the hand of the usurper is destroyed, by his act or without his act, then that possession makes him liable. The author of Hidayah says that in most copies, instead of 'al-naqli' it is 'al-ghash', and the intended meaning is movable property, because it has been established earlier that ghash only occurs in movable property. The reason for liability is that the property entered into his guarantee by the prior ghash, because ghash is the cause. And when he becomes unable to return it, returning its value becomes obligatory. Or for those who say that returning the value is the original, then by that cause the value is determined, and for this reason the value which was on the day of ghash is considered.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a complete ruling with proof. It establishes the general principle: any movable property (manqul) that comes into the usurper's possession is guaranteed (daman) if it is destroyed, whether the usurper caused the destruction or not. The proof given is that the property entered the usurper's liability (daman) from the moment of usurpation, because usurpation itself is the cause (sabab) of liability. If return of the actual item is impossible, the value must be paid, and the value is assessed as of the day of usurpation. If the property suffers a deficiency (naqs) while in his possession, he must compensate for that deficiency, because all parts of the property are under his guarantee. However, this is distinguished from a mere decline in market price (taraju al-sa'r) when the property is returned at the original place; price fluctuation is not a loss of a physical part, so no compensation is required. The ruling also differs from the case of a sold item (mabi') where liability is contractual; in ghash, liability is possessory (qabd). Attributes (awsaf) are guaranteed by actual act (fi'l), not by contract. Importantly, the text specifies that this ruling applies to non-ribawi (interest-based) items only. For ribawi goods, one cannot take compensation for deficiency while returning the original, because that would lead to riba (since ribawi goods must be exchanged in equal measure). This is a critical limitation preserving usury rules.

Key Terms
منقول (manqul): Movable property that can be physically transferred.
ضمان قبض (daman al-qabd): Liability arising from possession, as opposed to contractual liability.
ربوی (ribawi): Relating to goods subject to riba (interest), such as gold, silver, wheat, barley, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between a decline in market price (taraju al-sa'r) and a physical deficiency (naqs) in the context of ghash?
A) There is no difference; both require compensation
B) Physical deficiency requires compensation; price decline does not, because it is not loss of a part
C) Price decline requires compensation if it is substantial
D) Both require compensation only if the usurper acted

Key Takeaway
Usurper is strictly liable for movable property destroyed in his possession; price fluctuation is not compensated, and ribawi goods have a special prohibition against combining return of original with deficiency compensation.
