Wages of a Usurped Slave: Charity or Ownership?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ghalla of usurped slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on wages from a usurped slave and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding charity.

Core Idea
Wages from a usurped slave must be given in charity according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf disagrees due to retrospective ownership.

This passage addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the wages (ghalla) earned by a usurper who hires out a usurped slave. While all agree compensation for depreciation is due, the key question is whether the usurper must give the wages in charity or may keep them. The dispute hinges on the nature of ownership acquired through liability (daman) versus the foulness (khabath) of unauthorized use.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the usurper must give the wages in charity. This is the ruling in the base text (matn).
The wages are considered acquired through a foul cause (sabab khabith).
2
Identify the opponent and his view
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the usurper does not give the wages in charity; rather, they become his own property because the slave entered his daman (liability) and he owns it retrospectively upon paying compensation.
The dispute also applies to the borrower (musta'ir) who rents out a borrowed item.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the slave entered the usurper's liability at the moment of usurpation, and since guaranteed things are owned by paying the value, the wages are produce of what is guaranteed and thus become the usurper's property.
Retrospective ownership (mulk mustanid) is key.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The two imams respond that the retrospective ownership is defective (naqis) and does not remove the foulness of the original acquisition. Since the wages were earned through unauthorized use, they must be purified by charity.
The branch (wages) takes the description of the root (foul cause).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Yusuf's view, the usurper may keep the wages; under the two, charity is mandatory. However, both agree that if the slave perishes, the wages may be used to pay compensation to the owner.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن غصب عبدا فاستغله فنقصته الغلة فعليه النقصان لما بينا ويتصدق بالغلة قال وهذا عندهما ايضا وعنده لا يتصدق بالغلة وعلى هذا الخلاف اذا أجر المستعير المستعار لابي يوسف انه حصل في ضمانه وملكه اما الضمان ،فظاهر، وكذلک الملک فی المضمون لان المضمونات تملک باداء الضمان مستندا الى وقت الغصب عندنا، ولهما انه حصل بسبب خبيث وهو التصرف فى ملك الغير، وما هذا حاله فسبيله التصدق اذ الفرع يحصل على وصف الاصل والملك المستند ناقص فلا ينعدم به الخبث فلو هلک العبد في يد الغاصب حتى ضمنه له ان يستعين بالغلة فى اداء الضمان لان الخبث لاجل المالك، ولهذا لو ادى اليه يباح له التناول فيزول الخبث بالاداء اليه بخلاف ما اذا باعه فهلك فى يد المشترى ثم استحق وغرمه ليس له ان يستعين بالغلة فى اداء الثمن اليه لان الخبث ما كان لحق المشترى الا اذا كان لا يجد غيره لانه محتاج اليه فله ان يصرفه الى حاجة نفسه، فلو اصاب ما لا يتصدق بمثله ان كان غنيا وقت الاستعمال وان كان فقيرا فلا شيء عليه لما ذكرنا
He said: Whoever usurps a slave and employs him (for hire), and the employment causes a decrease in him, then upon him is the compensation for the decrease as we have explained, and he gives the wages in charity. He said: And this (giving in charity) is according to both of them as well, and according to him he does not give the wages in charity. And upon this difference is the case when the borrower (musta'ir) rents out the borrowed item. For Abu Yusuf: it has entered his liability and ownership. As for liability, it is apparent, and likewise ownership in what is guaranteed, because guaranteed things become owned by payment of liability, traced back to the time of ghasb according to us. And for the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): it was acquired through a foul cause, namely acting in another's property. And something in this state should be given in charity because the branch takes on the description of the root, and the delayed ownership is defective, so foulness is not removed by it. If the slave perishes in the hands of the usurper such that he becomes liable, he may use the wages to pay the liability because the foulness was due to the owner. For this reason, if he pays it to him, it becomes permissible for him to take it, so foulness is removed by payment. Contrary to if he sold it and it perished in the hands of the buyer, then it was found to be owned by someone else, and he (the buyer) paid compensation; the seller cannot use the wages to pay the price to the buyer because the foulness was not due to the buyer's right, unless he finds no other means because he needs it, then he may spend it on his own need. If he has property (i.e., is wealthy), he gives in charity an amount equivalent to it; if he was poor at the time of use, then nothing is upon him, as we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wages (ghalla) earned by a usurped slave who was hired out by the usurper and suffered depreciation. The base ruling (from the matn) is that the usurper must compensate for the decrease (nuqsan) and give the wages in charity (yatassadaq bi al-ghalla). The commentator notes that this ruling is according to both Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani). However, Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the usurper does not give the wages in charity; rather, the wages become his own property because the slave entered his daman (liability) and he may own the fruits of what is under liability. The dispute is also applied to the case of a borrower (musta'ir) who rents out the borrowed item. Abu Yusuf's reasoning: the slave entered the usurper's liability (daman) from the moment of ghasb, and by paying compensation later, he effectively owns the slave and its produce retrospectively. Since the wages are part of the slave's produce, they are owned by the usurper. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that the wages were acquired through a foul cause (sabab khabith) – unauthorized use of another's property. Anything acquired through such a cause must be given in charity. The defective ownership that arises by retrospective liability does not remove the foulness. However, if the slave is destroyed, the usurper may use the wages to pay the compensation to the owner because the foulness was connected to the owner's right; once paid, the foulness is removed. In contrast, if the usurper sold the slave and the buyer paid compensation after the slave was found to be owned by someone else, the usurper (as seller) cannot use the wages to reimburse the buyer because the foulness is not related to the buyer's right. But if the usurper has no other means, he may use them out of necessity. Additionally, if the usurper was wealthy at the time of the usufruct, he must give an equivalent amount in charity; if poor, nothing is required.

Key Terms
غلة (ghalla): The wages or income earned by hiring out the usurped slave.
خبث (khabath): Foulness or ill-gotten nature; the quality of property acquired through unauthorized means.
ملك مستند (mulk mustanid): Retrospective ownership acquired by paying compensation traced back to the time of ghasb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, what must a usurper do with the wages earned by hiring out a usurped slave (assuming the slave is returned with depreciation)?
A) Keep the wages as compensation for his trouble.
B) Give the wages in charity.
C) Return the wages to the owner of the slave.
D) Use the wages to pay for any decrease in the slave's value.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) requires wages from a usurped slave to be given in charity due to foul acquisition, while Abu Yusuf allows them based on retrospective ownership.

The Dispute on Charity from Usurped Property: Ghallah and Khabath
Explains the ruling on ghallah and the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on giving ghallah in charity and explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa versus the two companions.

Core Idea
Profit from usurped property is tainted (khabīth) and must be purified by charity—except according to Abu Hanifa.

In Kitab al-Ghasb, al-Hidayah presents a clear ruling: the usurper gives the profit from the slave in charity. But then it discloses an internal disagreement—Abu Hanifa disagreed. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind each position and clarifies the applied ruling (muftā bihi).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position from the matn
Identify the ruling as stated in the matn: the usurper gives the ghallah in charity. Note that this is attributed to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that Abu Hanifa holds a different view: no charity required. This difference is the core of the passage.
3
Follow Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the profit belongs to the usurper because he is liable (damān) for the slave. Ownership is established by paying compensation traced back to the time of usurpation, so the profit is lawful.
4
Analyze the two companions' proof
The two companions argue that the profit is acquired through a bad cause (sabab khabīth) – unlawful use of another's property. Even if ownership is established, it is deficient and does not remove the taint; hence charity is required.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the applied position
The practical difference: according to the two companions, the usurper must give the profit in charity; according to Abu Hanifa, he may keep it. The relied-upon (muftā bihi) position is that of the two companions, as stated in the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الغصب
۳۴۰
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲
غاصب نے غلام غصب کر کے مزدوری پر لگایا جس پر اس کا نقصان ہوا تو غاصب پر صرف
نقصان لازم ہے
قال ومن غصب عبدا فاستغله فنقصته الغلة فعليه النقصان لما بينا ويتصدق بالغلة قال وهذا عندهما ايضا وعنده لا يتصدق بالغلة وعلى هذا الخلاف اذا أجر المستعير المستعار لابي يوسف انه حصل في ضمانه وملكه اما الضمان ،فظاهر، وكذلک الملک فی المضمون لان المضمونات تملک باداء الضمان مستندا الى وقت الغصب عندنا، ولهما انه حصل بسبب خبيث وهو التصرف فى ملك الغير، وما هذا حاله فسبيله التصدق اذ الفرع يحصل على وصف الاصل والملك المستند ناقص فلا ينعدم به الخبث فلو هلک العبد في يد الغاصب حتى ضمنه له ان يستعين بالغلة فى اداء الضمان لان الخبث لاجل المالك، ولهذا لو ادى اليه يباح له التناول فيزول الخبث بالاداء اليه بخلاف ما اذا باعه فهلك فى يد المشترى ثم استحق وغرمه ليس له ان يستعين بالغلة فى اداء الثمن اليه لان الخبث ما كان لحق المشترى الا اذا كان لا يجد غيره لانه محتاج اليه فله ان يصرفه الى حاجة نفسه، فلو اصاب ما لا يتصدق بمثله ان كان غنيا وقت الاستعمال وان كان فقيرا فلا شيء عليه لما ذكرنا
ترجمہ کسی نے غلام غصب کر کے اجارہ پر دیا اور مزدوری کے کام نے اس کو ناقص کر دیا تو اس پر خالی نقصان واجب ہوگا بدلیل مذکور اور اس کی اجرت کو صدقہ کر دے صاحب ہدا یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ بھی طرفین کے نزدیک ہے امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اجرت کو صدقہ نہیں کرے گا، اسی اختلاف پر ہے جب مستعیر نے مستعار چیز کو اجارہ پر دیا۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ مال اس کی ضمانت اور ملکیت میں آگیا ضمانت میں آنا تو ظاہر ہے اور یوں ہی مضمون میں ملک کا ہونا ہے کیونکہ مضمون چیزیں ملک میں آجاتی ہیں اداء ضمان سے وقت غصب کی طرف مستند ہو کر ہمارے نزدیک ، طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ سبب خبیث سے حاصل ہوا ہے اور دوسرے کی ملک میں تصرف کرنا ہے اور جس کا یہ حال ہو اس کی راہ صدقہ کرنا ہے اس لئے کہ فرع کا حصول اصل کی صفت پر ہوتا ہے اور ملک مستند ناقص ہوتا ہے تو اس سے محبت دور نہ ہوگا پھر اگر غلام غاصب کے پاس تلف ہو گیا حتی کہ وہ اس کا ضامن تھیرا تو وہ ادائے ضمان میں اجرت سے مدد لے سکتا ہے کیونکہ خبث تو مالک کی وجہ سے تھا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر غاصب وہ اجرت مالک کو دیتا تو اس کے لئے تناول مباح ہوتا۔ پس اس کو ادا کرنے کی وجہ سے محبت زائل ہو گیا۔ بخلاف اس کے جب غلام کو فرخت کر دیا اور وہ مشتری کے پاس تلف ہو گیا پھر وہ مستحق قرار پایا اور مشتری نے تاوان دے دیا تو غاصب بائع ادائیگی شمن میں اجرت سے مدد نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ خبث حق مشتری کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ اس کے علاوہ کچھ نہ پائے کیونکہ وہ اس کا محتاج ہے تو اپنی ضرورت میں صرف کر سکتا ہے پھر جب اس کو مال ہے تو اس کے مثل صدقہ کر دے۔ اگر بوقت استعمال غنی ہو اور اگر فقیر ہوتو اس پر کچھ نہیں ۔ تشریح قوله ومن غصب عبداً .... الخ - اگر غاصب نے مغصوب سے کوئی منفعت حاصل کی ۔ مثلاً مغصوب غلام تھا نا صب تھا نے اس کو مزدوری پر دیدیا اور استعمال کی وجہ سے اس میں نقص آ گیا تو نقصان کا ضمان دے اور ضمان کے بعد جو کچھ نفع باقی رہے اس کو خیرات دے اسی طرح اگر عین مغصوب یا ودیعت میں کوئی تصرف کیا۔ مثلاً اس کو بیچ ڈالا اور اس میں نفع حاصل ہوا تو منفعت خیرات کر دے ( جب مغصوب اور ودیعت ایسی شئی ہو جو اشارہ سے متعین ہو جاتی ہو یعنی از قسم اسباب ہو ) یہ حکم طرفین کے نزدیک ہے ۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تصدق واجب نہیں ۔ وہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ غاصب کو جو نفع حاصل ہوا ہے وہ اس کے معمان اور اس کی ملک میں ظاہر ہوا ہے حصول فی الضمان تو ظاہر ہے کہ شئی مغصوب اس کے عمان میں داخل ہو گئی اور حصول فی الملک اس لئے ہے کہ ادائیگی عضمان کے بعد مضمون مملوک ہو جاتی ہے اور ملک وقت غصب کی طرف منسوب ہوتی ہے اور جب نفع اس کی ملک میں حاصل ہوا ہے تو تصدیق واجب نہیں۔ طرفین یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نفع گو اس کی ملک میں حاصل ہوا ہے۔ لیکن اس کا حصول سبب خبیث یعنی غیر کی ملک میں تصرف کرنے. سے ہوا ہے اور جو چیز سبب خبیث کے ذریعہ حاصل ہو اس کا راستہ یہی ہے کہ خیرات کر دے ۔ فقیہ ابواللیث کا بیان ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف کا جو قول مذکور ہوا ہے وہ پہلا قول ہے اور آخری قول قول طرفین کے مثل ہے۔۔
قوله فلو هلک العبد ... الخ - پھر اگر غلام مذکور غاصب کے پاس تلف ہو گیا یہاں تک کہ اس کی قیمت کا تاوان دینا لازم آیا تو وہ اداء تاوان میں اس مزدوری سے مدد لے سکتا ہے ۔ کیونکہ خبث تو مالک کی وجہ سے تھا ، یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر غاصب وہ مزدوری مالک کو دے دیتا تو اس سے غاصب کو بھی تناول مباح ہو جاتا .
اگر چہ تو نگر ہو ۔ پس اس کو ادا کرنے کی وجہ سے خبث جا تا رہا۔ اس کے برخلاف غلام کو اگر فروخت کر دیا اور مشتری کے پاس قبضہ کے بعد تلف ہو گیا ۔ پھر مالک نے اپنا استحقاق ثابت کر کے مشتری سے تاوان لے لیا تو غاصب بائع اداء شمن میں اس مزدوری سے مدد نہیں لے سکتا اس لئے کہ مزدوری میں جو محبت ہے وہ حق مشتری کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے ۔ بلکہ حق مالک کی وجہ سے ہے ہاں اگر غاصب بائع کے پاس اس مزدوری کے علاوہ کچھ نہ ہو تو بالفعل اس سے ادا کر سکتا ہے۔ اس کے بعد مال ملنے پر اتنا ہی صدقہ کر دے۔ ہزار روپے غصب کئے اور باندی خریدی اور دو ہزار کی بیچ دی پھر دو ہزار کی باندی خریدی اسے تین ہزار میں بیچ دیا تو تمام منافع کا صدقہ لازم ہے
Book of Usurpation. 340. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 12. If the usurper employed the usurped slave and the work caused a loss to him, then only the loss is obligatory upon the usurper. He said: Whoever usurps a slave and then uses him for work, and the profit (ghallah) causes a decrease, then upon him is the loss as we have explained, and he gives the ghallah in charity. He said: This is also the view of the two (companions), and according to him (Abu Hanifa) he does not give the ghallah in charity. And upon this difference is the case when the borrower (musta'ir) rents out the borrowed item. According to Abu Yusuf, it (the profit) comes under his guarantee and ownership. As for the guarantee, it is apparent, and likewise ownership in the guaranteed item because guaranteed items are owned by paying the guarantee (damān) traced back to the time of usurpation according to us. And according to the two (companions), it is acquired through a bad cause (sabab khabīth), namely acting in the property of another. Whatever has this status, its way is charity, because the branch (far') takes the description of the origin (aṣl), and the traced ownership is deficient, so the taint (khabath) is not removed by it. So if the slave perishes in the hand of the usurper until he becomes liable for it, he may use the ghallah to pay the guarantee because the taint was for the sake of the owner. For this, if he pays it to the owner, it becomes permissible for him to use, so the taint is removed by paying to him, unlike if he sold it and it perished in the hand of the buyer, then it is reclaimed and he (the buyer) pays compensation, he (the usurper) cannot use the ghallah to pay the price to him because the taint was not for the right of the buyer, unless he has nothing else because he is in need, then he may spend it for his own need. So if he acquires something that he does not give in charity like it, if he was rich at the time of use, and if he was poor, nothing is upon him due to what we have mentioned. Translation: Someone usurped a slave and gave him on rent, and the work caused loss to him, so only the loss is obligatory upon him by the mentioned proof, and he gives his wage in charity. The author of Hidayah says: This is also according to the two (companions). According to Imam Abu Yusuf, he will not give the wage in charity. Upon this difference is when the borrower rented out the borrowed item. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that the property came under his guarantee and ownership; coming under guarantee is apparent, and likewise ownership of the guaranteed item because guaranteed items come into ownership by paying the guarantee traced to the time of usurpation according to us. The proof of the two (companions) is that it is acquired through a bad cause, which is acting in the property of another, and whatever has this status, its way is charity, because the branch takes the description of the origin, and the traced ownership is deficient, so the taint is not removed. Then if the slave perishes in the hand of the usurper until he becomes its guarantor, he can seek help from the wage in paying the guarantee because the taint was due to the owner. This is why if the usurper gives that wage to the owner, it becomes permissible for him to use. Thus due to giving, the taint is removed. Contrary to when he sold the slave and it perished in the hand of the buyer, then it was reclaimed and the buyer paid compensation, the usurper seller cannot seek help from the wage in paying the price to him because the taint is not due to the right of the buyer, unless he has nothing else because he is in need, then he may spend it for his need. Then when he gets wealth, he gives charity equal to it. If he was rich at the time of use, he gives charity; if he was poor, nothing upon him. Commentary on his saying 'Whoever usurps a slave...' etc.: If the usurper obtained some benefit from the usurped property, e.g., the usurped was a slave, he gave him on rent, and due to use a loss occurred, he compensates the loss, and after compensation whatever profit remains, he gives it in charity. Similarly, if he made a transaction in the usurped item or deposit, e.g., sold it and obtained profit, then he gives the profit in charity (provided the usurped and deposited item is such that it is specified by pointing, i.e., of the type of goods). This ruling is according to the two (companions). According to Imam Abu Yusuf, charity is not obligatory. He says: The profit acquired by the usurper appears under his guarantee and his ownership; the occurrence under guarantee is apparent because the usurped item enters his guarantee, and the occurrence under ownership is because after paying the guarantee, the guaranteed item becomes owned, and ownership is attributed to the time of usurpation. So when the profit is acquired in his ownership, charity is not obligatory. The two (companions) say: Although the profit is acquired in his ownership, its acquisition was through a bad cause, i.e., acting in another's property, and whatever is acquired through a bad cause, its way is to give in charity. Faqih Abu al-Layth said: The mentioned saying of Imam Abu Yusuf is his first saying, and his last saying is like the saying of the two (companions). His saying 'so if the slave perishes...' etc.: Then if the mentioned slave perishes in the hand of the usurper so that it becomes necessary to pay its price, he may seek help from that wage in paying the compensation, because the taint was due to the owner. This is why if the usurper gives that wage to the owner, it becomes permissible for him to use, even if he is negligent. Thus due to giving, the taint is removed. Contrary to if he sold the slave and it perished in the hand of the buyer after possession, then the owner proved his right and took compensation from the buyer, the usurper seller cannot seek help from that wage in paying the price, because the taint in the wage is not due to the right of the buyer but due to the right of the owner. Yes, if the usurper seller has nothing besides that wage, he can pay with it for now, and later when he gets wealth, he gives charity equal to it. He usurped 1000 rupees, bought a slave girl, sold her for 2000, then bought a slave girl for 2000, sold her for 3000, then it is necessary to give all the profit in charity.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute from Kitab al-Ghasb of al-Hidayah, commented upon in Ashraf al-Hidayah. The ruling in the matn is that when a usurper (ghāṣib) uses a usurped slave for work and the work causes a loss to the slave (e.g., reduction in value), the usurper must compensate the loss and also give the profit (ghallah) earned from the work in charity. The author of al-Hidayah then notes that this ruling—giving the ghallah in charity—is the position of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), while Abu Hanifa holds that the usurper does not give it in charity. The reasoning is as follows: According to the two companions, the profit is acquired through a bad cause (sabab khabīth)—unlawful use of another's property—so it must be purified by charity. Although the usurper becomes the owner of the profit by virtue of his guarantee (damān) and traced ownership (milk mustanid), this ownership is deficient and does not remove the taint. Abu Hanifa argues that since the usurper is liable for the slave (he must pay its value if it perishes), the profit belongs to him lawfully as a secondary right, and no charity is required. The text then discusses a sub-case: if the slave perishes in the usurper's hand, he may use the ghallah to pay the compensation to the owner, because the taint was for the owner's right. Paying the compensation removes the taint. However, if the usurper sold the slave and the buyer paid compensation after the owner reclaimed it, the usurper cannot use the ghallah for that payment, because the taint was not for the buyer's right. But if the usurper has no other means, he may use it and later give charity when able. The commentary also mentions a narration from Faqih Abu al-Layth that Imam Abu Yusuf's final position aligns with the two companions. The dispute is practical: according to Abu Hanifa, the usurper may keep the profit; according to the two, he must give it away. The relied-upon (muftā bihi) position in the madhhab is that of the two companions, as stated in the matn.

Key Terms
غلة (ghallah): Profit, yield, or earnings from the usurped property, such as wages from hiring out a slave.
خبث (khabath): Moral or legal taint/impurity resulting from unlawful acquisition or use of property.
ضمان (damān): Guarantee or liability; the usurper's obligation to compensate the value of the usurped item if it perishes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what must a usurper do with the ghallah (profit) from a usurped slave?
A) Keep it as his own lawful property
B) Give it in charity
C) Return it to the owner
D) Destroy it

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, profit from usurped property is tainted and must be given in charity according to the relied-upon position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Profit from Trading with Usurped Money: The Dispute Between the Two and Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute with expansion on condition of actual payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on profit from usurped money, explain the proofs of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and apply the condition of actual payment (naqd) to determine when charity is obligatory.

Core Idea
Profit from usurped property must be purified, but only if the usurper actually used the specific usurped money.

In this lesson, we examine an important intra-Hanafi dispute concerning profits generated from trading with usurped property. The matn of al-Hidayah presents a clear example: a person usurps 1000 dirhams, buys and sells slave girls successively, making a total profit of 2000 dirhams. The question is: must the usurper give all that profit in charity, or may he keep it? The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say charity is obligatory; Abu Yusuf disagrees. Understanding this dispute and its finer details—especially the distinction between specific goods and fungibles—is crucial for applying the rule correctly.

Guided Path
1
State the Example and the Ruling
Identify the hypothetical given: a person usurps 1000 dirhams, buys a slave girl with it, sells her for 2000, uses that to buy another, sells for 3000. According to the Two, all profit (2000 dirhams) must be given in charity. Abu Yusuf holds it is not obligatory.
The matn explicitly says 'yatasadduq bi jami' al-ribh' (he gives all the profit in charity) as the view of the Two.
2
Analyze the Proofs of Each Side
Abu Yusuf argues: the profit appears under guarantee and traced ownership, so it is lawful. The Two respond: although the profit is owned, its acquisition was through a bad cause (acting in another's property), so purification is needed. In the case of a deposit (wadi'a), the reasoning is even clearer because no guarantee exists initially.
The text mentions that the response in wadi'a is 'azhar' (more apparent).
3
Distinguish Between Specific Goods and Fungibles
The rule applies to goods that are specified by pointing (mā yataʿayyanu bi al-ishāra), like specific items. For fungibles (like money, thamanayn), charity is only wajib if the usurper actually paid from the usurped money. If he merely pointed to it but paid from other wealth, the profit is lawful according to al-Karkhi.
Al-Karkhi argues that ishāra alone does not transfer the taint; actual payment (naqd) is required to establish khabath.
4
Note the Tarjih and the Chosen View
The later mashāyikh (authors of al-Jami'ayn and al-Mabsut) hold that the profit is never lawful for the usurper, whether before or after guarantee. This is the mufta bihi position.
The text says 'wa huwa al-mukhtār' (this is the chosen view) due to the absolute answer in those works.
5
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Under Abu Yusuf's first view, the usurper may keep the profit; under the Two and the final view, he must give it in charity. This practical difference affects whether the usurper must purify his earnings.
Faqih Abu al-Layth reports that Abu Yusuf's final view aligned with the Two.

Source Text

كتاب الغصب
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ خیرات دے اسی طرح اگر عین مغصوب یا ودیعت میں کوئی تصرف کیا۔ مثلاً اس کو بیچ ڈالا اور اس میں نفع حاصل ہوا تو منفعت خیرات کر دے ( جب مغصوب ودیعت ایسی شئی ہو جو اشارہ سے متعین ہو جاتی ہو یعنی از قسم اسباب ہو ) یہ حکم طرفین کے نزدیک ہے ۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تصدق واجب نہیں ۔ وہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ غاصب کو جو نفع حاصل ہوا ہے وہ اس کے معمان اور اس کی ملک میں ظاہر ہوا ہے حصول فی الضمان تو ظاہر ہے کہ شئی مغصوب اس کے عمان میں داخل ہو گئی اور حصول فی الملک اس لئے ہے کہ ادائیگی عضمان کے بعد مضمون مملوک ہو جاتی ہے اور ملک وقت غصب کی طرف منسوب ہوتی ہے اور جب نفع اس کی ملک میں حاصل ہوا ہے تو تصدیق واجب نہیں۔ طرفین یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نفع گو اس کی ملک میں حاصل ہوا ہے۔ لیکن اس کا حصول سبب خبیث یعنی غیر کی ملک میں تصرف کرنے. سے ہوا ہے اور جو چیز سبب خبیث کے ذریعہ حاصل ہو اس کا راستہ یہی ہے کہ خیرات کر دے ۔ فقیہ ابواللیث کا بیان ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف کا جو قول مذکور ہوا ہے وہ پہلا قول ہے اور آخری قول قول طرفین کے مثل ہے۔۔
قال ومن غصب الفا فاشترى بها جارية فباعها بالفين ثم اشترى بالالفين جارية فباعها بثلاثة آلاف درهم فانه يتصدق بجميع الربح، وهذا عندهما واصله ان الغاصب والمودع اذا تصرف فى المغصوب او الوديعة وربح لا يطيب لـه الـربـح عـنـدهـما خلافا لابي يوسف وقد مرت الدلائل وجوابهما في الوديعة اظهر لانه لا يستند الملك الى ما قبل التصرف لانعدام سبب الضمان، فلم يكن التصرف في ملكه، ثم هذا ظاهر فيما يتعين بالاشارة اما فيما لا يتعين كالثمنين فقوله فى الكتاب اشترى بها اشارة الى ان التصدق انما يجب اذا اشترى بها، ونقد منها الثمن، اما اذا اشار اليها ونقد من غيرها او نقد منها واشار الى غيرها او اطلق اطلاقا ونقد منها يطيب له وهكذا قال الكرخى لان الاشارة اذا كانت لا تفيد التعيين لابد ان يتاكد بالنقد ليتحقق الخبث، وقال مشايخنا لا يطيب له قبل ان يضمن وكذا بعد الضمان بكل حال، وهو المختار لاطلاق الجواب في الجامعين والمبسوط قال وان اشترى بالالف جارية تساوى الفين فوهبها او طعاما فاكله لم يتصدق بشيء وهذا قولهم
Book of Usurpation. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 13. He gives charity similarly if he transacted in the usurped item or deposit, e.g., sold it and obtained profit, then he gives the profit in charity (provided the usurped and deposited item is such that it is specified by pointing, i.e., of the type of goods). This ruling is according to the two (companions). According to Imam Abu Yusuf, charity is not obligatory. He says: The profit acquired by the usurper appears under his guarantee and his ownership; the occurrence under guarantee is apparent because the usurped item enters his guarantee, and the occurrence under ownership is because after paying the guarantee, the guaranteed item becomes owned, and ownership is attributed to the time of usurpation. So when the profit is acquired in his ownership, charity is not obligatory. The two (companions) say: Although the profit is acquired in his ownership, its acquisition was through a bad cause, i.e., acting in another's property, and whatever is acquired through a bad cause, its way is to give in charity. Faqih Abu al-Layth said: The mentioned saying of Imam Abu Yusuf is his first saying, and his last saying is like the saying of the two (companions). He said: And whoever usurps 1000 dirhams and with it buys a slave girl, then sells her for 2000, then with the 2000 buys a slave girl, then sells her for 3000 dirhams, then he gives all the profit in charity. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). The origin is that the usurper and the depositary (mudiʿ) when they transact in the usurped or deposited item and make profit, the profit is not permissible (ṭayyib) for them according to the two, contrary to Abu Yusuf. The proofs have passed, and their response in the case of deposit is clearer because ownership is not traced back to before the transaction due to the absence of a cause of guarantee (damān), so the transaction was not in his property. Then this is apparent in what is specified by pointing (mā yataʿayyanu bi al-ishāra). As for what is not specified, like the two prices (thamanayn), his saying in the Book 'purchased with it' indicates that charity is obligatory only when he purchased with it and paid the price from it. But if he pointed to it but paid from something else, or paid from it but pointed to something else, or made an absolute payment and paid from it, then it is permissible (ṭayyib) for him. Thus said al-Karkhi because pointing does not effect specification; it must be confirmed by actual payment to realize the taint (khabath). Our mashāyikh said: It is not permissible for him before he guarantees, and likewise after guarantee in any case, and this is the chosen view because of the absolute answer in al-Jāmiʿayn and al-Mabsūṭ. He said: And if he buys with the 1000 a slave girl worth 2000, and gives her as a gift, or food and eats it, he does not give charity for anything. This is their view.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on usurpation, now specifically addressing profits from multiple transactions using usurped money. The matn of al-Hidayah gives an example: a person usurps 1000 dirhams, buys a slave girl, sells her for 2000, uses that to buy another slave girl, sells her for 3000. The ruling according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that all the profit must be given in charity. Abu Yusuf disagrees and says the profit is permissible for the usurper. The dispute is the same as in the previous section: Abu Yusuf argues that the profit is owned by virtue of guarantee and traced ownership, while the two hold that the transaction is based on a bad cause (using another's property), so the profit is tainted and must be purified by charity. The text then mentions that in the case of deposit (wadīʿa), the response is even clearer because there is no guarantee at the outset. Important details follow: the ruling applies to specific goods (mā yataʿayyanu bi al-ishāra). For fungible goods like money (thamanayn), the taint is only established if the usurper actually used the specific usurped money to pay for the purchase. If he merely pointed to it but paid from other wealth, the profit is lawful. This is the view of al-Karkhi. However, the later mashāyikh (like those who authored al-Jāmiʿayn and al-Mabsūṭ) hold that the profit is never lawful for the usurper, whether before or after guarantee, and this is the chosen (mukhtār) view. Finally, if the usurper buys a slave girl worth 2000 with the 1000 (i.e., a bargain) and then gives her away or eats the food, no charity is required because there is no profit? Actually the text says 'did not give charity for anything' because the profit is not realized in a separate form? The comment clarifies that if he doesn't realize a profit in his hand, charity is not required. The passage ends with 'This is their view.' The relied-upon position is that all profit from trading with usurped money must be given in charity.

Key Terms
ثمنين (thamanayn): The two prices; refers to fungible goods like money (dirhams) that are not specific items.
إشارة (ishāra): Pointing; a method of specifying an item in a contract, but for fungibles it does not establish taint without actual payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Keep all the profit as his own
B) Return the original 1000 dirhams only
C) Give all the profit in charity
D) Give only the profit from the first transaction in charity

Key Takeaway
Profit from usurped property is tainted and must be given in charity; the later Hanafi position holds this applies regardless of guarantee and actual payment.

Charity from Profit of Usurped Property: Sahibayn vs Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on charity from usurped property profit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on giving charity from profit of usurped property and evaluate the evidence used by Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Profit from usurped property must be given in charity because its cause is corrupt.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi debate regarding profit earned from disposing of another's property (ghasb). While all agree that usurpation is unlawful, they differ on whether the usurper must give the profit in charity. The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold it wajib; Abu Yusuf initially disagreed but later adopted their view. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi fiqh purifies wealth obtained through corrupt means.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the legal issue
The passage deals with a person who disposes of usurped property (e.g., sells it) and makes a profit. The question is whether that profit becomes halal or must be given in charity.
The item must be from the category of goods (not real estate mentioned in some versions).
2
State the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani)
They rule that the profit must be given in charity. Their evidence: although the profit is in the usurper's ownership, it was obtained through a corrupt cause (tasarruf in another's property). Anything earned through a corrupt cause must be purified by charity.
Corrupt cause (sabab khabīth) is the key reasoning.
3
State Abu Yusuf's initial position and his rationale
Abu Yusuf initially held that charity is not obligatory. He argued that the profit appeared in the usurper's possession and ownership. Possession is obvious; ownership is established because after paying compensation, the usurped item becomes his property, and ownership is retroactively attributed to the time of usurpation.
Abu Yusuf's dalil is aqli: ownership voids the need for purification.
4
Note the resolution: Abu Yusuf's final view
Faqih Abu al-Layth reports that Abu Yusuf later adopted the Sahibayn's view. Thus the intra-Hanafi dispute is resolved in favor of wajib charity.
This shows that even within the school, opinions evolved.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: profit from usurped property must be given in charity. This is the established ruling in the Hanafi school.
Zahir al-Riwayah supports this; Abu Yusuf's final agreement strengthens it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الغصب
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ خیرات دے اسی طرح اگر عین مغصوب یا ودیعت میں کوئی تصرف کیا۔ مثلاً اس کو بیچ ڈالا اور اس میں نفع حاصل ہوا تو منفعت خیرات کر دے ( جب مغصوب اور ودیعت ایسی شئی ہو جو اشارہ سے متعین ہو جاتی ہو یعنی از قسم اسباب ہو ) یہ حکم طرفین کے نزدیک ہے ۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تصدق واجب نہیں ۔ وہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ غاصب کو جو نفع حاصل ہوا ہے وہ اس کے معمان اور اس کی ملک میں ظاہر ہوا ہے حصول فی الضمان تو ظاہر ہے کہ شئی مغصوب اس کے عمان میں داخل ہو گئی اور حصول فی الملک اس لئے ہے کہ ادائیگی عضمان کے بعد مضمون مملوک ہو جاتی ہے اور ملک وقت غصب کی طرف منسوب ہوتی ہے اور جب نفع اس کی ملک میں حاصل ہوا ہے تو تصدیق واجب نہیں۔ طرفین یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نفع گو اس کی ملک میں حاصل ہوا ہے۔ لیکن اس کا حصول سبب خبیث یعنی غیر کی ملک میں تصرف کرنے. سے ہوا ہے اور جو چیز سبب خبیث کے ذریعہ حاصل ہو اس کا راستہ یہی ہے کہ خیرات کر دے ۔ فقیہ ابواللیث کا بیان ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف کا جو قول مذکور ہوا ہے وہ پہلا قول ہے اور آخری قول قول طرفین کے مثل ہے۔۔
Book of Usurpation. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 13. He gives charity. Similarly, if he made any disposition in the usurped object or deposit, e.g., sold it and made a profit, then he gives the profit in charity (when the usurped object or deposit is something that becomes determinate by indication, i.e., of the category of goods). This is the ruling according to the two sides (Sahibayn). According to Imam Abu Yusuf, charity is not obligatory. He says: The profit the usurper obtained has appeared in his possession and in his ownership. As for appearance in possession, it is obvious that the usurped item entered his possession. As for appearance in ownership, it is because after paying compensation, the object becomes owned, and ownership is attributed to the time of usurpation. So when the profit is obtained in his ownership, charity is not obligatory. The two sides say: Although the profit is obtained in his ownership, its acquisition was through a corrupt cause, i.e., disposing in another's property. Whatever is obtained through a corrupt cause, its path is this: he gives it in charity. Faqih Abu al-Layth stated that the saying mentioned of Imam Abu Yusuf is his first saying, and his final saying is like the saying of the two sides.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether profit from usurped property must be given in charity. The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that it must, because the profit was obtained through a corrupt means (tasarruf in another's property). Abu Yusuf holds it is not obligatory because the profit is acquired in his own possession (since the usurped item is in his possession and becomes his property upon payment of compensation). However, Faqih Abu al-Layth reports that Abu Yusuf later adopted the view of the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Unlawful appropriation of another's property without right.
طرفین (tarafayn): The two sides: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, as opposed to Abu Yusuf.
سبب خبیث (sabab khabīth): A cause that is legally impure, i.e., a prohibited transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Using Wages from a Usurped Slave to Offset Compensation
Ruling on using impure wages to offset compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using wages from a usurped slave to offset compensation and identify the condition under which the impurity is removed.

Core Idea
Wages from a usurped slave become pure when given to the owner, allowing their use to offset compensation.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: a usurper uses a usurped slave for work and earns wages. If the slave later dies, the usurper owes compensation for the slave's value. The wages earned are considered impure (khabath) due to the wrongful use of the slave. May the usurper use those impure wages to pay the compensation? The Hanafi response is nuanced and depends on whether the wages are transferred to the rightful owner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Parties
Recognize the scenario: a usurper (ghāṣib) took a slave, used the slave for work, and earned wages (mazdūrī). The slave then perishes while in the usurper's possession. The usurper owes compensation (tāwān) for the slave's value.
2
Determine the Basis of Impurity (Khabath)
Understand that the wages are impure because they were earned through the wrongful use of the owner's property. The impurity is attached to the right of the owner, not the usurper. Therefore, returning the wages to the owner removes the impurity.
Key principle: khabath is removed when the profit goes to the rightful owner.
3
Apply the Condition: Transfer of Wages to Owner
If the usurper gives the wages to the owner (or intends to use them to pay compensation that ultimately benefits the owner), the impurity is lifted. He may then use those wages to offset his compensation debt. The text states, 'he can take help from that wage in paying the compensation.'
Even if you are wary (tawangur), the impurity is removed by payment.
4
Distinguish the Case of Sale to a Third Party
If the usurper sold the slave to a buyer and the slave later perished with the buyer, the owner takes compensation from the buyer. In that case, the usurper-seller cannot use the wages to offset his debt to the buyer, because the impurity is due to the owner's right, not the buyer's. Exception: if the usurper has no other means, he may pay with the wages and later give an equal amount in charity.
This distinction highlights that khabath is tied to the owner's right, not the buyer's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله فلو هلک العبد ... الخ - پھر اگر غلام مذکور غاصب کے پاس تلف ہو گیا یہاں تک کہ اس کی قیمت کا تاوان دینا لازم آیا تو وہ اداء تاوان میں اس مزدوری سے مدد لے سکتا ہے ۔ کیونکہ خبث تو مالک کی وجہ سے تھا ، یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر غاصب وہ مزدوری مالک کو دے دیتا تو اس سے غاصب کو بھی تناول مباح ہو جاتا .
اگر چہ تو نگر ہو ۔ پس اس کو ادا کرنے کی وجہ سے خبث جا تا رہا۔ اس کے برخلاف غلام کو اگر فروخت کر دیا اور مشتری کے پاس قبضہ کے بعد تلف ہو گیا ۔ پھر مالک نے اپنا استحقاق ثابت کر کے مشتری سے تاوان لے لیا تو غاصب بائع اداء شمن میں اس مزدوری سے مدد نہیں لے سکتا اس لئے کہ مزدوری میں جو محبت ہے وہ حق مشتری کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے ۔ بلکہ حق مالک کی وجہ سے ہے ہاں اگر غاصب بائع کے پاس اس مزدوری کے علاوہ کچھ نہ ہو تو بالفعل اس سے ادا کر سکتا ہے۔ اس کے بعد مال ملنے پر اتنا ہی صدقہ کر دے۔ ہزار روپے غصب کئے اور باندی خریدی اور دو ہزار کی بیچ دی پھر دو ہزار کی باندی خریدی اسے تین ہزار میں بیچ دیا تو تمام منافع کا صدقہ لازم ہے
His saying: 'So if the slave perishes...' - Then if the mentioned slave perishes with the usurper such that he is obliged to pay compensation for its value, he can take help from that wage in paying the compensation. Because the impurity was due to the owner. This is why if the usurper gave that wage to the owner, then consumption becomes permissible for the usurper as well. Even if you are wary. So due to his paying it, the impurity went away. Conversely, if he sold the slave and it perished with the buyer after possession, then the owner proves his right and takes compensation from the buyer, the usurper-seller cannot take help from that wage in paying the price. Because the impurity in the wage is not due to the right of the buyer, but due to the right of the owner. Yes, if the usurper-seller has nothing besides that wage, he can pay with it effectively. Then when he gets property, he gives an equal amount in charity. He usurped a thousand rupees and bought a slave-girl and sold her for two thousand, then bought a slave-girl with two thousand and sold her for three thousand, then he must give all profit in charity.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about wages earned from a usurped slave. If a usurper uses a slave for work (taking wages) and the slave then dies, the impurity in the wages is removed if the usurper pays the wages to the owner. He can use those wages to reduce the compensation he owes for the slave's death. However, if he sold the slave and the buyer suffered loss (the slave died after possession, and the owner took compensation from the buyer), the usurper-seller cannot use the wages to offset the price he owes to the buyer, because the impurity was due to the owner's right, not the buyer's. But if he has nothing else, he may use the wages, then later give an equal amount in charity when he can. The passage ends with an example: if someone usurps 1000, buys a slave-girl, sells for 2000, buys another with 2000, sells for 3000, all profit must be given in charity.

Key Terms
تاوان (tāwān): Compensation or indemnity paid for the loss of property due to usurpation.
مزدوری (mazdūrī): Wages earned from the service of the usurped slave.
خبث (khabath): Spiritual impurity of property acquired through prohibited means.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, because the wages are impure
B) Yes, because the impurity is removed if he gives the wages to the owner
C) Yes, but only with the owner's permission
D) No, compensation must be paid separately

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling permits using impure wages from a usurped slave to offset compensation if the wages are given to the rightful owner, removing the impurity.

Profit from Usurped Money: When Must It Be Given in Charity?
Details conditions for charity on profit from usurped property, distinguishing specific and non-specific property, and presents the preferred absolute view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on profit from usurped money, distinguish the conditions for specific vs non-specific property, and identify the preferred view (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
Profit from usurped money is never pure for the usurper; charity is wajib based on the preferred Hanafi view.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical issue in transactions involving usurped property. It presents the Sahibayn's view that any profit from disposing of usurped goods must be given in charity, and then explores the conditions under which this applies, especially when the property is fungible like money. The text also records a stronger position from the later scholars (mashāyikh) that profit is never pure, which is the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The scenario: a usurper buys and sells with usurped money and makes a profit. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani together), he must give all profit in charity (wajib).
Abu Yusuf alone holds the profit is pure — this is the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is based on qiyas: the profit arises from a corrupt cause (tasarruf in another's property without ownership). In a deposit, the impurity is clearer because there is no liability (damān) at all.
The text mentions that for deposit, ownership is not established before disposition, making the profit impure.
3
Distinguish property types
For property that becomes specific by indication (muta'ayyin bi al-ishāra, e.g., a specific slave), the impurity is obvious. For non-specific property like dirhams, charity is only required if the usurper actually used the usurped money (pointed to them and paid from them).
Al-Karakhi requires both indication and actual payment; mashāyikh ignore this condition.
4
Note the tarjih
The mashāyikh hold that profit is never pure, whether before or after compensation. This is the preferred view (mukhtār) based on the absolute answers in Jāmi' al-Saghir, Jāmi' al-Kabīr, and al-Mabsūt.
The text explicitly says 'wa huwa al-mukhtār' (and this is preferred).
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under al-Karakhi's condition, the usurper might keep the profit if he uses other money; under the mashāyikh, he must give charity regardless.
Also, the requirement of ittiḥād al-jins: profit is only realized when the sale and purchase are of the same type (e.g., both dirhams).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن غصب الفا فاشتری بها جارية فباعها بالفين ثم اشترى بالالفين جارية فباعها بثلاثة آلاف درهم فانه يتصدق بجميع الربح، وهذا عندهما واصله ان الغاصب والمودع اذا تصرف فى المغصوب او الوديعة وربح لا يطيب لـه الـربـح عـنـدهـما خلافا لابي يوسف وقد مرت الدلائل وجوابهما في الوديعة اظهر لانه لا يستند الملك الى ما قبل التصرف لانعدام سبب الضمان، فلم يكن التصرف في ملكه، ثم هذا ظاهر فيما يتعين بالاشارة اما فيما لا يتعين كالثمنين فقوله فى الكتاب اشترى بها اشارة الى ان التصدق انما يجب اذا اشترى بها، ونقد منها الثمن، اما اذا اشار اليها ونقد من غيرها او نقد منها واشار الى غيرها او اطلق اطلاقا ونقد منها يطيب له وهكذا قال الكرخى لان الاشارة اذا كانت لا تفيد التعيين لابد ان يتاكد بالنقد ليتحقق الخبث، وقال مشايخنا لا يطيب له قبل ان يضمن وكذا بعد الضمان بكل حال، وهو المختار لاطلاق الجواب في الجامعين والمبسوط قال وان اشترى بالالف جارية تساوى الفين فوهبها او طعاما فاكله لم يتصدق بشيء وهذا قولهم جميعا، لان الربح انما يتبين عند اتحاد الجنس

قوله ثم هذا ظاهر ... الخ - پھر نفع کا پاکیزہ نہ ہونا ایسے مال مغصوب میں تو ظاہر ہے جو اشارہ سے متعین ہو جاتا ہے جیسے عروض و اسباب کا عقد کا تعلق انہیں سے ہوتا ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر قبضہ سے پہلے اسباب ہلاک ہو جائے تو بیع باطل ہو جاتی ہے(فیستفيد الرقبة واليد في المبيع بملک خبیث فیتصدق به) رہا ایسا مال مغصوب جو اشارہ سے متعین نہیں ہوتا جیسے مین مینی در جم ودنا نیز سو اس کی بابت اختلاف ہے۔ امام محمد سے جامع صغیر میں جو یہ فرمایا ہے 'اشتری بھا یہ اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ نفع کا صدقہ کرنا اسی وقت ضروری ہے۔ جب انہیں در اہم کے عوض خریدے اور انہیں سے دام ادا کرے بقول فخر الاسلام مذکورہ عبارت کا ظاہر اسی پر دال
He said: Whoever usurps a thousand dirhams and buys a slave-girl with them, then sells her for two thousand, then buys a slave-girl with the two thousand and sells her for three thousand dirhams, then he gives all the profit in charity. This is according to the two sides. The basis is that when a usurper or depositee disposes of the usurped or deposited property and profits, the profit is not permissible for him according to the two sides, contrary to Abu Yusuf. The proofs have passed, and their answer is more apparent in the case of a deposit because ownership is not established before disposition due to the absence of a cause for liability. So the disposition was not in his own property. Then this is apparent in what becomes determinate by indication. As for what does not become determinate, like the two prices, his saying in the book 'he bought with them' is an indication that charity is only obligatory when he buys with them and pays the price from them. But if he pointed to them and paid from other than them, or paid from them and pointed to other than them, or made an absolute contract and paid from them, then the profit is permissible for him. Al-Karakhi said likewise because indication does not effect determination, so it must be reinforced by payment to establish the impurity. Our scholars (mashāyikh) said: It is not permissible for him before compensation, nor after compensation in any case, and this is preferred due to the absolute nature of the answer in Jāmi' al-Saghir, Jāmi' al-Kabīr, and al-Mabsūt. He said: If he bought a slave-girl worth two thousand with the thousand and then gave her as a gift or bought food and ate it, he does not give charity in anything. This is the saying of all of them, because profit is only realized when the types unite. Book of Ghasb. All of them, because profit is only realized when the types unite. 342. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 12. Translation: Someone usurped a thousand dirhams and bought a slave-girl with them, sold her for two thousand, then bought a slave-girl with the thousand (actually two thousand) and sold her for three thousand, then he gives all profit in charity. This is according to the two sides. Its basis is that when a usurper or depositee disposes of the usurped or deposited property and makes a profit, according to the two sides the profit is not pure for him. Contrary to Imam Abu Yusuf; the proofs have passed. The answer of the two sides is more apparent in the case of a deposit, because ownership is not established to the property before disposition due to the absence of a cause of liability. So the disposition was not in his own property. Then this is apparent in property that becomes determinate by indication. As for property that does not become determinate, like the two prices, the statement in the book 'he bought with them' is an indication that charity becomes obligatory only when he buys with them and pays the price from them. If he pointed to them and paid from other than them, or paid from them and pointed to other than them, or made an absolute contract and paid from them, then the profit is pure for him. Imam Karakhi said likewise, because indication does not effect determination, so it must be reinforced by payment so that the impurity is realized. Our scholars said: It is not pure for him before compensation nor after compensation in any case, and this is preferred due to the absolute answer in Jāmi' al-Saghir, Jāmi' al-Kabīr, and al-Mabsūt. If he bought with the thousand a slave-girl worth two thousand, then gifted her or bought food and ate it, he does not give charity, and this is the saying of all of them, because profit is only realized when the types unite. Annotation... His saying: 'Whoever usurps a thousand...' – Zayd usurped a thousand dirhams from Bakr and bought a slave-girl with those same dirhams, sold her for two thousand, then bought another slave-girl with the two thousand and sold her for three thousand, then he gives all profit in charity. This is according to the two sides. Imam Shafi'i's new view and one narration from Imam Ahmad also is this, and some Malikis also hold this. The author of Hidayah says: The basis of the difference is that if a usurper or depositee disposes of the usurped or deposited property and makes profit, according to the two sides this profit is not pure for him, contrary to Imam Abu Yusuf, who says it is pure. Then in the case of a deposit, the proof of the two sides is more apparent because before disposition, ownership is not established, since the cause of liability is absent, so the disposition was not in his own property, thus the profit is impure. His saying: 'Then this is apparent...' – Then the impurity of profit is apparent in usurped property that becomes determinate by indication, like perishable goods and effects, where the contract relates to them, such that if the goods perish before possession, the sale becomes void. (Thus he gains ownership and possession of the sold item with a corrupt ownership, so he gives charity.) As for usurped property that does not become determinate by indication, like the two prices of dirhams and dinars, there is a difference of opinion. Imam Muhammad said in Jāmi' al-Saghir: 'He bought with them' – this indicates that charity is only necessary when he buys with those same dirhams and pays the price from them. According to Fakhr al-Islam, the apparent meaning of the mentioned passage indicates this.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on when profit from usurped money must be given in charity. It presents the Sahibayn's position that profit from disposing of usurped property is impure and must be given in charity, contrasting with Abu Yusuf who considered it pure. The passage then delves into the distinction between property that is specific (like goods that become determined by pointing) and non-specific (like money). For non-specific property, charity is only necessary if the usurped money is actually used in the purchase (pointed to and paid from that very money). If the purchase is made with other funds, the profit is pure for the usurper. Imam Karakhi agrees with this, but the later scholars (mashāyikh) hold a stronger view: profit is never pure, whether before or after compensation. This is the preferred view. The passage also clarifies that if no profit is realized (e.g., buying a slave-girl worth the same as the usurped money and then gifting her), no charity is required. The commentary by the author of Hidayah reiterates the dispute and emphasizes that in deposit cases, the impurity is clearer because the depositee never had ownership. The annotation (tashrīh) further explains the basis and mentions other schools' positions.

Key Terms
اشارة (ishāra): Indication; in sales, pointing to a specific item to identify it, which makes the item determinate.
متعين بالاشارة (muta'ayyin bi al-ishāra): Becoming determinate by indication; used for property that can be specified by pointing (e.g., a specific slave, a car).
ضمان (damān): Liability or compensation; the obligation to pay for loss or destruction of property.
اتحاد الجنس (ittiḥād al-jins): Unity of type or genre; profit is only realized when the sale and purchase involve items of the same type (e.g., both dirhams).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (mukhtār) in the Hanafi school, when is profit from usurped money considered pure for the usurper?
A) Before compensation, but not after
B) Only if the usurper uses his own money and points to the usurped money
C) Never; profit from usurped money is always impure
D) Only if the owner gives permission after the fact

Key Takeaway
Profit from usurped property is never pure for the usurper; charity is wajib according to the preferred Hanafi view.

Change in Usurped Property: Ownership Transfer and Liability
States ruling on transformation of usurped property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a usurper's transformation of property transfers ownership and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Ownership transfers to the usurper when he completely transforms the property; compensation is due.

When a usurper changes the stolen item so thoroughly that its original name and function vanish, a legal question arises: does the owner still own it? This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi answer, along with the Shafi'i challenge and an intra-madhhab nuance from Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for ownership transfer
Note the two criteria: loss of original name and loss of primary utility. Both must be present for ownership to depart from the original owner.
Example: wheat ground into flour loses the name 'wheat' and its primary benefit as whole grain.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
Ownership departs from the original owner and vests in the usurper. The usurper is liable to pay compensation (badal) and cannot benefit from the transformed property until he pays.
The ruling is general and applies to all similar transformations.
3
Examine the examples given
The text gives four clear examples: sheep to cooked meat, wheat to flour, iron to sword, brass to vessels. Each illustrates loss of name and benefit.
These examples help identify what constitutes a fundamental change.
4
Compare the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the owner's right persists despite transformation; the substance remains. The Hanafi objection is that the identity is lost.
The practical difference: Hanafi owner gets value, Shafi'i owner can claim the transformed object.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi variation
Abu Yusuf has two narrations: (1) if the owner chooses to take the flour, no compensation for loss is due (to avoid riba); (2) ownership departs but the transformed property is sold for debts and the owner has priority.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the clear Hanafi view: full ownership transfer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ فِيمَا يَتَغَيَّرُ بِفِعْلِ الْغَاصِبِ، قَالَ: وَإِذَا تَغَيَّرَتِ الْعَيْنُ الْمَغْصُوبَةُ بِفِعْلِ الْغَاصِبِ حَتَّى زَالَ اسْمُهَا وَأَعْظَمُ مَنَافِعِهَا زَالَ مِلْكُ الْمَغْصُوبِ مِنْهُ عَنْهَا، وَمَلَكَهَا الْغَاصِبُ وَضَمِنَهَا وَلَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ الِانْتِفَاعُ بِهَا حَتَّى يُؤَدِّيَ بَدَلَهَا كَمَنْ غَصَبَ شَاةً وَذَبَحَهَا وَشَوَاهَا أَوْ طَبَخَهَا أَوْ حِنْطَةً فَطَبَخَهَا أَوْ حَدِيدًا فَاتَّخَذَهُ سَيْفًا أَوْ صُفْرًا فَعَمِلَهُ آنِيَةً وَهَذَا كُلُّهُ عِنْدَنَا، وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يَنْقَطِعُ حَقُّ الْمَالِكِ وَهُوَ رِوَايَةٌ عَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا اخْتَارَ أَخْذَ الدَّقِيقِ لَا يَضْمَنُهُ النُّقْصَانَ عِنْدَهُ، لِأَنَّهُ يُؤَدِّي إِلَى الرِّبَا، وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ يَضْمَنُهُ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ يَزُولُ مِلْكُهُ عَنْهُ لَكِنَّهُ يُبَاعُ فِي دَيْنِهِ وَهُوَ أَحَقُّ بِهِ مِنَ الْغُرَمَاءِ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهِ
Chapter on what changes by the act of the usurper. He said: When the usurped property changes by the act of the usurper until its name and major benefits are lost, the ownership of the owner deptarts from it, and the usurper owns it and is liable for it, and it is not permissible for him to benefit from it until he pays its substitute. For example, one who usurps a sheep and slaughters it and roasts or cooks it, or wheat and cooks it, or iron and makes it into a sword, or brass and makes it into vessels. All this is according to us (Hanafi). Al-Shafi'i said: The right of the owner does not terminate. And there is a narration from Abu Yusuf that if he chooses to take the flour, he does not guarantee the loss according to him, because it leads to riba. And according to al-Shafi'i, he guarantees it. And from Abu Yusuf: His ownership departs from it, but it is sold for his debt, and he has greater right to it than creditors after his death.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This is a ruling on a fundamental change (taghayyur) in usurped property by the usurper. The Hanafi position (عندنا) is that if the usurper transforms the property so completely that its name and primary benefit are lost (e.g., sheep into cooked meat, wheat into flour, iron into a sword, brass into vessels), the original owner's ownership is extinguished, and the usurper becomes the owner. However, the usurper is liable to pay the value (or substitute) to the original owner, and he cannot use the new property until he pays. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that the original owner's right persists (he can still reclaim the transformed object if he wishes). There is also a narration from Abu Yusuf that if the original owner chooses to take the flour (from ground wheat), the usurper does not pay compensation for any decrease in value, because that would involve riba (since paying for loss in value of a food item could be seen as selling gold for gold with inequality). But al-Shafi'i says he must compensate the loss. Another narration from Abu Yusuf says ownership departs, but the new property is sold for the usurper's debts, and the original owner has priority over other creditors after the usurper's death.

Key Terms
زوال الاسم (zawāl al-ism): The loss of the original name of the property, e.g., wheat becomes flour, sheep becomes meat.
بدل (badal): Compensation or substitute; the usurper must pay the value of the original property to the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if someone usurps wheat and grinds it into flour, what happens to the ownership?
A) The original owner remains owner of the flour
B) The usurper becomes owner but must pay the value of the wheat
C) The usurper becomes owner and may use the flour freely
D) The flour is considered destroyed and the usurper pays nothing

Key Takeaway
When a usurper transforms property so its name and major benefit are lost, ownership transfers to the usurper who must pay compensation; this is the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Change of Usurped Property and Transfer of Ownership
Dispute on whether usurper gains ownership by changing property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ownership transfer when usurped property is fundamentally changed, identify the Shafi'i counter-argument, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When a usurper changes property beyond recognition, ownership transfers in Hanafi, but not in Shafi'i.

This lesson explores a classic inter-madhhab dispute over usurped property that has been transformed—like grinding wheat into flour. The Hanafi school holds that the usurper becomes the owner, while Imam al-Shafi'i maintains the original owner's right remains. Understanding the reasoning behind each position, especially the Hanafi reliance on istihsan, is crucial for applying the correct ruling in cases of property transformation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the conditions under which the Hanafi school transfers ownership: the usurper must change the property such that its name and major benefits are lost.
Examples: wheat ground into flour, iron made into a sword, timber built into a house.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and intra-Hanafi variation
State that Imam al-Shafi'i (and a narration from Abu Yusuf) hold the original owner's right is not severed. Note the nuance: if the owner takes the transformed item, no compensation due to usury concern.
Abu Yusuf also has a narration agreeing with the Hanafi position.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
Examine the Shafi'i analogy: the specific property remains, so ownership stays; work follows property; prohibited acts cannot transfer ownership (like wind blowing wheat into a mill).
They also analogize to slaughtering a usurped goat.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the cause of ownership is not the prohibited act but the creation of a valuable new work (ṣanʿah mutaqawwimah). The goat analogy fails because the name 'goat' remains after slaughter, whereas here the name changes.
Hanafi uses istihsan to prioritize the new work over the original right.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi allows the owner only to claim value (or take the item without compensation to avoid riba); Shafi'i allows the owner to reclaim the transformed property directly.
This affects how courts resolve disputes over improved or altered goods.

He made it. All this is according to us. Imam al-Shafi'i says the owner's right is not severed. This is one narration from Imam Abu Yusuf, only that if the owner chooses to take the flour, he cannot take compensation for loss. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, because this would lead to usury, and according to Imam al-Shafi'i, he can take compensation. And there is also a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf that the owner's ownership is nullified and it will be sold for his debt, and after the usurper's death, the owner has more right to it than other creditors. Commentary on 'When it changes etc.': The usurper usurped something and changed it such that its name and most of its purposes are lost. For example, a goat was usurped, slaughtered, roasted or cooked; or wheat was ground; or sown in a field; or iron made into a sword; or wool made into a vessel; or he mixed it with his property so that separation is impossible, e.g., a teak beam used in construction. In all these cases, according to us, the usurper becomes its owner. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the original owner's right is not severed. This is also a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf and the saying of Imam Ahmad. The only difference is that if the owner chooses to take the flour, he cannot take compensation from the usurper because it would entail usury, and according to al-Shafi'i, he can take the compensation. Also a narration from Abu Yusuf that the owner's property is nullified, but if the usurper dies, it will be sold for the owner's debt. For example, the flour is sold and wheat like it is bought and given to the owner, and the owner has more right to it than other creditors. The proof of Imam al-Shafi'i and the Hanafis: For al-Shafi'i: The specific thing remains, so it remains in his ownership, and the work follows it, like when the wind blows wheat into another's mill and it is ground. His act is not considered because it is prohibited, so it cannot be a cause of ownership, as known, just as if the act were non-existent, and it becomes like slaughtering the usurped goat, skinning it, and cutting it into pieces. And for us: He created a valuable work. So the owner's right is destroyed in one aspect; do you not see that the name changes and most purposes are lost, while his right in the work is established in every aspect? So it outweighs the original which is lost in one aspect. We do not make it a cause of ownership because it is prohibited, but because it is the creation of a work, unlike the goat, because its name remains after slaughter and skinning. This reasoning includes the mentioned chapters and others branch from it, so memorize it. Explanation of language: ... Translation: The proof of Imam al-Shafi'i is that the specific property remains, so it remains in the owner's ownership. The work is subordinate to it, like wheat blown by wind into another's mill and ground. The usurper's act is not considered because it is prohibited and cannot be a cause of ownership. So it is as if the act were non-existent, and like the usurped goat slaughtered, skinned, and cut into pieces. Our proof: The usurper created a valuable work, causing the owner's right to be lost in one aspect—the name changed and major benefits lost—while the usurper's right in the work is complete in every aspect. So it outweighs the original which is lost in one aspect. We do not consider the act as a cause because it is prohibited, but because it creates a new work, unlike the goat case, because its name remains after slaughter. This reasoning covers the mentioned issues and others branch from it, so preserve it.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage presents a major inter-madhhab dispute regarding usurped property that has been significantly altered by the usurper's actions. The passage first states the Hanafi position: when the usurper changes the property to such an extent that its name and primary benefits are lost, the usurper becomes the owner. Examples include grinding wheat into flour, building a house using usurped timber, or making a sword from iron. The original owner's right is severed. The Shafi'i position holds that the original owner's right remains intact. Within the Hanafi school, there is a narrated view from Imam Abu Yusuf that aligns with the Shafi'i position, but with a nuance: if the owner chooses to take the transformed property (e.g., flour), he cannot claim compensation from the usurper because that would involve interest (riba). Another narration from Abu Yusuf states that the owner's ownership is nullified, but the property is sold for the owner's debt if the usurper dies, and the owner has priority over other creditors. The passage then provides the proofs: Shafi'i argues that the specific property remains and the work follows it, using the analogy of wind blowing wheat into someone else's mill—the act is prohibited and cannot transfer ownership. The Hanafi proof is based on istihsan: the usurper's creation of a valuable work outweighs the original owner's right because the latter is lost in one aspect (name and benefits) while the usurper's right in the work is complete. The Hanafis respond to the Shafi'i objection by clarifying that they do not consider the prohibited act itself as the cause of ownership, but rather the creation of a new work. The distinction from the goat example is that after slaughter, the name 'goat' remains, whereas in the given cases the name changes (wheat becomes flour, timber becomes building). The passage emphasizes that this reasoning applies to all similar cases. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Hanafi view, with the caveat from Abu Yusuf about compensation.

Key Terms
غصب (ghaṣb): The wrongful taking of someone else's property without permission but not with intent to steal.
صنعة متقومة (ṣanʿah mutaqawwimah): A valuable work or manufacturing effort that has a monetary value in the market.
منقطع (munqaṭiʿ): Severed or cut off; here it means the owner's right of ownership is terminated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what happens to the original owner's right when a usurper grinds wheat into flour?
A) The owner's right is severed and he can only claim the value of wheat.
B) The owner's right remains and he can reclaim the flour.
C) The owner's right is severed but he can choose to take the flour without compensation.
D) The owner's right is transferred to the usurper's debt.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a usurper becomes owner of property when it is fundamentally changed (name and major benefits lost) due to the creation of a valuable work, but the original owner retains an option to take the item without compensation to avoid usury.
