Ruling on Removing Usurped Thread from a Non-Edible Animal's Wound
Ruling on whether to remove usurped thread from a non-edible animal's wound if removal risks harm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether to remove a usurped thread from a wound of a non-edible animal, and apply the maxim 'la darar wa la dirar' to justify the ruling.

Core Idea
If removing the thread harms the animal, it is not removed; the usurper compensates with the animal's value.

This passage addresses a specific scenario where a usurper uses stolen thread to stitch the wound of a non-edible animal (e.g., mule, donkey). The question is whether the thread must be removed and returned to its owner, especially if removal would kill the animal. The Hanafi school prioritizes the prohibition of causing harm, and the solution involves transferring ownership of the animal to the usurper with compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and parties
The usurper uses stolen thread (مغصوب) to sew a wound of a non-edible animal (غیر ماکول). The owner of the thread, the usurper, and the animal are the relevant parties.
Non-edible animals include humans, mules, and domestic donkeys (as per the text).
2
Determine the conflict of interests
The owner of the thread has the right to reclaim their property, but removing the thread would cause harm (possibly death) to the animal. The principle 'لا ضرر ولا ضرار' (no harm shall be inflicted nor reciprocated) prohibits causing harm.
The harm of losing the thread is lesser than the harm of losing the animal.
3
Apply the legal maxim
Since removing the thread would cause greater harm (talah of the animal), it is not allowed to remove it. The maxim dictates that one harm cannot be removed by inflicting another harm.
The hadith 'لا ضرر ولا ضرار' is the evidence.
4
State the Hanafi ruling
The thread is not removed; the animal becomes the property of the usurper, and the usurper must compensate the thread owner with the value of the animal.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Note the scholarly ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad have two views: one requiring removal, the other allowing compensation. Some Hanbali scholars (like al-Qadi) insist on removal, while others (like Abu al-Khattab) have two opinions.
The Hanafi view aligns with the second opinion of Shafi'i/Ahmad and the one opinion in Hanbali school that prioritizes avoiding harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدہ ... اگر مخصوب دھاگے سے غیر ماکول کا زخم سیا تو اس کی بابت امام شافعی واحمد کے دو قول ہیں ۔ ایک یہ کہ دھاگہ واپس کرنا ضروری ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ اس کا حق منتقل بقیمت ہو جائے گا مغنی حنابلہ میں ہے: فان خاط به جرح حيوان محترم لا يحل اكله كا لآدمى، والبغل، والحمار الاهلى و خيف التلف بنزعه لم يجب النزع لانه اضرار لصاحبه ولا يزال المضر بالضرر وكان الحيوان للغاصب وقال القاضى يجب نزعه وردّه و قال ابو الخطاب فيه وجهان احدهما هذا والثاني لا اگر دھاگے سے کسی ایسے محترم حیوان کا رشم سیا جس کا کھانا حلال نہیں ، جیسے آدمی، خچر، پالتو گدھا اور دھاگہ نکالنے سے تلف ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو تو نکالنا واجب نہیں ۔ کیونکہ اس میں مالک کو نقصان پہنچانا ہے حالانکہ ایک ضرر کا ازالہ دوسرے ضرر سے نہیں کیا جاتا۔ اب وہی جانور غاصب کا ہوگا ، قاضی نے کہا کہ دھاگا نکال کر واپس کرنا ضروری ہے اور ابو الخطاب نے کہا ہے کہ اس کی بابت دو جہیں ہیں ایک تو یہی ۔ دوسری یہ کہ نہیں۔
Benefit: If the wound of a non-edible animal was sewn with usurped thread, then regarding this, Imam al-Shafi'i and Ahmad have two statements. One: returning the thread is obligatory. Second: his right transfers to value. In Mughni al-Hanabila: If he sewed with it the wound of a respected animal whose meat is not permissible to eat, such as a human, mule, domestic donkey, and there is fear of destruction by removing it, removal is not obligatory, because it causes harm to its owner, and harm is not removed by harm, and the animal becomes the usurper's. Al-Qadi said: removal and return are obligatory. Abu al-Khattab said: there are two aspects; one is this, and the second is no (removal not obligatory).
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage (labeled 'فائدہ' or benefit) addresses a specific subsidiary ruling: if a usurper sews the wound of an animal with the usurped thread, and the animal is of a type not eaten (like a mule or donkey), what is the ruling? The Hanafi position (and the view adopted in the text) is that if removing the thread would endanger the animal's life, the thread is not removed; the animal becomes the property of the usurper, who must pay its value. The proof is the principle 'لا ضرر ولا ضرار' (no harm shall be inflicted nor reciprocated): removing the thread to return it to the owner would cause greater harm (the animal's death). The Hanbali school has an internal ikhtilaf: some (like al-Qadi) say removal is obligatory, while others (like Abu al-Khattab) have two views. The text brings this to show that even within other schools, there is support for the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
غیر ماکول (ghayr ma'kul): An animal whose meat is not permissible to eat (e.g., human, mule, donkey).
محترم (muhtaram): Respected, inviolable; an animal whose life is protected (i.e., not to be harmed without cause).
ضرر (darar): Harm; the principle that harm cannot be removed by inflicting equal or greater harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The thread must be removed and returned to its owner.
B) The thread is not removed, and the animal becomes the usurper's property with compensation.
C) The animal must be slaughtered to retrieve the thread.
D) The owner of the thread can take the animal as compensation.

Key Takeaway
When a usurped thread is used on a ghayr ma'kul animal and removal causes harm, the thread is not removed; the usurper compensates the owner with the animal's value.

Liability for Slaughtering Another's Animal: Owner's Options
Ruling on liability for slaughtering another's animal or cutting limbs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to the owner when someone slaughters their animal without permission, and apply the distinction between partial and total destruction (itlaf min wajh vs. istihlak min kulli wajh) to determine liability.

Core Idea
Partial destruction gives a choice; total destruction gives only full value.

When someone wrongfully slaughters another's sheep, the owner is not limited to just accepting the meat. The Hanafi school, based on sound analogy, grants the owner a powerful legal option: either claim the full value of the live animal or keep the carcass and claim the loss in value. This ruling, recorded as Zahir al-Riwayah, hinges on whether some benefit of the animal remains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
What exactly is the wrongful act? (Unauthorized slaughter). The ruling is wajib liability (daman) on the usurper. The owner has a choice.
The act is not total destruction because the meat remains beneficial.
2
Understand the owner's two options
Option 1: Claim full value and give the slaughtered animal to the usurper. Option 2: Keep the carcass and claim the deficiency (difference between live and dead value).
The deficiency accounts for lost purposes like milk, offspring, carrying.
3
Recognize the Qiyas (Analogy)
The act is likened to tearing a garment badly (kharq fahish). Both are partial destruction: some utility remains (meat / torn cloth). The same legal options apply.
The illa (cause) is that some benefits are lost while others remain.
4
Distinguish three scenarios
Edible animal (sheep/camel) → two options. Non-edible animal (e.g., donkey) → only full value because no benefit remains. Slave → owner takes the slave plus compensation for the limb (arsh) because a human remains useful.
The distinction hinges on whether any lawful benefit remains after the act.
5
Appreciate the authority
The text explicitly calls this the ruling of Zahir al-Riwayah, meaning it is the most authoritative and relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
Contrast with nawadir (rare narrations) that may differ.

قال ومن ذبح شاة غيره فمالكها بالخيار ان شاء ضمنه قيمتها وسلمها اليه وان شاء ضمنه نقصانها وكذا الجزور وكذا اذا قطع يدهما، هذا هو ظاهر الرواية ووجهه انه اتلاف من وجه باعتبار فوت بعض الاغراض من الحمل والدرّ والنسل وبقاء بعضها وهو اللحم، فصار كالخرق الفاحش فى الثوب ولو كانت الدابة غير ماكول اللحم فقطع الغاصب طرفها للمالك ان يضمنه جميع قيمتها لوجود الاستهلاك من كل وجه بخلاف قطع طرف المملوك حيث يأخذه مع ارش المقطوع لان الآدمى يبقى منتفعا به بعد قطع الطرف ترجمہ اور اگر غیر کی بکری ذبح کر ڈالی تو مالک کو اختیار ہے چاہے اس کی قیمت کا ضامن کر کے مذبوحہ اس کو دیدے اور چاہے اس کے نقصان کا ضامن کرے ۔ ایسے ہی اونٹ وغیرہ ہے یونہی اگر ان کے ہاتھ کاٹ ڈالے ظاہر الروایۃ یہی ہے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ ایک وجہ سے اتلاف ہے بایں لحاظ کہ بار برداری، دودھ، نسل وغیرہ بعض مقاصد جاتے رہے اور بعض باقی ہیں اور وہ گوشت ہے۔ تو کپڑے میں شدید شگاف کر دینے کی طرح ہو گیا اور اگر جانور غیر ماکول اللحم ہو اور غاصب اس کا کوئی ہاتھ پاؤں کاٹ دے تو مالک کو اختیار ہے کہ اس سے پوری قیمت تاوان لے سکتا ہے ہر طرح تلف کرنا پائے جانے کی وجہ سے بخلاف غلام کا ہاتھ پاؤں کاٹنے کے کہ وہ اس کو مقطوع کے جرمانہ کے ساتھ لے سکتا ہے کیونکہ آدمی ہاتھ پاؤں کٹ جانے کے بعد بھی قابل انتفاع رہتا ہے۔ تشریح قوله و من ذبح .... الخ - اگر کسی نے غیر کی بکری اس کی اجازت کے بغیر ذبح کر ڈالی تو مالک کو اختیا ر ہے چاہے اس سے بکری کی قیمت کا تاوان لے کر مذبوحہ بکری اس کو دیدے چاہے مذبوحہ خود رکھ کر اس سے نقصان لے لے ۔ یعنی مذبوحہ اور زندہ کی قیمت میں جو فرق ہوتا ہے وہ نقصان لے لے۔ یہی حکم جزور کا ہے۔ جزور اس اونٹ یا اونٹنی کو کہتے ہیں جو ذبح کے لیئے تیار کی جائے۔ سوال ... جب بکری کا یہ حکم ذکر کر چکے کہ مالک کو تضمین قیمت اور تضمین نقصان کا اختیار ہے تو پھر ذکر جزور کی کیا ضرورت؟ جواب اس کے ذکر سے ایک شبہ کا دفعیہ مقصود ہے جو تضمین نقصان اختیار کرنے پر وارد ہوتا ہے اور وہ یہ کہ ذبح شاہ میں جو نقصان ہے وہ اس سبب سے ہے کہ بکری میں جو درونسل کی صلاحیت تھی ذابح نے وہ فوت کر دی اور جزور تو ذبح کے لئے ہوتا ہی ہے تو اس میں در نسل مقصود نہیں۔ پر غاصب نقصان کا ضامن نہیں ہونا چاہیئے ۔ بلکہ اس کو تو ذبح کرنے کی اجرت ملنی چاہیئے کہ مالک کا جو مقصد تھا وہ اس نے
He said: And whoever slaughters another's sheep, its owner has the option: if he wishes, he can make him liable for its value and hand it over to him, or if he wishes, he can make him liable for its deficiency. Similarly for a camel, and similarly if he cuts off its limbs. This is the apparent narration. and its explanation is that it is destruction from one aspect, considering that some purposes (carrying, milk, offspring) are lost, and some remain (the meat). So it is like a large tear in a garment. And if the animal is not of edible meat, and the usurper cuts off a limb, the owner can make him liable for its entire value, because it is completely consumed, unlike cutting the limb of a slave, where he takes him with compensation for the cut, because a human remains of benefit after the cut. Translation: And if he slaughters another's sheep, the owner has the option: either he makes him liable for its value and gives him the slaughtered animal, or he makes him liable for the deficiency. Similarly for a camel, and similarly if he cuts off their limbs. This is the apparent narration. The reason is that it is destruction from one aspect: some purposes (carrying, milk, offspring) are lost, and some remain (the meat). So it is like a large tear in a garment. And if the animal is not of edible meat, and the usurper cuts off a limb, the owner can make him liable for its entire value, due to complete consumption, unlike cutting the limb of a slave, where he takes him with compensation for the cut, because a human remains of benefit after the cut. Commentary: (Regarding his statement 'And whoever slaughters...') If someone slaughters another's sheep without permission, the owner has the option: either he takes compensation for its value and gives the slaughtered sheep to him, or he keeps the slaughtered sheep and takes compensation for the deficiency, i.e., the difference between the value of the live and slaughtered sheep. This is the same ruling for a jazur (a camel prepared for slaughter). Question: Since the ruling for a sheep has been given, why mention a camel? Answer: It is to remove a doubt: the loss in slaughtering a sheep is due to the loss of offspring, etc., but a camel prepared for slaughter has no such loss; so one might think the usurper should not pay for deficiency, but rather be paid for the benefit of slaughtering it. The text clarifies that the owner still has the option to claim deficiency because the act is still a wrongful destruction.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on liability when someone slaughters or maims another's animal. The ruling, stated as 'zahir al-riwayah', gives the owner a choice: if the animal is edible (like sheep or camel), the owner can either take compensation for the full value and give the slaughtered animal to the usurper, or keep the slaughtered animal and claim the difference in value (the deficiency) caused by the loss of some purposes (e.g., milk, offspring, carrying). This is analogized to tearing a garment: the garment retains some value but is diminished. The reasoning is that the act is partial destruction (itlaf min wajh); the meat remains beneficial. For non-edible animals (e.g., a donkey), cutting a limb is total destruction (istihlak min kulli wajh) because the animal loses all utility, so the owner can claim full value. However, for a slave (a human), cutting a limb does not make him worthless; he still has utility (e.g., work), so the owner takes the slave plus compensation for the limb (arsh). The passage includes a question about why a camel prepared for slaughter is mentioned separately; the answer is to clarify that even though its purpose was slaughter, the unauthorized act still causes loss (the owner could have eaten it or sold it, etc.), so the same option applies. The commentary reinforces the analogy and distinctions.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or authoritative narration of the Hanafi school; rulings transmitted in the six major works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
جزور (jazur): A camel or camel prepared for slaughter; often used in the context of sacrifice or food.
اتلاف من وجه (itlaf min wajh): Partial destruction: the item is not entirely destroyed but loses some of its beneficial purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone slaughters another's camel that was prepared for slaughter (jazur), what are the owner's options under Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) The owner can only claim the value of the meat.
B) The owner can claim full value and give the carcass, or claim the deficiency (difference from live value).
C) The owner must accept the slaughtered animal and cannot claim any compensation.
D) The owner can claim full value but must return the meat to the usurper.

Key Takeaway
When someone wrongfully slaughters or maims your animal, you have the right to choose compensation for full value or the deficiency, depending on whether any benefit remains.

Owner's Options When Goat Is Slaughtered Without Permission
Ruling with proof: owner's options and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to the owner when his goat is slaughtered without permission and explain the Hanafi proof based on qiyas.

Core Idea
The owner may take full value (surrender meat) or keep meat and claim depreciation—partial destruction like a large tear in cloth.

In this passage, Al-Marghinani presents the ruling from Zahir al-Riwaya: the owner of a goat slaughtered without permission has two distinct options. He then provides the legal reasoning (talil) by analogizing to a large tear in cloth, establishing that the act is a partial destruction. The passage also mentions an intra-Hanafi difference with Hasan ibn Ziyad, which the commentary refutes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling options
Recognize that the act is slaughtering another's goat without permission. The owner has two options: demand full value and surrender the carcass, or keep the carcass and claim depreciation.
2
Note the scope: goat and camel
The same ruling applies to a camel (jazur) intended for slaughter, addressing a potential doubt that slaughtering a purpose-bred camel causes no loss.
3
Understand the reasoning: partial destruction
The ruling is based on partial destruction (itlaf min wajh): some benefits (milk, offspring, carrying) are lost, but the meat remains. Thus the owner may choose between full compensation (if he surrenders the meat) or partial compensation (if he keeps it).
4
Follow the qiyas: analogy to large tear in cloth
The author draws an analogy (qiyas) to a large tear in a garment: the owner may either take the full value (surrendering the torn cloth) or keep the cloth and claim the depreciation. The illa is partial destruction of benefits.
The qiyas is based on the common illa of partial destruction.
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and tarjih
Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated that if the owner keeps the meat, he cannot claim compensation because slaughtering is an improvement. The Zahir al-Riwaya rejects this, and the commentary (Ashraf al-Hidaya) affirms the two-option ruling as mufta bihi.

كتاب الغصب
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ پورا کر دیا۔ صاحب کتاب نے و كذا الجزور بڑھا کر اس شبہ کو دفع کر دیا اور بتلا دیا کہ ذیج جزور میں بھی یہی حکم ہے اس لئے کہ ایک جاندار کی زندگی ختم کر دینا کیا کم نقصان ہے؟
کیونکہ در و نسل کے علاوہ مالک کے اور بہت سے مقاصد ہو سکتے ہیں۔ لہذا ما لک کو اختیار ہو گا۔

قوله هو ظاهر الرواية ... الخ - اس تصریح کے ذریعہ حسن ابن زیاد کی روایت سے احتراز ہے کہ مذبوحہ بکری رکھ لینے کی صورت میں ضمان نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ ذبح کرتا اور کھال اتارنا بکری میں ایک قسم کا اضافہ ہے بایں معنی کہ اس نے گوشت سے فائدہ اٹھا نا قریب تر کر دیا۔ ظاہر الروایۃ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ بکری سے مختلف منافع حاصل ہوتے ہیں مثلاً دودھ پینا نسل بڑھانا، گوشت کھانا وغیرہ اور ذبح کے بعد کچھ منافع باقی ہیں کچھ فوت ہو گئے۔ اس لئے مالک کے دونوں اختیار ہوں گے جیسے کپڑے میں کثیر شگاف کر دینے سے مالک کو ضمان یا نقصان کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔

قول قطع طرف المملوك..... الخ - يه قول سابق للمالك ان يضمنه حمبيع القیمہ سے متعلق ہے یعنی اگر مملوک یہ " کا کوئی ہاتھ پاؤں کاٹا تو عضو مقطوع کے جرمانہ کے ساتھ وہ مملوک کو لے سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ آدمی ہاتھ پاؤں کٹ جانے کے بعد بھی اس قابل رہتا ہے کہ اس سے نفع اٹھایا جائے۔ بخلاف دابہ کے کہ اس سے جو حمل اور کوب و غیرہ کا فائدہ مقصود ہوتا ہے وہ ہاتھ پاؤں کٹ جانے کے بعد اس فائدہ کے قابل نہیں رہتا۔
And if someone slaughters another's goat, then its owner has the option: if he wishes, he may make him liable for its full value and surrender the slaughtered animal to him; and if he wishes, he may make him liable for the depreciation. Similarly for a camel (jazur). Similarly if he cuts its limb. This is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). Its reasoning: it is destruction from one aspect, considering the loss of some purposes like carrying, milk, offspring, while some remain, namely the meat. So it is like a large tear in a garment. And if the animal is not edible and the usurper cuts its limb, the owner may make him liable for its full value because total consumption exists from every aspect. Unlike cutting the limb of a slave, where he takes the slave along with the compensation for the cut limb because a human remains beneficial after the cut.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when someone slaughters another's goat without permission. The owner has two options: (1) demand the full market value of the goat and surrender the slaughtered goat to the usurper, or (2) keep the slaughtered goat and claim compensation for the difference between its value before and after slaughter (depreciation). The same ruling applies to a camel intended for slaughter (jazur). The text mentions 'zahir al-riwaya' to indicate this is the established position from the core books of Imam Muhammad, distinguishing it from a narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad who held a different view. The reasoning is that slaughtering causes partial destruction: some benefits (milk, offspring, carrying) are lost, but the meat remains. This is analogized to making a large tear in someone's cloth, where the owner likewise has options. For an inedible animal (like a donkey) whose limb is cut, the owner may claim full value because no benefit remains. However, for a slave whose limb is cut, the owner takes the slave along with compensation for the limb because a human can still be used for services after the loss of a limb. The commentary also refutes a potential doubt: why mention the camel separately? Because one might think the camel was already intended for slaughter so no depreciation, but the author clarifies that ending an animal's life is itself a harm, and there may be other purposes beyond offspring.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The established, widely transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six core books (the zahir al-riwaya), which are the relied-upon positions in the Hanafi school.
جزور (jazur): A camel (male or female) prepared for slaughter, typically for food.
غراض (aghrad): Purposes or benefits: the various uses an owner expects from his animal, such as milk, offspring, carrying loads, and meat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if someone slaughters another's goat without permission and the owner chooses to keep the meat, what can the owner claim?
A) Full value of the goat.
B) Nothing.
C) The depreciation (difference between live and slaughtered value).
D) Only the value of the skin.

Key Takeaway
The owner of a goat slaughtered without permission may claim either full value (surrendering the meat) or depreciation (keeping the meat), based on the principle of partial destruction analogized to a large tear in cloth.

Cutting Limb of Inedible Animal vs Slave: Full vs Partial Compensation
Ruling with proof: comparison between inedible animal and slave for limb cutting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the ruling for cutting a limb of an inedible animal (full compensation) from cutting a limb of a slave (partial compensation) and explain the underlying illa.

Core Idea
Cutting a limb of an inedible animal destroys all value (full compensation); cutting a slave's limb leaves him usable (only compensation for the limb).

This passage extends the previous discussion to cases where a limb is cut from an animal that is not eaten, and contrasts this with a slave. The key distinction lies in the remaining benefits: an inedible animal becomes completely useless after the limb cut, while a human can still be employed for services. Hence, the owner's remedy differs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario: usurper cuts limb of inedible animal
The text presents a case where a usurper cuts a limb (hand or foot) of an animal that is not edible, like a donkey or mule. This is a distinct form of usurpation (ghasb) with its own ruling.
2
Note the ruling: full value may be claimed
For an inedible animal, the owner may demand the full value of the animal because the cut renders it completely useless (no meat, no work capacity).
3
Understand the cause: total destruction of all benefits
The reasoning (illa) is 'complete consumption from every aspect' (istihlak min kull wajh). The animal loses all its purposes: no riding, no carrying, no milk, no offspring, and it is not even edible. Nothing remains.
4
Contrast with slave: limb cut but human remains useful
A slave, even after losing a limb, can still perform many services (e.g., light work, supervision). Therefore, the owner cannot claim full value; he may keep the slave and claim only the compensation (arsh) for the limb.
5
Extract the principle: compensation matches extent of destruction
The key principle is that compensation is determined by how much benefit remains. If nothing remains, full compensation; if some benefit remains, only the depreciation is compensated.

غیر کی بکری ذبح کر ڈالی مالک کو اختیار ہے چاہے اس کی قیمت کا ضامن کر لئے مذبوحہ بکری اس کو دے دے چاہے نقصان کا ضامن ٹھہرائے

قال ومن ذبح شاة غيره فمالكها بالخيار ان شاء ضمنه قيمتها وسلمها اليه وان شاء ضمنه نقصانها وكذا الجزور وكذا اذا قطع يدهما، هذا هو ظاهر الرواية ووجهه انه اتلاف من وجه باعتبار فوت بعض الاغراض من الحمل والدرّ والنسل وبقاء بعضها وهو اللحم، فصار كالخرق الفاحش فى الثوب ولو كانت الدابة غير ماكول اللحم فقطع الغاصب طرفها للمالك ان يضمنه جميع قيمتها لوجود الاستهلاك من كل وجه بخلاف قطع طرف المملوك حيث يأخذه مع ارش المقطوع لان الآدمى يبقى منتفعا به بعد قطع الطرف

ترجمہ اور اگر غیر کی بکری ذبح کر ڈالی تو مالک کو اختیار ہے چاہے اس کی قیمت کا ضامن کر کے مذبوحہ اس کو دیدے اور چاہے اس کے نقصان کا ضامن کرے ۔ ایسے ہی اونٹ وغیرہ ہے یونہی اگر ان کے ہاتھ کاٹ ڈالے ظاہر الروایۃ یہی ہے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ ایک وجہ سے اتلاف ہے بایں لحاظ کہ بار برداری، دودھ، نسل وغیرہ بعض مقاصد جاتے رہے اور بعض باقی ہیں اور وہ گوشت ہے۔ تو کپڑے میں شدید شگاف کر دینے کی طرح ہو گیا اور اگر جانور غیر ماکول اللحم ہو اور غاصب اس کا کوئی ہاتھ پاؤں کاٹ دے تو مالک کو اختیار ہے کہ اس سے پوری قیمت تاوان نے ہر طرح تلف کرنا پائے جانے کی وجہ سے بخلاف غلام کا ہاتھ پاؤں کاٹنے کے کہ وہ اس کو مقطوع کے جرمانہ کے ساتھ لے سکتا ہے کیونکہ آدمی ہاتھ پاؤں کٹ جانے کے بعد بھی قابل انتفاع رہتا ہے۔

كتاب الغصب
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ پورا کر دیا۔ صاحب کتاب نے و كذا الجزور بڑھا کر اس شبہ کو دفع کر دیا اور بتلا دیا کہ ذیج جزور میں بھی یہی حکم ہے اس لئے کہ ایک جاندار کی زندگی ختم کر دینا کیا کم نقصان ہے؟
کیونکہ در و نسل کے علاوہ مالک کے اور بہت سے مقاصد ہو سکتے ہیں۔ لہذا ما لک کو اختیار ہو گا۔

قوله هو ظاهر الرواية ... الخ - اس تصریح کے ذریعہ حسن ابن زیاد کی روایت سے احتراز ہے کہ مذبوحہ بکری رکھ لینے کی صورت میں ضمان نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ ذبح کرتا اور کھال اتارنا بکری میں ایک قسم کا اضافہ ہے بایں معنی کہ اس نے گوشت سے فائدہ اٹھا نا قریب تر کر دیا۔ ظاہر الروایۃ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ بکری سے مختلف منافع حاصل ہوتے ہیں مثلاً دودھ پینا نسل بڑھانا، گوشت کھانا وغیرہ اور ذبح کے بعد کچھ منافع باقی ہیں کچھ فوت ہو گئے۔ اس لئے مالک کے دونوں اختیار ہوں گے جیسے کپڑے میں کثیر شگاف کر دینے سے مالک کو ضمان یا نقصان کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔

قول قطع طرف المملوك..... الخ - يه قول سابق للمالك ان يضمنه حمبيع القیمہ سے متعلق ہے یعنی اگر مملوک یہ " کا کوئی ہاتھ پاؤں کاٹا تو عضو مقطوع کے جرمانہ کے ساتھ وہ مملوک کو لے سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ آدمی ہاتھ پاؤں کٹ جانے کے بعد بھی اس قابل رہتا ہے کہ اس سے نفع اٹھایا جائے۔ بخلاف دابہ کے کہ اس سے جو حمل اور کوب و غیرہ کا فائدہ مقصود ہوتا ہے وہ ہاتھ پاؤں کٹ جانے کے بعد اس فائدہ کے قابل نہیں رہتا۔
And if someone slaughters another's goat, then its owner has the option: if he wishes, he may make him liable for its full value and surrender the slaughtered animal to him; and if he wishes, he may make him liable for the depreciation. Similarly for a camel (jazur). Similarly if he cuts its limb. This is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). Its reasoning: it is destruction from one aspect, considering the loss of some purposes like carrying, milk, offspring, while some remain, namely the meat. So it is like a large tear in a garment. And if the animal is not edible and the usurper cuts its limb, the owner may make him liable for its full value because total consumption exists from every aspect. Unlike cutting the limb of a slave, where he takes the slave along with the compensation for the cut limb because a human remains beneficial after the cut.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when someone slaughters another's goat without permission. The owner has two options: (1) demand the full market value of the goat and surrender the slaughtered goat to the usurper, or (2) keep the slaughtered goat and claim compensation for the difference between its value before and after slaughter (depreciation). The same ruling applies to a camel intended for slaughter (jazur). The text mentions 'zahir al-riwaya' to indicate this is the established position from the core books of Imam Muhammad, distinguishing it from a narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad who held a different view. The reasoning is that slaughtering causes partial destruction: some benefits (milk, offspring, carrying) are lost, but the meat remains. This is analogized to making a large tear in someone's cloth, where the owner likewise has options. For an inedible animal (like a donkey) whose limb is cut, the owner may claim full value because no benefit remains. However, for a slave whose limb is cut, the owner takes the slave along with compensation for the limb because a human can still be used for services after the loss of a limb. The commentary also refutes a potential doubt: why mention the camel separately? Because one might think the camel was already intended for slaughter so no depreciation, but the author clarifies that ending an animal's life is itself a harm, and there may be other purposes beyond offspring.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The established, widely transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six core books (the zahir al-riwaya), which are the relied-upon positions in the Hanafi school.
ارش (arsh): Compensation paid for injury to a slave or free person where the injury is not pre-defined by diyah; it is the difference in value before and after the injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone cuts the hand of a slave without permission, what compensation is due?
A) Full value of the slave.
B) Only the compensation (arsh) for the hand, and the owner keeps the slave.
C) The owner must return the slave and claim nothing.
D) The owner may choose full value or depreciation.

Key Takeaway
For an inedible animal, cutting a limb destroys all value so full compensation applies; for a human slave, remaining benefits trigger only partial compensation for the limb.

Ruling on Tearing Another's Cloth: Slight vs. Large Tear
Distinguishes between slight and large tear in another's cloth and owner's options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a slight and a large tear in another's cloth and state the owner's options for claiming damages.

Core Idea
A slight tear only entitles to depreciation; a large tear gives the owner the option to claim full value or keep cloth and claim depreciation.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies the Hanafi ruling on liability for tearing another's cloth. The key distinction is whether the tear is slight (yasir) or large (fahish), which determines whether the owner can only claim the loss in value or also have the option to demand full compensation. We will explore the definitions, the analogy to burning, and the precise criteria set by the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of tear
Read the text and classify the tear as yasir (slight) or fahish (large) based on whether the tear causes loss of benefit (manfa'a) or just a defect. A yasir tear does not destroy any benefit; a fahish tear destroys the type of benefit and part of the substance.
The definition of fahish is refined: it is not merely destruction of most benefits but loss of the essence of the utility and some substance.
2
Determine liability
For a slight tear: the owner keeps the cloth and the tearer is liable only for the depreciation (nagsan). For a large tear: the owner has two options – claim full value (as if burned) and leave the cloth with the tearer, or keep the cloth and claim depreciation.
The text compares a large tear to burning because both eliminate the primary benefit.
3
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The text uses qiyas: just as burning another's cloth makes the burner liable for the full value, a large tear that destroys the benefit is analogous to burning. This reasoning (ta'lil) is explicit: 'faka annahu ahraqahu' (as if he burned it).
Even though the cloth may not be completely destroyed, the loss of the type of benefit justifies full value, because the purpose of the garment is lost.
4
Refine the definition of fahish
The text corrects a common view that fahish means destruction of most benefits. The correct Hanafi position (sahih) is that fahish means loss of part of the substance (al-ayn) and the type of benefit (jins al-manfa'a), while some substance and some benefit remain. This is broader than total destruction.
Imam Muhammad's position in al-Asl treated even cutting cloth as a large defect (nagsan fahish), showing that the criterion is qualitative, not purely quantitative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی نے دوسرے کے کپڑے میں خفیف شگاف کر دیا تو وہ نقصان کا ضامن ہوگا اور کپڑا مالک کا ہوگا

ومن خرق ثوب غيره خرقا يسيرا ضمن نقصانه والثوب لمالكه لان العين قائم من كل وجه وانما دخله عيب فيضمنه، وان خرق خرقا كثيرا تبطل عامة منافعه فلمالكه ان يضمنه جميع قيمته لانه استهلاک من هذا الوجه، فكانه احرقه قال معناه يترك الثوب عليه وان شاء اخذ الثوب وضمنه النقصان لانه تعيب من وجه ومن حيث ان العين باق وكذا بعض المنافع قائم ثم اشارة الكتاب الى ان الفاحش ما يبطل به عامة المنافع والصحيح ان الفاحش ما يفوت به بعض العين وجنس المنفعة ويبقى بعض العين وبعض المنفعة واليسير ما لا يفوت به شيء من المنفعة، وانما يدخل فيه النقصان لان محمدا جعل في الاصل قطع الثوب نقصانا فاحشا والفائت به بعض المنافع

ترجمہ اگر کسی نے دوسرے کے کپڑے میں خفیف شگاف کر دیا تو وہ نقصان کا ضامن ہوگا اور کپڑا مالک کا ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مال عین ہر
And if someone tears another's cloth with a slight tear, he is liable for the depreciation, and the cloth remains the owner's because the substance (ayn) remains intact from every aspect, only a defect entered it, so he is liable for that. And if he tears a large tear that destroys most of its benefits, then the owner may make him liable for its full value because it is consumption from that aspect, as if he burned it. He said: meaning the owner may leave the cloth with him, or if he wishes, he may take the cloth and make him liable for the depreciation because it is defective from one aspect and the substance remains, and some benefits remain. Then the book indicates that 'fahish' (large) is what destroys most benefits, but the correct view is that 'fahish' is what causes loss of part of the substance and the type of benefit, while some substance and some benefit remain. 'Yasir' (slight) is what does not cause loss of any benefit, and only depreciation enters into it. Because Muhammad made in the original (al-Asl) the cutting of cloth a large defect (nagsan fahish) and what is lost thereby is some benefits.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage differentiates between two types of damage to another's cloth: a slight tear (kharaq yasir) and a large tear (kharaq kathir/fahish). For a slight tear that does not destroy any functionality, the cloth remains with the owner, and the usurper is liable only for the depreciation (nagsan) — the reduction in value. For a large tear that destroys most benefits, the owner has two options similar to total destruction: (1) claim full value and leave the cloth with the usurper, or (2) keep the cloth and claim depreciation. The reasoning is that a large tear is like burning in that it renders the item useless for its primary purposes. The text then clarifies the definition of 'fahish' (large/excessive): it is not necessarily that all benefits are destroyed, but rather that some part of the substance and the type of benefit is lost, while some substance remains. A slight tear does not cause any loss of benefit, only a defect. The author notes that Imam Muhammad, in al-Asl (a core book of zahir al-riwaya), considered cutting cloth as a large defect causing loss of some benefits, implying that even a cut can be considered fahish depending on the context.

Key Terms
خرق يسير (kharaq yasir): A slight tear that does not cause any loss of benefit; only a defect in the cloth.
خرق فاحش (kharaq fahish): A large tear that causes loss of part of the cloth's substance and the type of benefit, though some substance and benefit remain.
عين (ayn): The physical substance of the cloth that remains after the tear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what distinguishes a 'large tear' (kharaq fahish) from a 'slight tear' (kharaq yasir) in another's cloth?
A) Size of the tear in length
B) Whether the cloth becomes unstitchable
C) Whether the tear causes loss of some of the cloth's substance and the type of benefit
D) Whether the tear is made intentionally or accidentally

Key Takeaway
The distinction between a slight tear (only depreciation owed) and a large tear (owner can claim full value or keep cloth with depreciation) hinges on loss of substance and type of benefit.

Owner's Option When Usurper Cuts Limb of Non-Edible Animal
States ruling on cutting limb of non-edible animal with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the owner's options when a usurper cuts a limb of a non-edible animal, and cite the narration from Imam Muhammad as proof.

Core Idea
When a usurper cuts a limb of a non-edible animal, the owner may choose full compensation or keep the animal and claim the deficiency.

In this lesson, we examine a specific application of ghasb law: cutting a limb of a non-edible animal like a donkey. The Hanafi school, drawing on a narration from Imam Muhammad, grants the owner an option that balances compensation for total loss and partial damage. Understanding this ruling illuminates the principle that liability in ghasb depends on remaining benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is cutting a limb of a non-edible animal by a usurper. The ruling is that the owner has an option: either take full value (if no benefit remains) or keep the animal and claim the deficiency in value.
The animal must be non-edible (e.g., donkey, mule).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a narration from Imam Muhammad via Hisham: 'A man cut the hand or foot of a donkey, and there remained some value; he has the option to retain and take the deficiency.'
This is a Sunnah ahad with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'فله أن يمسك ويأخذ النقصان' explicitly grants the owner the choice to keep and take the deficiency, implying the option is permissible.
The wording 'falahu' indicates permission (ibaha).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
No disagreement is mentioned within the Hanafi school or between madhabs in this text; the ruling appears to be agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) as per the source.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The narration is from the nawadir (rare transmissions), yet it is relied upon for fatwa (mufta bihi) as it aligns with the principle of compensating actual loss.
Authority weight: nawadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولو كانت الدابة .... الخ - اور اگر وہ جانور غیر ماکول اللحم ہو اور غاصب اس کا ہاتھ پاؤں کاٹ ڈالے تو مالک کو اختیار ہوگا کہ اس سے پوری قیمت کا تاوان لے لے۔ جبکہ قطع اطراف کے بعد اس کی کوئی منفعت اور قیمت باقی نہ رہے کہ اس صورت میں ہر طرح سے اتلاف پایا گیا اور اگر قطع اطراف کے بعد اس کی کچھ قیمت ہو تو مالک کو اختیار ہو گا کہ اس کو رکھ کر نقصان لے لے چنانچہ [؟متقی؟] میں امام محمد سے ہشام کی روایت منقول ہے۔ "رجل قطع يد حمار او رجله وكان لما بقى قيمة فله ان يمسك و يأخذ النقصان ."
His saying: 'And if the animal...' - And if that animal is non-edible and the usurper cuts off its hand or foot, the owner has the option to take full compensation from him. When after cutting the limbs no benefit and value remains, then in that case total destruction occurred. And if after cutting the limbs there is some value, then the owner has the option to keep it and take the deficiency. Thus, in [؟Muttaqi؟], a narration from Imam Muhammad via Hisham is transmitted: 'A man cut the hand or foot of a donkey, and there remained some value; he has the option to retain and take the deficiency.'
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This is a ruling on ghasb (usurpation) regarding cutting a limb of a non-edible animal (like a donkey). The owner has two options: if the animal is now completely useless, he can demand full value from the usurper; if some value remains, he can keep the animal and claim only the loss in value. The text cites a narration from Imam Muhammad through Hisham to support this ruling. The underlying principle is that the usurper has effectively destroyed part of the property.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation: taking another's property without right.
غاصب (ghasib): The usurper who wrongfully takes property.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The owner must keep the donkey and cannot claim any compensation.
B) The owner can either take full value and surrender the donkey, or keep the donkey and claim the 30% deficiency.
C) The owner can only claim the full value, not keep the donkey.
D) The owner must return the donkey to the usurper.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a usurper cuts a limb of a non-edible animal, the owner may either claim full value (surrendering the animal) or keep the animal and claim the deficiency—a choice that hinges on remaining benefit.

Ruling for Cutting a Slave's Limb: Owner's Option
States ruling on cutting limb of a slave with comparative reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on cutting a slave's limb and distinguish it from the case of a non-edible animal based on remaining utility.

Core Idea
A slave remains beneficial after limb loss; an animal does not — so the owner can keep the slave and claim compensation.

This passage expands the ruling on ghasb (usurpation) when a limb of a slave is cut. Unlike a non-edible animal (dabbah), a human retains utility even after losing a limb. Therefore, the owner has a choice to keep the slave and take compensation for the severed limb, whereas for an animal the owner must take full value because its intended benefit is lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is cutting a limb of a slave. The ruling: the owner may take compensation for the limb (the 'diya' or value) and keep the slave.
This is an expansion from the previous case of an animal.
2
Understand the analogy with the animal case
The previous ruling (presumably for a non-edible animal) states that the owner must take full value of the animal because the animal loses its intended benefit (e.g., carrying loads) after limb loss.
The animal becomes completely useless; hence the owner cannot keep it and also claim compensation for the limb.
3
Trace the reasoning (talīl)
The differentiating factor is the remaining utility after injury. A person, even with a missing limb, can still perform many tasks (work, service, etc.), so the slave is still valuable. An animal's primary function is destroyed.
This is a reason-based distinction (ta‘līl) rather than a textual proof.
4
Apply the distinction
If a slave loses a limb, the owner can claim partial compensation (the value of the limb) and retain the slave. If an animal loses a limb, the owner must claim full compensation (the entire value) and cannot retain the animal.
The key is whether the property retains its intended benefit after the injury.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول قطع طرف المملوك..... الخ - يه قول سابق للمالك ان يضمنه جميع القیمة سے متعلق ہے یعنی اگر مملوک کا کوئی ہاتھ پاؤں کاٹا تو عضو مقطوع کے جرمانہ کے ساتھ وہ مملوک کو لے سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ آدمی ہاتھ پاؤں کٹ جانے کے بعد بھی اس قابل رہتا ہے کہ اس سے نفع اٹھایا جائے۔ بخلاف دابہ کے کہ اس سے جو حمل اور کوب و غیرہ کا فائدہ مقصود ہوتا ہے وہ ہاتھ پاؤں کٹ جانے کے بعد اس فائدہ کے قابل نہیں رہتا۔
His saying: 'Cutting the limb of a slave...' - This relates to the previous statement that the owner may claim full value. That is, if a limb of a slave is cut, along with the penalty for the severed limb, he may take the slave. Because a person, even after losing a limb, remains capable of being benefited from. Unlike an animal, from which the intended benefit of carrying loads etc. is not possible after losing a limb.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage expands the ruling on cutting a slave's limb. Unlike the non-edible animal, a slave retains utility even after limb loss (e.g., can still perform work). Therefore, the owner can take compensation for the limb (the 'diya' or value of the limb) and keep the slave. The animal is different because its primary benefits (load carrying, etc.) are lost. The reasoning (ta'lil) distinguishes based on the nature of the property.

Key Terms
مملوك (mamluk): A slave, a human property.
دابة (dabbah): A riding or pack animal (non-edible).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, why does a slave differ from a non-edible animal when a limb is cut?
A) Because a slave has a soul, while an animal does not.
B) Because a slave can still be benefited from after losing a limb, while an animal loses its primary benefit.
C) Because the value of a slave is higher than that of an animal.
D) Because cutting a slave's limb is a crime (jinayat) while cutting an animal's limb is not.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between slaves and animals in ghasb based on whether the property retains beneficial utility after injury.
